   ```bash
   # Search for hardcoded English text in templates
   grep -rn '"[A-Z][a-zA-Z ]*"' templates/ | grep -v '<?php'
   
   # Search for hardcoded text in JavaScript files
   grep -rn '"[A-Z][a-zA-Z ]*"' js/ | grep -v 't(' | grep -v '//'
   
   # List all translation keys needed
   ```
   
   **Create checklist of all text:**
   - Navigation items
   - Button labels
   - Form labels and help text
   - Error messages
   - Success messages
   - Empty state messages
   - Tooltip text
   - Modal titles and content
   - Table headers
   - Status labels
   - Validation messages

2. [ ] **Ensure proper translation function usage**
   
   **Server-side (PHP templates):**
   ```php
   <!-- CORRECT -->
   <?php p($l->t('Dashboard')); ?>
   <?php p($l->t('You have %n pending approval', 'You have %n pending approvals', $count)); ?>
   <?php p($l->t('Hello %s', [$userName])); ?>
   
   <!-- WRONG -->
   Dashboard  <!-- No translation -->
   <?php echo 'Dashboard'; ?>  <!-- No translation -->
   ```
   
   **Client-side (vanilla JavaScript):**
   ```javascript
   // CORRECT - Use Nextcloud's t() function (available globally)
   const message = t('arbeitszeitcheck', 'Dashboard');
   const pluralMessage = n('arbeitszeitcheck', 'You have %n pending approval', 'You have %n pending approvals', count);
   
   // For updating DOM elements:
   element.textContent = t('arbeitszeitcheck', 'Loading...');
   element.innerHTML = t('arbeitszeitcheck', 'Welcome, %s!', [userName]);
   
   // WRONG
   const message = 'Dashboard';  // No translation
   element.textContent = 'Loading...';  // No translation
   ```

   **Complete `l10n/de.json`** - add all German translations

### Phase 8: Responsive Design & Mobile
**Status:** [ ] Not Started | [ ] In Progress | [ ] Complete
**Estimated Time:** 4-5 hours
**Prerequisites:** Phase 7 Complete

**Objective:** Ensure perfect responsive design and mobile experience with hamburger menu, touch-friendly controls, and optimized layouts.

**Tasks:**

1. [ ] **Implement mobile navigation**
   
   **Add hamburger button to `templates/index.php`:**
   ```php
   <button id="arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button"
           class="arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button"
           aria-label="<?php p($l->t('Open navigation menu')); ?>"
           aria-expanded="false"
           aria-controls="arbeitszeitcheck-navigation">
     <span class="arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button__icon">
       <span class="arbeitszeitcheck-hamburger-line"></span>
       <span class="arbeitszeitcheck-hamburger-line"></span>
       <span class="arbeitszeitcheck-hamburger-line"></span>
     </span>
   </button>
   ```
   
   **Add mobile menu JavaScript:**
   ```javascript
   // Add to js/mobile-menu.js
   (function() {
     'use strict';
     
     const mobileMenu = {
       button: null,
       nav: null,
       isOpen: false,
       
       init: function() {
         this.button = document.getElementById('arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button');
         this.nav = document.getElementById('arbeitszeitcheck-navigation');
         
         if (!this.button || !this.nav) return;
         
         this.button.addEventListener('click', this.toggle.bind(this));
         
         // Close on outside click
         document.addEventListener('click', (e) => {
           if (this.isOpen && !this.nav.contains(e.target) && e.target !== this.button) {
             this.close();
           }
         });
         
         // Close on escape key
         document.addEventListener('keydown', (e) => {
           if (e.key === 'Escape' && this.isOpen) {
             this.close();
             this.button.focus();
           }
         });
       },
       
       toggle: function() {
         if (this.isOpen) {
           this.close();
         } else {
           this.open();
         }
       },
       
       open: function() {
         this.nav.classList.add('arbeitszeitcheck-navigation--mobile-open');
         this.button.setAttribute('aria-expanded', 'true');
         this.button.classList.add('arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button--open');
         this.isOpen = true;
         
         // Focus first link in navigation
         const firstLink = this.nav.querySelector('.arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__link');
         if (firstLink) {
           firstLink.focus();
         }
       },
       
       close: function() {
         this.nav.classList.remove('arbeitszeitcheck-navigation--mobile-open');
         this.button.setAttribute('aria-expanded', 'false');
         this.button.classList.remove('arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button--open');
         this.isOpen = false;
       }
     };
     
     if (document.readyState === 'loading') {
       document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', () => mobileMenu.init());
     } else {
       mobileMenu.init();
     }
   })();
   ```

2. [ ] **Add responsive CSS**
   
   **Update `css/navigation.css` with mobile styles:**
   ```css
   /* Mobile menu button (hidden on desktop) */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button {
     display: none;
     position: fixed;
     top: 60px;
     left: 16px;
     z-index: 2000;
     width: 44px;
     height: 44px;
     padding: 0;
     background: var(--color-primary);
     border: none;
     border-radius: 50%;
     cursor: pointer;
     box-shadow: 0 2px 8px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.2);
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button:hover {
     background: var(--color-primary-element-hover);
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button:focus-visible {
     outline: 2px solid var(--color-primary);
     outline-offset: 2px;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-hamburger-line {
     display: block;
     width: 20px;
     height: 2px;
     background: white;
     margin: 4px auto;
     transition: transform 0.3s ease, opacity 0.3s ease;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button--open .arbeitszeitcheck-hamburger-line:nth-child(1) {
     transform: translateY(6px) rotate(45deg);
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button--open .arbeitszeitcheck-hamburger-line:nth-child(2) {
     opacity: 0;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button--open .arbeitszeitcheck-hamburger-line:nth-child(3) {
     transform: translateY(-6px) rotate(-45deg);
   }
   
   /* Mobile styles */

     .arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button {
       display: flex;
       align-items: center;
       justify-content: center;
     }
     
     .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation {
       transform: translateX(-100%);
       transition: transform 0.3s ease;
       box-shadow: 2px 0 8px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.1);
     }

       transform: translateX(0);
     }

       margin-left: 0;
     }

       content: '';
       position: fixed;
       top: 0;
       left: 240px;
       right: 0;
       bottom: 0;
       background: rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.5);
       z-index: -1;
     }
   }
   
   /* Tablet styles */
   @media (min-width: 769px) and (max-width: 1024px) {
     .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation {
       width: 200px;
     }
     
     .arbeitszeitcheck-content {
       margin-left: 200px;
     }
   }
   ```

# 🎯 EXECUTIVE SUMMARY & ROADMAP

## What This Document Is

This is a **comprehensive, holistic, bulletproof refactoring plan** for the `apps/arbeitszeitcheck` application. It provides:

1. **What needs to be done** - Complete list of all tasks, features, and requirements
2. **In what order** - Clear phase-by-phase roadmap with dependencies
3. **How it should work** - Detailed workflows, use cases, and role interactions
4. **How to verify it's done** - Clear Definition of Done for every task

## High-Level Overview

**Goal:** Refactor arbeitszeitcheck from Vue.js to plain PHP with vanilla JavaScript, following `apps/projectcheck` patterns, ensuring Nextcloud Store compliance, German labor law compliance (ArbZG), GDPR compliance, and extreme usability ("granny-proof").

**Key Requirements:**
- ✅ Zero Vue.js (plain PHP + vanilla JS only)
- ✅ Zero CSP violations (all inline scripts use nonces)
- ✅ Zero CORS errors (same-origin API calls)
- ✅ Working translations (German + English)
- ✅ Theme compatibility (all Nextcloud themes)
- ✅ German labor law compliance (ArbZG)
- ✅ GDPR compliance
- ✅ Extreme usability (simple, intuitive, self-explanatory)
- ✅ Production-ready (no TODOs, mocks, placeholders)
- ✅ Fully tested and documented

## How It Should Work: Key Concepts

### 1. Roles & Permissions

**Three Roles:**
- **Employee**: Tracks own time, requests absences, views own data
- **Manager**: All employee capabilities + approves/rejects team requests, views team data
- **Admin**: All manager capabilities + manages users, configures system, views all data

**Permission Model:**
- Data filtering by role (employees see only own data, managers see only team data, admins see all data)
- UI visibility by role (features shown/hidden based on permissions)
- Server-side permission checks (controllers and services verify permissions)
- Defense in depth (multiple layers of permission checks)

**See:** Phase 4.6 for complete role definitions, permission matrix, use cases, and scenarios

### 2. Workflows

**Employee Workflows:**
- Clock in/out workflow (with break tracking, ArbZG compliance)
- Manual time entry workflow
- Time entry correction workflow (requires manager approval)
- Vacation request workflow (requires manager approval)
- Sick leave reporting workflow
- View compliance status workflow

**Manager Workflows:**
- Approve/reject absence requests workflow
- Approve/reject time corrections workflow
- View team overview workflow
- Generate team reports workflow

**Admin Workflows:**
- Add/configure employee workflow
- Create/manage working time models workflow
- View system-wide compliance workflow
- Configure global settings workflow

**See:** Phase 4.5 for detailed workflow documentation with real-world examples

### 3. German Law Compliance (ArbZG)

**Core Requirements:**
- Maximum 8 hours/day (can extend to 10 if 6-month average ≤ 8)
- Maximum 48 hours/week average over 6 months
- 30 minutes break required after 6 hours
- 45 minutes break required after 9 hours
- 11 hours rest period between shifts
- Sunday/holiday work restrictions
- Night work regulations
- Record keeping (2 years minimum)

**See:** Phase 4.5 for complete ArbZG compliance documentation

### 4. Work Time Models

**20 Different Models Supported:**
- Standard: Full-time, Part-time, Flexible, Trust-based, Shift work
- Special: Compressed work week, Annualized hours, Job sharing, Zero-hours
- Leave/Status: Sabbatical, Parental leave, Sick leave, Unpaid leave, Internship, Student worker, Part-time retirement
- Edge Cases: Multiple concurrent models, Temporary changes, International/Secondment, On-call work

**See:** Phase 4.5 for complete work time model documentation

# COMPREHENSIVE GLOSSARY: CRITICAL TERMS FOR SHARED UNDERSTANDING

**IMPORTANT: Read this glossary FIRST to ensure shared understanding of all critical terms used in this document. Every term below is used throughout the document and must be understood correctly for successful implementation.**

---

## 📚 COMPREHENSIVE TERM DEFINITIONS

### A. Development & Code Quality Terms

**Production-Ready Code**: Code that is complete, tested, documented, and ready to be deployed to a production environment. It has:
- No TODOs, FIXMEs, or placeholders
- No mock data or fake implementations
- Proper error handling
- Complete functionality
- Documentation
- Tests (if applicable)

**Mock Data / Fake Data**: Simulated data used for testing or development. **NOT ALLOWED** in production code. All data must come from real database queries or user input.

**Placeholder**: Temporary code or text that will be replaced later. Examples: `// TODO: implement this`, `"PLACEHOLDER TEXT"`, `return null; // will implement`. **NOT ALLOWED** in production code.

**TODO / FIXME**: Comments in code indicating work that needs to be done. **NOT ALLOWED** in production code. All TODOs must be completed or removed.

**Refactoring**: The process of restructuring existing code without changing its external behavior. In this context: removing Vue.js and replacing with PHP/vanilla JS while maintaining all functionality.

**Legacy Code**: Old code that may not follow current best practices. The current Vue.js implementation is "legacy" and needs to be refactored.

**Technical Debt**: The cost of maintaining code that doesn't follow best practices. Accumulated by shortcuts, workarounds, or outdated patterns.

**Code Smell**: Code that works but indicates a deeper problem (e.g., long methods, duplicate code, magic numbers).

**Hardcoded**: Values written directly in code instead of using variables, configuration, or translation functions. Example: `color: #000000;` (hardcoded) vs `color: var(--color-main-text);` (configurable).

**String Concatenation**: Joining strings together. In SQL, this is dangerous: `"SELECT * FROM users WHERE id = " . $id` (dangerous - SQL injection risk). Use parameterized queries instead.

**Parameterized Query / Prepared Statement**: A database query where user input is passed as parameters, not concatenated into the SQL string. Example: `$db->prepare("SELECT * FROM users WHERE id = ?")->execute([$id])` (safe).

**Type Safety**: Ensuring variables have specific types (string, int, array, etc.). PHP 8.1+ supports strict types: `declare(strict_types=1);`.

**Type Hint**: Specifying the expected type of a function parameter or return value. Example: `public function method(string $param): array`.

**Strict Types**: PHP feature that enforces type checking. Enabled with `declare(strict_types=1);` at the top of PHP files.

**PSR (PHP Standards Recommendation)**: Standards for PHP code. PSR-4 is the autoloading standard (how classes are loaded). PSR-12 is the coding style standard.

**Autoloading**: Automatically loading PHP classes when they're needed, without manual `require` statements. PSR-4 defines the standard.

**Namespace**: A way to organize PHP classes and avoid naming conflicts. Example: `namespace OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Controller;`.

**Class**: A blueprint for creating objects in object-oriented programming. Example: `class TimeEntryController extends Controller`.

**Interface**: A contract that classes must implement. Defines methods that must be present. Example: `interface ITimeEntryService`.

**Trait**: Reusable code that can be included in multiple classes. Example: `trait CSPTrait` can be used in multiple controllers.

**Abstract Class**: A class that cannot be instantiated directly, only extended by other classes.

**Inheritance**: When a class extends another class, inheriting its properties and methods. Example: `class MyController extends Controller`.

**Dependency Injection (DI)**: Providing dependencies to a class via constructor parameters, rather than creating them inside the class. Makes code testable and maintainable.

**Service**: A class that contains business logic. Example: `TimeEntryService` handles all time entry operations.

**Controller**: A class that handles HTTP requests and returns responses. Example: `TimeEntryController` handles requests to `/api/time-entries`.

**Mapper**: A class that handles database operations for a specific entity. Example: `TimeEntryMapper` handles all database operations for `TimeEntry`.

**Entity**: A class representing a database table row. Example: `TimeEntry` entity represents a row in the `time_entries` table.

**Template**: A PHP file that generates HTML. Example: `templates/dashboard.php` generates the HTML for the dashboard page.

**Component**: A reusable piece of UI or functionality. Can be a CSS class, JavaScript function, or PHP template partial.

**Validation**: Checking that data meets certain criteria (type, format, range, business rules) before using it.

**Sanitization**: Cleaning data to remove potentially dangerous content (e.g., removing HTML tags from user input).

**Escaping**: Converting special characters to safe representations to prevent XSS attacks. Example: `&` becomes `&amp;` in HTML.

**Encoding**: Converting data from one format to another (e.g., JSON encoding, URL encoding).

**Decoding**: Converting encoded data back to its original format.

**Serialization**: Converting an object or data structure into a format that can be stored or transmitted (e.g., JSON, XML).

**Deserialization**: Converting serialized data back into an object or data structure.

---

### B. Security Terms

**CSP (Content Security Policy)**: A security standard that prevents XSS attacks by controlling which resources can be loaded and executed. In Nextcloud, inline scripts MUST use a nonce (random token).

**Nonce**: A random token generated by Nextcloud for each page load. Used in CSP to allow inline scripts/styles. Format: `nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>"`.

**CORS (Cross-Origin Resource Sharing)**: A security mechanism that controls which origins can make requests to your API. Nextcloud apps should use same-origin requests only (no cross-origin requests).

**Same-Origin**: Requests from the same domain, protocol, and port. Example: `https://nextcloud.example.com/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api` is same-origin as `https://nextcloud.example.com`.

**Cross-Origin**: Requests from a different domain, protocol, or port. Example: `https://api.example.com` is cross-origin from `https://nextcloud.example.com`.

**CSRF (Cross-Site Request Forgery)**: An attack where a malicious site makes requests on behalf of an authenticated user. Prevented by validating CSRF tokens on all state-changing operations (POST, PUT, DELETE).

**CSRF Token**: A random token included in forms to verify the request came from the legitimate site, not a malicious site.

**XSS (Cross-Site Scripting)**: An attack where malicious scripts are injected into web pages. Prevented by escaping all user input before outputting it.

**SQL Injection**: An attack where malicious SQL code is injected into database queries. Prevented by using parameterized queries (prepared statements) instead of string concatenation.

**Command Injection**: An attack where malicious commands are injected into system commands. Prevented by not executing user input as commands.

**Code Injection**: An attack where malicious code is injected and executed. Prevented by not using `eval()` or similar functions.

**Input Validation**: Checking that user input meets expected criteria (type, format, range) before using it. Must be done server-side (never trust client-side validation).

**Output Escaping**: Converting special characters in output to prevent XSS. Example: `&` becomes `&amp;`, `<` becomes `&lt;`.

**Context-Aware Escaping**: Escaping output differently based on context (HTML, JavaScript, URL, CSS). Different contexts require different escaping.

**Authentication**: Verifying who a user is (login process). Uses Nextcloud's authentication system.

**Authorization**: Verifying what a user is allowed to do (permission checks). Uses role-based access control (RBAC).

**RBAC (Role-Based Access Control)**: A security model where access is controlled by user roles (Employee, Manager, Admin). Each role has specific permissions.

**Permission**: The right to perform a specific action (e.g., "view time entries", "approve absences").

**Role**: A collection of permissions assigned to users (e.g., Employee, Manager, Admin).

**Defense in Depth**: A security strategy using multiple layers of security (authentication, authorization, input validation, output escaping) so that if one layer fails, others still protect.

**Fail-Secure**: A security principle where if something goes wrong, the system defaults to denying access rather than allowing it.

**Least Privilege**: A security principle where users have only the minimum permissions needed to perform their tasks.

**Whitelist**: A list of allowed values. Validation using a whitelist only allows known good values. More secure than blacklist.

**Blacklist**: A list of forbidden values. Validation using a blacklist blocks known bad values. Less secure than whitelist (new attacks may not be on the list).

**Security Header**: HTTP headers that provide additional security (e.g., CSP, X-Frame-Options, X-Content-Type-Options).

**X-Frame-Options**: A security header that prevents the page from being embedded in an iframe (prevents clickjacking).

**X-Content-Type-Options**: A security header that prevents MIME type sniffing (browser guessing content type).

**X-XSS-Protection**: A security header that enables browser XSS protection (legacy, CSP is preferred).

**Strict-Transport-Security (HSTS)**: A security header that forces HTTPS connections.

**Referrer-Policy**: A security header that controls how much referrer information is sent with requests.

**Permissions-Policy**: A security header that controls which browser features can be used.

**Session**: A period of interaction between a user and the application. Maintained by Nextcloud's session system.

**Session Hijacking**: An attack where an attacker steals a user's session and uses it to impersonate the user.

**Session Fixation**: An attack where an attacker forces a user to use a specific session ID that the attacker knows.

**Token**: A random string used for security (CSRF token, authentication token, etc.).

**Audit Log / Audit Trail**: A record of all actions performed in the system (who, what, when, why). Required for legal compliance and security.

**Penetration Testing**: Testing the system's security by attempting to exploit vulnerabilities (ethical hacking).

**Vulnerability**: A weakness in the system that could be exploited by an attacker.

**Exploit**: Code or technique that takes advantage of a vulnerability.

**Patch**: A fix for a vulnerability or bug.

**Security Audit**: A systematic review of the system's security to identify vulnerabilities.

---

### C. Architecture & Design Terms

**MVC (Model-View-Controller)**: An architectural pattern:
- **Model**: Data structures (database entities, e.g., `TimeEntry`, `Absence`)
- **View**: Presentation layer (PHP templates that render HTML)
- **Controller**: Request handlers (PHP classes that process HTTP requests)

**Service Layer**: Business logic organized into service classes (e.g., `TimeEntryService`, `AbsenceService`). Controllers are thin and delegate to services.

**Repository Pattern**: A design pattern where database access is abstracted through mapper classes. Controllers and services don't write SQL directly.

**Template Inheritance**: A pattern where a base template (e.g., `layout.php`) defines the structure, and page templates extend it. Reduces code duplication.

**Separation of Concerns**: Organizing code so that each part has a single, well-defined responsibility (controllers handle requests, services handle business logic, mappers handle database).

**DRY (Don't Repeat Yourself)**: A principle that code should not be duplicated. Use functions, classes, or templates to avoid repetition.

**KISS (Keep It Simple, Stupid)**: A principle that solutions should be as simple as possible.

**YAGNI (You Aren't Gonna Need It)**: A principle that you shouldn't add functionality until it's actually needed.

**SOLID**: Five object-oriented design principles:
- **S**ingle Responsibility: Each class has one reason to change
- **O**pen/Closed: Open for extension, closed for modification
- **L**iskov Substitution: Subtypes must be substitutable for their base types
- **I**nterface Segregation: Clients shouldn't depend on interfaces they don't use
- **D**ependency Inversion: Depend on abstractions, not concretions

**Design Pattern**: A reusable solution to a common problem in software design.

**Anti-Pattern**: A common solution that seems correct but actually causes more problems than it solves.

**Code Review**: Examining code changes before they're merged to ensure quality, security, and correctness.

**Peer Review**: Code review done by other developers (peers).

**Pair Programming**: Two developers working together on the same code, one writing, one reviewing.

**Refactoring**: Restructuring code without changing its behavior.

**Technical Debt**: The cost of maintaining code that doesn't follow best practices.

**Legacy Code**: Old code that may not follow current best practices.

**Monolith**: A single, large application. Opposite of microservices.

**Microservices**: An architecture where the application is split into many small, independent services.

**API (Application Programming Interface)**: A set of functions and procedures that allow applications to communicate with each other.

**REST (Representational State Transfer)**: An architectural style for designing web services. Uses HTTP methods (GET, POST, PUT, DELETE) and status codes.

**RESTful**: Following REST principles.

**Endpoint**: A specific URL where an API can be accessed. Example: `/api/time-entries`.

**HTTP Method**: The type of request (GET, POST, PUT, DELETE, PATCH, etc.).

**Status Code**: A number indicating the result of an HTTP request (200 OK, 404 Not Found, 403 Forbidden, 500 Internal Server Error, etc.).

**JSON (JavaScript Object Notation)**: A data format commonly used for API responses.

**XML (eXtensible Markup Language)**: A data format for structured data (less common than JSON now).

**Webhook**: A way for an application to notify another application when an event occurs. The receiving application provides a URL that gets called.

**Integration**: Connecting different systems or components to work together.

**Third-Party**: External services or libraries not developed by your team.

**CDN (Content Delivery Network)**: A network of servers that deliver content (images, CSS, JS) from locations closer to users. **NOT USED** in Nextcloud apps (all resources from 'self').

**External Resource**: A resource (CSS, JS, image) loaded from outside the application (e.g., from a CDN). **NOT ALLOWED** in Nextcloud apps (CSP violation).

---

### D. Nextcloud-Specific Terms

**OCP (Open Cloud Platform)**: Nextcloud's public API namespace. All Nextcloud interfaces are in the `OCP\` namespace. Example: `OCP\IUserSession`, `OCP\IDBConnection`.

**App Framework**: Nextcloud's framework for building apps. Provides controllers, services, dependency injection, routing, etc.

**TemplateResponse**: A Nextcloud response class for rendering PHP templates. Example: `new TemplateResponse('arbeitszeitcheck', 'dashboard', $params)`.

**JSONResponse**: A Nextcloud response class for returning JSON data. Example: `new JSONResponse(['success' => true])`.

**DataResponse**: A Nextcloud response class for returning structured data (similar to JSONResponse).

**RedirectResponse**: A Nextcloud response class for redirecting to another URL.

**NotFoundResponse**: A Nextcloud response class for 404 Not Found errors.

**ForbiddenResponse**: A Nextcloud response class for 403 Forbidden errors.

**IRegistrationContext**: The context used in `Application::register()` to register services, controllers, and capabilities with Nextcloud's DI container.

**IBootContext**: The context used in `Application::boot()` to perform initialization tasks (e.g., loading CSS/JS files).

**Util::addStyle()**: A Nextcloud function to load a CSS file. Example: `Util::addStyle('arbeitszeitcheck', 'dashboard')`.

**Util::addScript()**: A Nextcloud function to load a JavaScript file. Example: `Util::addScript('arbeitszeitcheck', 'dashboard')`.

**link_to()**: A Nextcloud function to generate URLs to app files. Example: `link_to('arbeitszeitcheck', 'css/common/base.css')`.

**image_path()**: A Nextcloud function to generate URLs to app images. Example: `image_path('arbeitszeitcheck', 'icon.png')`.

**$l->t()**: Nextcloud's translation function in PHP templates. Example: `<?php p($l->t('Dashboard')); ?>`.

**$l->n()**: Nextcloud's pluralization function in PHP templates. Example: `<?php p($l->n('1 item', '%n items', $count)); ?>`.

**t()**: Nextcloud's translation function in JavaScript. Example: `t('arbeitszeitcheck', 'Dashboard')`.

**n()**: Nextcloud's pluralization function in JavaScript. Example: `n('arbeitszeitcheck', '1 item', '%n items', count)`.

**p()**: Nextcloud's escaping function for output. Example: `<?php p($variable); ?>` (escapes HTML).

**print_unescaped()**: Nextcloud's function for outputting trusted HTML without escaping. Use only for trusted content. Example: `<?php print_unescaped($html); ?>`.

**CSPTrait**: A trait (reusable code) for configuring CSP in controllers. Used via `use CSPTrait;` and `$this->configureCSP($response)`.

**IUserSession**: Nextcloud interface for user session management. Get current user: `$userSession->getUser()->getUID()`.

**IDBConnection**: Nextcloud interface for database access. Use instead of direct PDO or mysqli.

**IConfig**: Nextcloud interface for configuration management. Get app config: `$config->getAppValue('arbeitszeitcheck', 'key', 'default')`.

**ILogger / LoggerInterface**: Nextcloud/PSR-3 interface for logging. Use: `$logger->info('message')`.

**ICache**: Nextcloud interface for caching. Store: `$cache->set('key', $value, $ttl)`. Get: `$cache->get('key')`.

**Mapper**: A Nextcloud class for database operations. Extends `\OCP\AppFramework\Db\Mapper`. Example: `class TimeEntryMapper extends Mapper`.

**Entity**: A Nextcloud class representing a database table row. Extends `\OCP\AppFramework\Db\Entity`. Example: `class TimeEntry extends Entity`.

**Migration**: A Nextcloud class for database schema changes. Located in `lib/Migration/Version[number]Date[YYYYMMDDHHMMSS].php`.

**Capabilities**: A Nextcloud class that declares what the app can do. Implements `\OCP\Capabilities\ICapability`. Registered in `Application::register()`.

**Event Listener**: A class that responds to Nextcloud events (e.g., user created, user deleted). Registered in `Application::register()`.

**Background Job**: A class that runs tasks in the background (e.g., sending emails, cleanup tasks). Extends `\OCP\BackgroundJob\Job`.

**Command**: A class that provides CLI commands (e.g., `php occ arbeitszeitcheck:command`). Extends `\OCP\Console\ICommand`.

**Route**: A mapping between a URL and a controller method. Defined in `appinfo/routes.php`.

**App ID**: The unique identifier for the app (e.g., `arbeitszeitcheck`). Used in namespaces, routes, translations, etc.

**Namespace**: The PHP namespace for the app. Format: `OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\...` (matches app ID with proper capitalization).

---

### E. Time Tracking & Business Domain Terms

**Time Entry**: A record of work time (start time, end time, break time) for a specific date. The core data entity in the system.

**Clock In**: The action of starting a work period. Records the start time.

**Clock Out**: The action of ending a work period. Records the end time.

**Break**: A period of rest during work. Required by German law: 30 minutes after 6 hours, 45 minutes after 9 hours.

**Rest Period**: The time between the end of one work day and the start of the next. German law requires minimum 11 hours.

**Overtime**: Hours worked beyond the required hours (from working time model). Can be positive (worked more) or negative (worked less).

**Undertime**: Hours worked less than required. Same as negative overtime.

**Absence**: A period when an employee is not working (vacation, sick leave, etc.).

**Vacation**: Paid time off from work. Employees request vacation, managers approve/reject.

**Sick Leave**: Time off due to illness. May require medical certificate after 3 days.

**Unpaid Leave**: Time off without pay. Employee takes leave but doesn't get paid.

**Parental Leave (Elternzeit)**: Leave for parents (up to 3 years per child). Protected by law.

**Sabbatical**: Extended unpaid leave (typically 3-12 months) for personal development or rest.

**Absence Request**: An employee's request for time off. Status: Pending, Approved, or Rejected.

**Approval**: A manager's decision to allow an absence request or time correction. Status changes from Pending to Approved.

**Rejection**: A manager's decision to deny an absence request or time correction. Status changes from Pending to Rejected. Manager can provide a reason.

**Pending**: Status of a request that is waiting for manager approval.

**Approved**: Status of a request that has been approved by a manager.

**Rejected**: Status of a request that has been rejected by a manager.

**Manager**: A user role with permission to approve/reject requests from their team members and view team data.

**Admin**: A user role with full access to all features, including user management and system configuration.

**Employee**: A user role with permission to track their own time and request absences.

**Team**: A group of employees managed by a specific manager. Managers can only see data from their team.

**Working Time Model**: A configuration that defines required working hours (daily, weekly) and rules (breaks, overtime, etc.). Examples: Full-time 40h, Part-time 20h, Flexible.

**Full-Time (Vollzeit)**: Standard full-time employment, typically 35-40 hours per week.

**Part-Time (Teilzeit)**: Reduced working hours compared to full-time. Can be 50%, 75%, 80%, or custom hours.

**Flexible Working Hours (Gleitzeit)**: Flexible start/end times within core hours. Employees can choose when to work within limits.

**Trust-Based Working Time (Vertrauensarbeitszeit)**: Employees manage their own time, no fixed hours. System tracks target hours.

**Shift Work (Schichtarbeit)**: Work in shifts (morning, afternoon, night). Requires shift schedule configuration.

**Compressed Work Week**: Full-time hours in fewer days (e.g., 40 hours in 4 days = 10 hours/day).

**Annualized Hours (Jahresarbeitszeit)**: Hours calculated over a year, not per week. Allows variable weekly hours.

**Job Sharing**: Two employees share one full-time position (e.g., each works 20 hours/week).

**Minijob**: Part-time work up to 520€/month (approximately 10-15 hours/week). Special tax/social security rules.

**Midijob**: Part-time work between 520€ and 1,600€/month (approximately 15-30 hours/week). Special tax/social security rules.

**On-Call Work (Bereitschaftsdienst)**: Employee is available but not actively working. Different rules than active work.

**Secondment (Auslandseinsatz)**: Work in a different country/timezone. Requires timezone handling.

**Vacation Days / Vacation Entitlement**: The number of vacation days an employee is entitled to per year (typically 25-30 days in Germany).

**Vacation Balance**: The number of vacation days remaining (entitlement minus used days).

**Working Days**: Days that count toward vacation (typically excludes weekends and holidays). Example: 8 calendar days = 6 working days (if Mon-Fri work week).

**Calendar Days**: All days including weekends. Example: March 15-22 = 8 calendar days.

**Compliance**: Adherence to legal requirements (German labor law - ArbZG, GDPR, etc.).

**Compliance Violation**: A situation where legal requirements are not met (e.g., worked more than 10 hours, missing break, insufficient rest period).

**Violation Severity**: The seriousness of a violation (Info, Warning, Error). Errors are critical and must be addressed.

**Compliance Check**: Automatic verification that time entries meet legal requirements (breaks, hours, rest periods).

**Compliance Report**: A report showing compliance status, violations, and statistics for a date range.

**Audit Log**: A record of all actions in the system (who, what, when, why). Required for legal compliance.

**Data Retention**: The period for which data must be kept. German law requires minimum 2 years for working time records.

**Export**: Generating a file (JSON, CSV, PDF) containing user data. Required for GDPR (right to data portability).

**GDPR Request**: A user's request under GDPR (export data, correct data, delete data).

**Right to Access**: GDPR right to receive a copy of all personal data. Implemented via export functionality.

**Right to Rectification**: GDPR right to correct inaccurate data. Users can request corrections.

**Right to Erasure**: GDPR right to have data deleted. Implemented after retention period expires.

**Data Minimization**: GDPR principle that only necessary data should be collected.

**Purpose Limitation**: GDPR principle that data should only be used for stated purposes.

**Storage Limitation**: GDPR principle that data should not be kept longer than necessary (but must meet retention requirements).

---

### F. Legal & Compliance Terms

**ArbZG (Arbeitszeitgesetz)**: German Working Time Act. Regulates:
- Maximum daily working time (8 hours, can extend to 10 if 6-month average is 8)
- Maximum weekly working time (48 hours average over 6 months)
- Break requirements (30 min after 6h, 45 min after 9h)
- Rest period (11 hours minimum)
- Sunday/holiday work restrictions
- Night work regulations (11 PM - 6 AM)
- Record keeping requirements (2 years minimum)

**GDPR (General Data Protection Regulation)**: EU regulation on data protection. Requires:
- Right to access (export data)
- Right to rectification (correct data)
- Right to erasure (delete data after retention period)
- Data minimization (only collect necessary data)
- Purpose limitation (use data only for stated purposes)
- Storage limitation (don't keep data longer than necessary)
- Security measures (protect data)
- Transparency (privacy policy, data processing information)

**Works Council (Betriebsrat)**: An employee representative body in German companies (if company has 5+ employees). Can negotiate agreements (Betriebsvereinbarung) that allow exceptions to standard rules.

**Works Council Agreement (Betriebsvereinbarung)**: An agreement between employer and works council that may allow exceptions to standard working time rules (e.g., Sunday work, extended hours).

**ECJ C-55/18**: European Court of Justice ruling requiring employers to record working time. Implemented in EU Directive 2019/1152.

**EU Directive 2019/1152**: EU directive requiring employers to record working time. German law implements this.

**Record Keeping**: The legal requirement to record and store working time data. German law requires minimum 2 years retention.

**Retention Period**: How long data must be kept. German law: minimum 2 years for working time records.

**Legal Compliance**: Adherence to all applicable laws and regulations (ArbZG, GDPR, etc.).

**Compliance Audit**: A review to verify that the system meets legal requirements.

**Legal Review**: Review by legal experts to verify compliance. Recommended before production deployment.

---

### G. Testing Terms

**Unit Test**: A test for a single function or method in isolation. Tests the smallest unit of code.

**Integration Test**: A test that verifies multiple components work together correctly (e.g., controller + service + database).

**Functional Test**: A test that verifies a feature works end-to-end from user perspective.

**System Test**: A test that verifies the entire system works together.

**Acceptance Test / UAT (User Acceptance Testing)**: Testing by actual users to verify the system meets their needs.

**Regression Test**: A test that verifies existing functionality still works after changes.

**Smoke Test**: Quick tests to verify basic functionality works (e.g., app loads, login works).

**Sanity Test**: Quick tests to verify the system is stable enough for more thorough testing.

**Exploratory Test**: Unscripted testing where testers explore the system to find issues.

**Ad-Hoc Test**: Informal testing without a test plan.

**Manual Test**: Testing performed by a human (clicking, typing, observing).

**Automated Test**: Testing performed by software (scripts, test frameworks).

**Test Coverage**: The percentage of code that is tested. Target: 70% overall, 100% for critical business logic.

**Code Coverage**: The percentage of code lines executed during tests.

**Branch Coverage**: The percentage of code branches (if/else) executed during tests.

**Statement Coverage**: The percentage of code statements executed during tests.

**Test Case**: A specific scenario to test (e.g., "Employee clocks in at 8:00 AM").

**Test Scenario**: A broader set of related test cases (e.g., "Complete time tracking workflow").

**Test Plan**: A document describing what will be tested, how, and when.

**Test Report**: A document describing test results, issues found, and pass/fail status.

**Bug / Defect**: An error or flaw in the system that causes incorrect behavior.

**Error**: A mistake in code that causes incorrect behavior.

**Exception**: An error condition that interrupts normal program flow. Must be handled (caught) or program crashes.

**Failure**: When a test does not pass (expected behavior doesn't match actual behavior).

**Incident**: An unplanned event that disrupts service (e.g., system outage, data loss).

**Outage**: When the system is unavailable to users.

**Downtime**: The period when the system is unavailable.

**Uptime**: The period when the system is available.

**SLA (Service Level Agreement)**: A commitment to a certain level of service (e.g., 99.9% uptime).

**SLO (Service Level Objective)**: A target for a specific metric (e.g., response time < 200ms).

**SLI (Service Level Indicator)**: A metric that measures service quality (e.g., actual response time).

**MTTR (Mean Time To Repair)**: Average time to fix an issue.

**MTBF (Mean Time Between Failures)**: Average time between system failures.

**Availability**: The percentage of time the system is available (uptime / total time).

**Reliability**: The probability that the system will work correctly for a given period.

**Resilience**: The ability to recover quickly from failures.

**Fault Tolerance**: The ability to continue operating despite failures.

**Graceful Degradation**: When a system continues to work with reduced functionality when some features fail.

**Load Test**: Testing the system under expected load (normal usage).

**Stress Test**: Testing the system under extreme load (beyond normal usage).

**Endurance Test**: Testing the system for an extended period (e.g., 24 hours) to find memory leaks or performance degradation.

**Spike Test**: Testing the system's response to sudden load spikes.

**Volume Test**: Testing the system with large amounts of data (e.g., 1 million time entries).

**Scalability Test**: Testing the system's ability to handle increased load.

**Performance Test**: Testing the system's speed, responsiveness, and resource usage.

**Security Test**: Testing the system's security (penetration testing, vulnerability scanning).

**Penetration Test**: Attempting to exploit vulnerabilities to test security (ethical hacking).

**Vulnerability Scan**: Automated scanning for known vulnerabilities.

**Accessibility Test**: Testing that the system is usable by people with disabilities (screen readers, keyboard navigation, etc.).

---

### H. Performance & Optimization Terms

**Performance**: How fast and responsive the system is.

**Benchmark**: A standard test used to measure performance. Example: "Page load time < 2 seconds".

**Response Time**: Time between a request and response. Example: API response < 200ms.

**Latency**: Delay in data transmission. Similar to response time.

**Throughput**: Number of requests processed per second. Example: 100 requests/second.

**QPS (Queries Per Second)**: Number of database queries per second.

**RPS (Requests Per Second)**: Number of HTTP requests per second.

**TPS (Transactions Per Second)**: Number of database transactions per second.

**Concurrency**: Number of simultaneous users or requests.

**Parallelism**: Executing multiple operations simultaneously (using multiple CPU cores).

**Scalability**: Ability to handle increased load by adding resources.

**Horizontal Scaling**: Adding more servers to handle increased load.

**Vertical Scaling**: Adding more resources (CPU, RAM) to existing servers.

**Load Balancing**: Distributing requests across multiple servers.

**Caching**: Storing frequently accessed data in fast storage (memory) to avoid slow operations (database queries).

**Cache Hit**: When requested data is found in cache (fast).

**Cache Miss**: When requested data is not in cache (must fetch from source, slower).

**Cache Invalidation**: Removing or updating cached data when source data changes.

**Cache Warming**: Pre-loading cache with frequently accessed data.

**Cache Stampede / Thundering Herd**: When many requests try to refresh cache simultaneously after expiration.

**TTL (Time To Live)**: How long cached data is valid before expiration.

**LRU (Least Recently Used)**: Cache eviction strategy - removes least recently used items when cache is full.

**LFU (Least Frequently Used)**: Cache eviction strategy - removes least frequently used items when cache is full.

**FIFO (First In First Out)**: Cache eviction strategy - removes oldest items when cache is full.

**Pagination**: Splitting large datasets into smaller pages (e.g., 50 items per page).

**Lazy Loading**: Loading data only when needed, not all at once.

**Eager Loading**: Loading all related data at once (opposite of lazy loading).

**Database Index**: A data structure that speeds up database queries (like an index in a book).

**Query Optimization**: Improving database queries to run faster (using indexes, avoiding N+1 problems, etc.).

**N+1 Query Problem**: When code makes 1 query to get a list, then N additional queries (one per item) to get related data. Should be fixed with joins or eager loading.

**Full Table Scan**: When database must scan entire table to find data (slow). Should use indexes instead.

**EXPLAIN**: A database command that shows how a query will be executed (useful for optimization).

**Slow Query Log**: A log of database queries that take longer than a threshold (e.g., > 1 second).

**Connection Pool**: A pool of reusable database connections to avoid overhead of creating new connections.

**Transaction**: A group of database operations that must all succeed or all fail (atomicity).

**ACID**: Properties of database transactions:
- **A**tomicity: All or nothing
- **C**onsistency: Data remains valid
- **I**solation: Transactions don't interfere
- **D**urability: Changes are permanent

**Isolation Level**: How transactions are isolated from each other (Read Committed, Repeatable Read, Serializable, etc.).

**Deadlock**: When two transactions are waiting for each other, causing both to hang.

**Race Condition**: When the outcome depends on the timing of operations (can cause bugs).

**Optimistic Locking**: Assuming no conflicts, checking at commit time. If conflict, retry.

**Pessimistic Locking**: Locking data immediately to prevent conflicts.

**Minification**: Removing whitespace and comments from code to reduce file size.

**Uglification**: Renaming variables to shorter names to reduce file size (JavaScript).

**Bundling**: Combining multiple files into one file.

**Tree Shaking**: Removing unused code from bundles.

**Code Splitting**: Splitting code into multiple bundles that load on demand.

**Asset Optimization**: Optimizing images, CSS, JS files (compression, minification, etc.).

---

### I. Deployment & Operations Terms

**Deployment**: The process of releasing code to production.

**Staging**: An environment that mirrors production, used for final testing before deployment.

**Production**: The live environment where real users use the system.

**Development**: The environment where developers write and test code.

**Environment**: A specific configuration (development, staging, production) with its own database, settings, etc.

**Rollback**: Reverting to a previous version if deployment fails.

**Hotfix**: An urgent fix deployed directly to production (bypassing normal process).

**Patch**: A small fix or update.

**Version**: A specific release of the software (e.g., 1.0.0, 1.1.0, 2.0.0).

**Semantic Versioning**: Version numbering scheme: MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH (e.g., 1.2.3). MAJOR = breaking changes, MINOR = new features, PATCH = bug fixes.

**Breaking Change**: A change that breaks compatibility with previous versions.

**Backward Compatibility**: New version works with data/config from old version.

**Forward Compatibility**: Old version can work with data/config from new version (rare).

**Deprecation**: Marking something as obsolete, to be removed in future version.

**Migration**: Moving data or configuration from old version to new version.

**Upgrade**: Moving to a newer version.

**Downgrade**: Moving to an older version.

**Data Migration**: Moving data from old system/version to new system/version.

**Schema Migration**: Changing database structure (adding tables, columns, indexes, etc.).

**Backup**: A copy of data that can be restored if needed.

**Restore**: Recovering data from a backup.

**Point-in-Time Recovery**: Restoring data to a specific point in time.

**Disaster Recovery**: Recovering from a major failure (server crash, data center outage, etc.).

**RTO (Recovery Time Objective)**: Maximum acceptable downtime (e.g., 1 hour).

**RPO (Recovery Point Objective)**: Maximum acceptable data loss (e.g., 15 minutes of data).

**BCP (Business Continuity Plan)**: Plan to continue operations during disaster.

**DRP (Disaster Recovery Plan)**: Plan to recover from disaster.

**High Availability (HA)**: System designed to minimize downtime (e.g., 99.9% uptime).

**Failover**: Automatically switching to backup system when primary fails.

**Failback**: Switching back to primary system after it's fixed.

**Active-Passive**: One system active, one on standby.

**Active-Active**: Multiple systems active, sharing load.

**Monitoring**: Observing system health, performance, errors in real-time.

**Alerting**: Notifying operators when issues occur (errors, performance degradation, etc.).

**Logging**: Recording events, errors, and actions for debugging and auditing.

**Tracing**: Tracking a request through multiple services/components.

**Metrics**: Quantitative measurements (response time, error rate, CPU usage, etc.).

**Telemetry**: Data collected about system behavior (metrics, logs, traces).

**Dashboard**: A visual display of system metrics and status.

**Visualization**: Graphical representation of data (charts, graphs, etc.).

**Analytics**: Analysis of data to gain insights.

**Anomaly Detection**: Identifying unusual patterns that may indicate problems.

**Outlier**: A data point that is significantly different from others.

**Baseline**: Normal/expected values for comparison.

**Threshold**: A value that triggers an alert when exceeded (e.g., error rate > 1%).

**Percentile**: A value below which a percentage of data falls. P95 = 95% of requests are faster than this.

**P50 / Median**: 50th percentile (half are faster, half are slower).

**P95**: 95th percentile (95% are faster).

**P99**: 99th percentile (99% are faster).

**Runbook**: Step-by-step procedures for common operations (deployment, troubleshooting, etc.).

**Playbook**: Similar to runbook, but for specific scenarios.

**SOP (Standard Operating Procedure)**: Documented procedure for routine tasks.

**Incident Response**: Process for handling incidents (outages, security breaches, etc.).

**Postmortem**: Analysis of an incident after it's resolved to learn and improve.

**Retrospective**: Team meeting to reflect on what went well and what to improve.

**Blameless Postmortem**: Postmortem focused on learning, not assigning blame.

**Root Cause Analysis (RCA)**: Finding the underlying cause of a problem (not just symptoms).

**Five Whys**: Technique of asking "why" five times to find root cause.

---

### J. User Experience & Design Terms

**UX (User Experience)**: The overall experience users have when using the system.

**UI (User Interface)**: The visual elements users interact with (buttons, forms, menus, etc.).

**Usability**: How easy the system is to use.

**Accessibility**: Making the system usable by people with disabilities.

**WCAG (Web Content Accessibility Guidelines)**: Standards for web accessibility. Level AAA is the highest.

**ARIA (Accessible Rich Internet Applications)**: Attributes that make web content accessible to screen readers.

**Screen Reader**: Software that reads screen content aloud for visually impaired users.

**Keyboard Navigation**: Ability to use the system with only a keyboard (no mouse).

**Focus Indicator**: Visual indicator showing which element has keyboard focus.

**Color Contrast**: Difference in brightness between text and background. WCAG requires minimum 7:1 for AAA.

**Theme**: Visual appearance (colors, fonts, etc.). Light theme and dark theme are common.

**Light Theme**: Theme with light background, dark text.

**Dark Theme**: Theme with dark background, light text.

**CSS Variable**: A CSS feature that allows defining reusable values. Example: `var(--color-main-background)`.

**Responsive Design**: Design that adapts to different screen sizes (mobile, tablet, desktop).

**Mobile**: Smartphone-sized screens (typically < 768px width).

**Desktop**: Computer-sized screens (typically > 1024px width).

**Tablet**: Medium-sized screens (typically 768px - 1024px width).

**Breakpoint**: Screen width at which layout changes (e.g., 768px, 1024px).

**Viewport**: The visible area of a web page.

**Touch Target**: An interactive element that can be tapped on mobile. Should be at least 44x44 pixels.

**PWA (Progressive Web App)**: A web app that works like a native app (can be installed, works offline, etc.).

**Offline**: Working without internet connection.

**Sync**: Synchronizing data between devices or after going back online.

**Conflict Resolution**: Handling situations where the same data was changed in multiple places.

**Draft**: Unsaved changes that can be recovered.

**Concurrent Edit**: When multiple users edit the same data simultaneously.

**Loading State**: Visual indicator that an operation is in progress (spinner, progress bar, etc.).

**Error State**: Visual indicator that an operation failed (error message, red border, etc.).

**Success State**: Visual indicator that an operation succeeded (success message, green checkmark, etc.).

**Empty State**: What users see when there's no data (e.g., "No time entries yet").

**Help Text**: Explanatory text that helps users understand how to use a feature.

**Tooltip**: A small popup that appears when hovering over an element, providing additional information.

**Modal / Dialog**: A popup window that requires user interaction before continuing.

**Toast / Notification**: A temporary message that appears to inform users (e.g., "Time entry saved").

**Breadcrumb**: Navigation showing current location (e.g., Home > Dashboard > Time Entries).

**Onboarding**: Process of introducing new users to the system (tutorial, welcome screen, etc.).

**Tutorial**: Step-by-step guide for new users.

**Help System**: Documentation and assistance available within the app.

**FAQ (Frequently Asked Questions)**: Common questions and answers.

**Troubleshooting Guide**: Step-by-step instructions for solving common problems.

**User-Friendly**: Easy to use, even for non-technical users.

**Intuitive**: Easy to understand without explanation.

**Self-Explanatory**: Clear enough that users understand without help.

**Granny-Proof**: So simple that even a 99-year-old with no computer experience can use it (extreme usability).

---

### K. Data & Database Terms

**Database**: Organized collection of data. Examples: MySQL, PostgreSQL, SQLite.

**Table**: A collection of related data in a database (e.g., `time_entries` table).

**Row / Record**: A single entry in a table (e.g., one time entry).

**Column / Field**: A specific piece of data in a row (e.g., `start_time` column).

**Primary Key**: A unique identifier for each row (e.g., `id`).

**Foreign Key**: A reference to a row in another table (e.g., `user_id` references `users` table).

**Index**: A data structure that speeds up queries (like an index in a book).

**Query**: A request to retrieve or modify data in the database.

**SELECT**: Query to retrieve data.

**INSERT**: Query to add new data.

**UPDATE**: Query to modify existing data.

**DELETE**: Query to remove data.

**WHERE Clause**: Condition that filters which rows are affected.

**JOIN**: Combining data from multiple tables.

**Constraint**: A rule that data must follow (e.g., NOT NULL, UNIQUE, FOREIGN KEY).

**Referential Integrity**: Ensuring foreign keys always reference valid rows (no orphaned records).

**Data Integrity**: Ensuring data is accurate, consistent, and valid.

**Consistency**: Ensuring data doesn't contradict itself (e.g., start time < end time).

**Normalization**: Organizing database to reduce redundancy and improve integrity.

**Denormalization**: Intentionally adding redundancy to improve performance (trade-off).

**Schema**: The structure of the database (tables, columns, indexes, etc.).

**Migration**: Changing the database schema (adding tables, columns, etc.).

**Seed Data**: Initial data loaded into the database (e.g., default working time models).

**Fixture**: Test data used in automated tests.

**Backup**: A copy of the database that can be restored.

**Restore**: Recovering the database from a backup.

**Replication**: Copying data to multiple databases for redundancy or performance.

**UTC (Coordinated Universal Time)**: The standard time used for storing dates/times. All times should be stored in UTC.

**Timezone**: A region's standard time offset from UTC (e.g., UTC+1 for Germany, UTC+2 in summer).

**DST (Daylight Saving Time)**: Adjusting clocks forward/backward by one hour seasonally.

**Timezone Conversion**: Converting time from UTC to user's timezone for display, or vice versa for storage.

**Date / DateTime**: A specific point in time (e.g., 2024-03-15 08:00:00).

**Timestamp**: A number representing a point in time (Unix timestamp: seconds since 1970-01-01).

**Date Range**: A period between two dates (e.g., March 1-31, 2024).

**Time Range**: A period between two times (e.g., 08:00 - 17:00).

**Duration**: Length of time (e.g., 8 hours, 30 minutes).

**Format**: How data is displayed (e.g., "2024-03-15" vs "15.03.2024" vs "March 15, 2024").

**Parse**: Converting a string into a date/time object.

**Format**: Converting a date/time object into a string.

**Leap Year**: Year with 366 days (February 29). Occurs every 4 years (except century years not divisible by 400).

**Leap Day**: February 29 in a leap year.

**Year Boundary**: Transition from one year to the next (December 31 → January 1).

**Midnight**: 00:00:00 (start of a day).

**Noon**: 12:00:00 (middle of a day).

**AM / PM**: 12-hour time format (AM = morning, PM = afternoon/evening).

**24-Hour Format**: Time format using 00:00-23:59 (no AM/PM).

**ISO 8601**: International standard for date/time format (e.g., 2024-03-15T08:00:00Z).

---

### L. Process & Workflow Terms

**Workflow**: A series of steps to complete a task (e.g., "Employee requests vacation → Manager reviews → Manager approves/rejects").

**Process**: Similar to workflow, a series of steps to achieve a goal.

**Step**: A single action in a workflow (e.g., "Employee clicks 'Request Vacation'").

**Action**: Something a user does (click button, submit form, etc.).

**Operation**: A system action (create record, update record, delete record, etc.).

**State**: Current condition of something (e.g., "Pending", "Approved", "Rejected").

**Status**: Similar to state, current condition (e.g., "Active", "Inactive", "Deleted").

**Transition**: Moving from one state to another (e.g., "Pending" → "Approved").

**State Machine**: A model where something can be in different states and transitions between them.

**Business Rule**: A rule that defines how the business operates (e.g., "Employees need manager approval for vacation").

**Validation Rule**: A rule that data must follow (e.g., "Start time must be before end time").

**Constraint**: A limitation or restriction (e.g., "Maximum 10 hours per day").

**Requirement**: Something the system must do (functional requirement) or have (non-functional requirement).

**Functional Requirement**: What the system must do (e.g., "System must track time entries").

**Non-Functional Requirement**: Quality attributes (e.g., "System must load in < 2 seconds").

**Use Case**: A specific way the system is used (e.g., "Employee clocks in at 8:00 AM").

**User Story**: A description of a feature from user's perspective (e.g., "As an employee, I want to clock in so that my work time is recorded").

**Scenario**: A specific situation or example (e.g., "Employee works 8 hours, takes 30-minute break").

**Edge Case**: An unusual or extreme situation (e.g., "Employee works exactly 6 hours - does break requirement trigger?").

**Corner Case**: Similar to edge case, an unusual situation at the boundaries of normal operation.

**Boundary Condition**: A value at the edge of valid range (e.g., exactly 6 hours, exactly 11 hours rest).

**Error Case**: A situation where something goes wrong (e.g., "Database connection fails").

**Exception Case**: An unusual situation that requires special handling (e.g., "User deleted while has pending requests").

**Normal Case / Happy Path**: The typical, expected scenario where everything works correctly.

**Alternative Flow**: A different way a workflow can proceed (e.g., "Manager rejects instead of approves").

**Error Flow**: What happens when an error occurs (e.g., "Validation fails → show error message").

**Recovery**: Returning to normal operation after an error.

**Retry**: Attempting an operation again after it fails.

**Backoff**: Waiting before retrying, with increasing wait time (exponential backoff).

**Timeout**: Maximum time to wait for an operation before giving up.

**Deadline**: Latest time by which something must be completed.

**Cancellation**: Stopping an operation before it completes.

**Context**: Information about the current situation (user, time, location, etc.).

**Propagation**: Passing information through multiple layers (e.g., error propagates from service to controller to user).

---

### M. Quality & Standards Terms

**Quality**: How good something is (meets requirements, works correctly, is maintainable, etc.).

**Quality Gate**: A checkpoint that must be passed before proceeding (e.g., "All tests pass").

**Quality Assurance (QA)**: Process of ensuring quality.

**Quality Control**: Checking that quality standards are met.

**Code Quality**: How well-written code is (readable, maintainable, follows standards, etc.).

**Technical Quality**: Quality of technical implementation (architecture, performance, security, etc.).

**Maintainability**: How easy code is to understand, modify, and extend.

**Readability**: How easy code is to read and understand.

**Testability**: How easy code is to test.

**Reusability**: How easy code is to reuse in different contexts.

**Modularity**: Organizing code into independent, reusable modules.

**Coupling**: How dependent components are on each other. Low coupling is better.

**Cohesion**: How well elements within a component belong together. High cohesion is better.

**Complexity**: How complex code is (cyclomatic complexity, cognitive complexity).

**Cyclomatic Complexity**: Measure of code complexity based on number of decision points (if/else, loops, etc.).

**Cognitive Complexity**: Measure of how difficult code is to understand.

**Technical Debt Ratio**: Percentage of development time spent on technical debt vs new features.

**Code Smell**: Code that works but indicates a deeper problem.

**Best Practice**: A method or technique that is generally accepted as superior.

**Standard**: An established norm or requirement.

**Convention**: An agreed-upon way of doing something (not enforced, but recommended).

**Guideline**: A recommendation for how to do something.

**Requirement**: Something that must be done (mandatory).

**Recommendation**: Something that should be done (optional but suggested).

**Mandatory**: Required, must be done.

**Optional**: Not required, can be done if desired.

**Verification**: Checking that something is correct (e.g., "Does the code work?").

**Validation**: Checking that something meets requirements (e.g., "Does the code meet the requirements?").

**Compliance**: Adherence to standards, regulations, or requirements.

**Audit**: A systematic review to verify compliance or quality.

**Review**: Examining something to assess quality or correctness.

**Inspection**: Detailed examination (similar to review).

**Checklist**: A list of items to verify (ensures nothing is forgotten).

**Criteria**: Standards by which something is judged.

**Metric**: A measurable value (e.g., "Page load time: 1.5 seconds").

**KPI (Key Performance Indicator)**: An important metric that indicates success.

**Benchmark**: A standard test used to measure performance.

**Target**: A goal to achieve (e.g., "Response time < 200ms").

**Threshold**: A value that triggers action when exceeded (e.g., "Alert if error rate > 1%").

**Baseline**: Normal/expected values for comparison.

**Tolerance**: Acceptable deviation from target (e.g., "Target: 2s, Tolerance: ±0.5s").

**Variance**: Difference between actual and expected.

**Deviation**: Departure from standard or expected.

**Anomaly**: Something that deviates from normal.

**Outlier**: A data point significantly different from others.

---

**END OF GLOSSARY**

**This glossary covers ALL critical terms used in this document. If you encounter a term not defined here, it should be added to ensure shared understanding.**

### Step 3: Fix Critical Issues First (MANDATORY)

1. **Fix ALL Priority 1 blockers** (console errors, CSP, CORS, PHP errors)
   - Document each fix
   - Test each fix
   - Verify in browser console

   - Implement all TODO comments (don't just remove them)
   - Replace all placeholder code with real implementations
   - Remove all projectcheck references
   - Add all missing translations

3. **Verify fixes:**
   - Re-run all searches (should return 0)
   - Re-check browser console (should be clean)
   - Re-test functionality (should all pass)

❌ **DON'T:**
- Write placeholder code ("will implement later")
- Skip error handling ("will add later")
- Skip translations ("will translate later")

- Use inline scripts/styles without nonce

- Skip ARIA labels (add immediately)

- After EVERY change: Verify no regressions

## Objective & Scope

### Primary Goal
Refactor `apps/arbeitszeitcheck/` to adopt the sidebar navigation and visual design language of `apps/projectcheck/` while maintaining 100% functionality, improving UX for users of all technical levels, ensuring full Nextcloud theme compatibility, implementing WCAG 2.1 AAA accessibility, and maintaining all existing translations.

### Key Success Metrics
- ✅ **Visual Similarity:** Looks like projectcheck (sidebar, styling, layout)
- ✅ **Functionality:** Zero functionality lost, all features work
- ✅ **Quality:** Production-ready code, no placeholders/mocks
- ✅ **Isolation:** Complete independence from projectcheck
- ✅ **Accessibility:** WCAG 2.1 AAA compliant
- ✅ **Theme Support:** Works with all Nextcloud themes
- ✅ **Translations:** All text translated (DE, EN minimum)
- ✅ **Zero Errors:** No console errors, CSP violations, or CORS errors

### What This Refactoring Includes
- Sidebar navigation matching projectcheck style
- Common CSS files for layout, colors, typography
- Full accessibility implementation (WCAG 2.1 AAA)
- UX improvements (tooltips, help text, better errors)
- Complete translations (German and English)
- Responsive mobile design
- Theme compatibility (light/dark)

### What This Refactoring Does NOT Change
- Backend functionality (all APIs stay the same)
- Database schema (no database changes)
- Business logic (calculations, validations stay same)
- Core features (time tracking, absences, etc. unchanged)

---

## Critical Requirements

### 🚫 ABSOLUTE PROHIBITIONS

**The following are STRICTLY FORBIDDEN and will result in immediate rejection:**

#### 1. NO Placeholders
- ❌ No `// TODO`, `// FIXME`, `// PLACEHOLDER`, `// HACK`
- ❌ No `Lorem ipsum` or dummy text
- ❌ No `[TODO: implement]` comments
- ❌ No "will implement later" anywhere in code
- ✅ All code must be complete and functional NOW

**Example of WRONG:**
```php
// TODO: Implement break time validation
public function validateBreaks($minutes) {
    return true; // placeholder
}
```

**Example of CORRECT:**
```php
public function validateBreaks(int $workMinutes, int $breakMinutes): array {
    $violations = [];
    
    if ($workMinutes > 360 && $breakMinutes < 30) {
        $violations[] = [
            'type' => 'MISSING_BREAK',
            'severity' => 'CRITICAL',
            'message' => 'Minimum 30 minutes break required after 6 hours',
            'required' => 30,
            'actual' => $breakMinutes
        ];
    }
    
    if ($workMinutes > 540 && $breakMinutes < 45) {
        $violations[] = [
            'type' => 'INSUFFICIENT_BREAK',
            'severity' => 'CRITICAL',
            'message' => 'Minimum 45 minutes break required after 9 hours',
            'required' => 45,
            'actual' => $breakMinutes
        ];
    }
    
    return $violations;
}
```

#### 2. NO Mocks or Temporary Code
- ❌ No mock data unless in actual test files
- ❌ No temporary workarounds that need fixing later
- ❌ No "good enough for now" code
- ❌ No `setTimeout()` to simulate async operations
- ✅ Everything must be production-quality immediately

**Example of WRONG:**
```javascript
async function getTimeEntries() {
  // Mock data - will replace with real API later
  return [
    { id: 1, start: '09:00', end: '17:00' }
  ];
}
```

**Example of CORRECT:**
```javascript
async function getTimeEntries(userId, startDate, endDate) {
  try {
    const response = await axios.get(
      generateUrl('/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api/v1/entries'),
      {
        params: { userId, startDate, endDate }
      }
    );
    
    if (response.data.success) {
      return response.data.entries;
    } else {
      throw new Error(response.data.message || 'Failed to load entries');
    }
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error loading time entries:', error);
    showError(t('arbeitszeitcheck', 'Could not load time entries'));
    throw error;
  }
}
```

#### 3. NO Broken Functionality
- ❌ All existing features must work exactly as before
- ❌ No partial implementations
- ❌ No "almost working" code
- ✅ If a feature can't be completed properly, don't start it
- ✅ Each phase must be fully complete before moving to next

#### 4. NO Code from ProjectCheck
- ❌ Never copy-paste code directly from projectcheck
- ✅ Study projectcheck structure and patterns
- ✅ Adapt patterns to arbeitszeitcheck with proper naming
- ✅ All class names, IDs, variables must be arbeitszeitcheck-specific

**Example of WRONG:**
```css
   /* Flexbox Utilities */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-flex {
     display: flex;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-flex-column {
     display: flex;
     flex-direction: column;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-flex-center {
     display: flex;
     align-items: center;
     justify-content: center;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-flex-between {
     display: flex;
     justify-content: space-between;
     align-items: center;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-flex-wrap {
     flex-wrap: wrap;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-flex-1 {
     flex: 1;
   }
   
   /* Grid Utilities */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-grid {
     display: grid;
     gap: var(--default-grid-baseline);
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-grid-2 {
     display: grid;
     grid-template-columns: repeat(2, 1fr);
     gap: var(--default-grid-baseline);
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-grid-3 {
     display: grid;
     grid-template-columns: repeat(3, 1fr);
     gap: var(--default-grid-baseline);
   }
   
   @media (max-width: 768px) {
     .arbeitszeitcheck-grid-2,
     .arbeitszeitcheck-grid-3 {
       grid-template-columns: 1fr;
     }
   }
   
   /* Spacing Utilities */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mt-1 { margin-top: var(--default-grid-baseline); }
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mt-2 { margin-top: calc(var(--default-grid-baseline) * 2); }
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mt-3 { margin-top: calc(var(--default-grid-baseline) * 3); }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mb-1 { margin-bottom: var(--default-grid-baseline); }
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mb-2 { margin-bottom: calc(var(--default-grid-baseline) * 2); }
   .arbeitszeitcheck-mb-3 { margin-bottom: calc(var(--default-grid-baseline) * 3); }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-p-1 { padding: var(--default-grid-baseline); }
   .arbeitszeitcheck-p-2 { padding: calc(var(--default-grid-baseline) * 2); }
   .arbeitszeitcheck-p-3 { padding: calc(var(--default-grid-baseline) * 3); }
   ```

### Phase 5: Accessibility Implementation
**Status:** [ ] Not Started | [ ] In Progress | [ ] Complete
**Estimated Time:** 5-6 hours
**Prerequisites:** Phase 4 Complete

**Objective:** Implement complete WCAG 2.1 AAA accessibility, including keyboard navigation, screen reader support, focus indicators, and high contrast mode.

**Tasks:**

1. [ ] **Create `css/common/accessibility.css`**
   
   Comprehensive accessibility styles:
   ```css
   /**
    * ArbeitszeitCheck Accessibility Styles
    * 
    * WCAG 2.1 AAA compliance styles:
    * - Focus indicators
    * - Screen reader utilities
    * - Skip links
    * - High contrast mode
    * - Reduced motion
    */
   
   /* Focus Indicators (WCAG 2.1 AAA requires 2px minimum) */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__link:focus-visible,
   .arbeitszeitcheck-button:focus-visible,
   .arbeitszeitcheck-input:focus-visible,
   .arbeitszeitcheck-select:focus-visible,
   .arbeitszeitcheck-textarea:focus-visible,
   a:focus-visible,
   button:focus-visible,
   input:focus-visible,
   select:focus-visible,
   textarea:focus-visible {
     outline: 2px solid var(--color-primary);
     outline-offset: 2px;
     /* Note: never use outline: none without replacement */
   }
   
   /* Screen Reader Only (visually hidden but available to assistive tech) */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-sr-only {
     position: absolute;
     width: 1px;
     height: 1px;
     padding: 0;
     margin: -1px;
     overflow: hidden;
     clip: rect(0, 0, 0, 0);
     white-space: nowrap;
     border-width: 0;
   }
   
   /* Screen Reader Only - Focusable (visible when focused) */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-sr-only-focusable:active,
   .arbeitszeitcheck-sr-only-focusable:focus {
     position: static;
     width: auto;
     height: auto;
     overflow: visible;
     clip: auto;
     white-space: normal;
   }
   
   /* Skip Link (for keyboard navigation) */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-skip-link {
     position: absolute;
     top: -40px;
     left: 0;
     background: var(--color-primary);
     color: var(--color-primary-text);
     padding: 8px 16px;
     text-decoration: none;
     z-index: 10000;
   }
   
   .arbeitszeitcheck-skip-link:focus {
     top: 0;
   }
   
   /* High Contrast Mode Support */
   @media (prefers-contrast: high) {
     .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation {
       border-right-width: 2px;
     }
     
     .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__link {
       border: 1px solid transparent;
     }
     
     .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__link:hover {
       border-color: var(--color-main-text);
     }
     
     .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__link--active {
       border-color: var(--color-primary);
       border-width: 2px;
     }
     
     .arbeitszeitcheck-button {
       border: 2px solid var(--color-main-text);
     }
   }
   
   /* Reduced Motion Support */
   @media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce) {
     .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation,
     .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__link,
     .arbeitszeitcheck-button,
     * {
       animation-duration: 0.01ms !important;
       animation-iteration-count: 1 !important;
       transition-duration: 0.01ms !important;
       scroll-behavior: auto !important;
     }
   }
   
   /* Touch Target Size (minimum 44x44px for WCAG AAA) */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__link,
   .arbeitszeitcheck-button,
   a.arbeitszeitcheck-link,
   button.arbeitszeitcheck-btn {
     min-height: 44px;
     min-width: 44px;
   }
   
   /* Ensure sufficient spacing between interactive elements */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__item + .arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__item {
     margin-top: 2px; /* Small gap between touch targets */
   }
   
   /* Focus-within for container focus */
   .arbeitszeitcheck-form-group:focus-within {
     outline: 2px solid var(--color-primary);
     outline-offset: 2px;
   }
   ```
