4. [ ] **Implement keyboard navigation JavaScript**
   
   **Create `js/keyboard-navigation.js`:**
   ```javascript
   /**
    * ArbeitszeitCheck Keyboard Navigation
    * 
    * Implements keyboard shortcuts and navigation:
    * - Arrow keys for menu navigation
    * - Enter/Space to activate links
    * - Escape to close mobile menu
    * - Tab trap in modals
    */
   
   (function() {
     'use strict';
     
     const navigation = {
       init: function() {
         this.setupArrowKeyNavigation();
         this.setupEscapeKey();
         this.setupModalFocusTrap();
       },
       
       setupArrowKeyNavigation: function() {
         const menu = document.querySelector('.arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__menu');
         if (!menu) return;
         
         const menuItems = Array.from(menu.querySelectorAll('.arbeitszeitcheck-navigation__link'));
         
         menu.addEventListener('keydown', function(e) {
           const currentIndex = menuItems.indexOf(document.activeElement);
           
           if (e.key === 'ArrowDown') {
             e.preventDefault();
             const nextIndex = (currentIndex + 1) % menuItems.length;
             menuItems[nextIndex].focus();
           } else if (e.key === 'ArrowUp') {
             e.preventDefault();
             const prevIndex = currentIndex <= 0 ? menuItems.length - 1 : currentIndex - 1;
             menuItems[prevIndex].focus();
           } else if (e.key === 'Home') {
             e.preventDefault();
             menuItems[0].focus();
           } else if (e.key === 'End') {
             e.preventDefault();
             menuItems[menuItems.length - 1].focus();
           }
         });
       },
       
       setupEscapeKey: function() {
         document.addEventListener('keydown', function(e) {
           if (e.key === 'Escape') {
             // Close mobile menu if open
             const nav = document.querySelector('.arbeitszeitcheck-navigation');
             if (nav && nav.classList.contains('arbeitszeitcheck-navigation--mobile-open')) {
               nav.classList.remove('arbeitszeitcheck-navigation--mobile-open');
               // Return focus to menu button
               const menuButton = document.querySelector('.arbeitszeitcheck-mobile-menu-button');
               if (menuButton) {
                 menuButton.focus();
               }
             }
             
             // Close modals if open
             const openModal = document.querySelector('[role="dialog"][aria-hidden="false"]');
             if (openModal) {
               const closeButton = openModal.querySelector('[aria-label*="Close"]');
               if (closeButton) {
                 closeButton.click();
               }
             }
           }
         });
       },
       
       setupModalFocusTrap: function() {
         // Focus trap for modals
         document.addEventListener('keydown', function(e) {
           const modal = document.querySelector('[role="dialog"][aria-hidden="false"]');
           if (!modal || e.key !== 'Tab') return;
           
           const focusableElements = modal.querySelectorAll(
             'button, [href], input, select, textarea, [tabindex]:not([tabindex="-1"])'
           );
           
           if (focusableElements.length === 0) return;
           
           const firstElement = focusableElements[0];
           const lastElement = focusableElements[focusableElements.length - 1];
           
           if (e.shiftKey) {
             if (document.activeElement === firstElement) {
               e.preventDefault();
               lastElement.focus();
             }
           } else {
             if (document.activeElement === lastElement) {
               e.preventDefault();
               firstElement.focus();
             }
           }
         });
       }
     };
     
     // Initialize when DOM is ready
     if (document.readyState === 'loading') {
       document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
         navigation.init();
       });
     } else {
       navigation.init();
     }
   })();
   ```
   
   **Register script in `lib/Controller/PageController.php`:**
   ```php
   \OCP\Util::addScript('arbeitszeitcheck', 'keyboard-navigation');
   ```

### Phase 6: Extreme Usability & Simplicity (Granny-Proof Design)

**Status:** [ ] Not Started | [ ] In Progress | [ ] Complete  
**Prerequisites:** Phase 5.5 Complete  
**Estimated Time:** 10-12 hours

**CRITICAL OBJECTIVE:** Make the app so simple and intuitive that a 99-year-old who has never touched a computer can use it. This applies to ALL interfaces: employee, manager, admin, and HR. Every action must be self-explanatory, every error must be helpful, and every workflow must be obvious.

**Design Principles:**
1. **Zero Learning Curve**: Users should understand how to use it immediately
2. **Self-Explanatory**: Every button, field, and action should be clear
3. **Forgiving**: Mistakes should be easy to undo, errors should be helpful
4. **Progressive Disclosure**: Show only what's needed, when it's needed
5. **Clear Visual Hierarchy**: Important things are obvious
6. **Consistent Patterns**: Same actions work the same way everywhere
7. **Help Always Available**: Contextual help, tooltips, examples everywhere
8. **Plain Language**: No technical jargon, use everyday words

#### Task 6.1: Simplify All Labels and Text (Plain Language)

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] All labels use plain, everyday language (no technical jargon)
- [ ] All button labels clearly describe what will happen
- [ ] All form field labels are self-explanatory
- [ ] All error messages explain what went wrong AND how to fix it
- [ ] All help text uses simple examples
- [ ] All navigation items have clear, descriptive names
- [ ] All page titles clearly describe the page content
- [ ] No abbreviations unless universally understood
- [ ] No technical terms without explanation
- [ ] All text tested with non-technical users (or reviewed for simplicity)
- [ ] Text is clear for 99-year-old non-computer-user level

**Examples of WRONG (too technical):**
- "CRUD operations"
- "Submit form data"
- "Configure working time model parameters"
- "Invalid input format"
- "API endpoint error"

**Examples of CORRECT (simple and clear):**
- "Add, view, edit, or delete"
- "Save your time entry"
- "Set up working hours"
- "Please enter the time like this: 09:00"
- "Something went wrong. Please try again or contact support."

**Verification Steps:**
1. Review all labels in templates
2. Replace technical terms with plain language
3. Review all button labels
4. Ensure buttons say what they do: "Save Time Entry" not "Submit"
5. Review all error messages
6. Ensure errors explain the problem AND solution
7. Review all help text
8. Add examples to help text
9. Test with someone unfamiliar with the system (or self-review for simplicity)
10. Document all text changes

**Files to Modify:**
- All template files
- All translation files (`l10n/en.json`, `l10n/de.json`)

**Cannot check off until:** All text uses plain language, all labels are self-explanatory, all errors are helpful, and text is understandable by non-technical users.

---

#### Task 6.3: Create Helpful Error Messages

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] All error messages explain WHAT went wrong in plain language
- [ ] All error messages explain HOW to fix it
- [ ] All error messages include examples of correct input
- [ ] Error messages appear next to the field that has the error
- [ ] Error messages are visually distinct (color, icon)
- [ ] Error messages are accessible (ARIA labels)
- [ ] No technical error codes shown to users
- [ ] No stack traces shown to users
- [ ] All error messages are translated
- [ ] Error messages are tested - users can understand and fix issues

**Example Error Message Implementation:**
```php
<?php if (isset($errors['start_time'])): ?>
    <div class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-error" role="alert" aria-live="polite">
        <span class="arbeitszeitcheck-icon-error" aria-hidden="true">⚠️</span>
        <div>
            <strong><?php p($l->t('Time format is incorrect')); ?></strong>
            <p><?php p($l->t('Please enter the time in this format: HH:MM (hours:minutes). For example: 09:00 for 9 in the morning, or 14:30 for 2:30 in the afternoon.')); ?></p>
        </div>
    </div>
<?php endif; ?>
```

**Verification Steps:**

#### Task 6.4: Simplify Forms and Input Fields

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Forms use clear, logical order (most important first)
- [ ] Required fields are clearly marked
- [ ] Field labels are above inputs (not beside)
- [ ] Input fields are large enough to click easily (44x44px minimum)
- [ ] Date/time inputs use native browser pickers where possible
- [ ] Dropdowns have clear options (no technical codes)
- [ ] Forms have clear section headers
- [ ] Forms show progress (step 1 of 3, etc.) if multi-step
- [ ] Forms have "Save" and "Cancel" buttons (not "Submit")
- [ ] Forms show confirmation before destructive actions
- [ ] Forms are tested - easy to fill out without instructions

**Example Simplified Form:**
```php
<form method="post" action="<?php p($urlGenerator->linkToRoute('arbeitszeitcheck.timeentry.create')); ?>" class="arbeitszeitcheck-form">
    <h2 class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-section-title">
        <?php p($l->t('When did you work?')); ?>
    </h2>
    
    <div class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-group">
        <label for="date" class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-label">
            <?php p($l->t('Date')); ?>
            <span class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-required">*</span>
        </label>
        <input type="date" 
               id="date" 
               name="date" 
               class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-input"
               value="<?php p(date('Y-m-d')); ?>"
               required
               aria-describedby="date-help">
        <p id="date-help" class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-help">
            <?php p($l->t('Select the day you worked. Click the calendar icon to pick a date.')); ?>
        </p>
    </div>
    
    <div class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-group">
        <label for="start-time" class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-label">
            <?php p($l->t('Start Time')); ?>
            <span class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-required">*</span>
        </label>
        <input type="time" 
               id="start-time" 
               name="start_time" 
               class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-input"
               required
               aria-describedby="start-time-help">
        <p id="start-time-help" class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-help">
            <?php p($l->t('What time did you start working? Example: 09:00 (9 in the morning) or 14:30 (2:30 in the afternoon).')); ?>
        </p>
    </div>
    
    <div class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-actions">
        <button type="submit" class="arbeitszeitcheck-btn arbeitszeitcheck-btn--primary">
            <?php p($l->t('Save Time Entry')); ?>
        </button>
        <a href="<?php p($urlGenerator->linkToRoute('arbeitszeitcheck.timeentries.index')); ?>" class="arbeitszeitcheck-btn arbeitszeitcheck-btn--secondary">
            <?php p($l->t('Cancel')); ?>
        </a>
    </div>
</form>
```

**Verification Steps:**
1. Review all forms
2. Ensure logical order
3. Mark required fields clearly
4. Ensure labels above inputs
5. Check input sizes (touch-friendly)
6. Use native date/time pickers
7. Simplify dropdown options
8. Add section headers
8. Add progress indicators if multi-step
9. Use clear button labels
10. Add confirmations for destructive actions
11. Test forms - should be fillable without instructions

**Cannot check off until:** All forms are simple, logical, clearly labeled, touch-friendly, and easy to use without instructions.

```php
                        <?php p($user->getDisplayName()); ?>
                    </option>
                <?php endforeach; ?>
            </select>
            <p class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-help">
                <?php p($l->t('Choose the employee you want to add to time tracking. Only employees who are not yet added will appear in this list.')); ?>
            </p>
        </div>
        
        <!-- More fields with help text -->
        
        <div class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-actions">
            <button type="submit" class="arbeitszeitcheck-btn arbeitszeitcheck-btn--primary">
                <?php p($l->t('Add Employee')); ?>
            </button>
            <a href="<?php p($urlGenerator->linkToRoute('arbeitszeitcheck.admin.users')); ?>" class="arbeitszeitcheck-btn arbeitszeitcheck-btn--secondary">
                <?php p($l->t('Cancel')); ?>
            </a>
        </div>

</div>
```

```php
</button>
```

**Phase 6 Quality Gate Checklist:**

Before marking Phase 6 as complete, verify ALL of the following:

- [ ] All labels use plain language (no technical jargon)
- [ ] All buttons clearly describe actions
- [ ] All form fields have help text with examples
- [ ] All error messages explain problems and solutions
- [ ] All forms are simple and logical
- [ ] Admin/HR/manager interfaces are as simple as employee interfaces
- [ ] All empty states have clear instructions
- [ ] All success messages are clear
- [ ] All confirmations are understandable
- [ ] Navigation is clear and logical
- [ ] First-time users see helpful onboarding
- [ ] Help is easily accessible everywhere
- [ ] Tested with non-technical users (or self-reviewed for extreme simplicity)
- [ ] App is usable by 99-year-old non-computer-user level
- [ ] Manual usability testing completed and documented

**Phase 6 cannot be marked complete until ALL items above are checked.**

**Usability Test Criteria:**
- Can a non-technical user complete common tasks without instructions?
- Are all labels and buttons self-explanatory?
- Can users recover from errors easily?
- Is help available when needed?
- Are admin/HR tasks as simple as employee tasks?

   ```php

       </label>

              id="start-time"

              class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-input"
              value="<?php p($startTime ?? ''); ?>"
              required

              aria-invalid="<?php echo isset($errors['start_time']) ? 'true' : 'false'; ?>">
       
       <p id="start-time-help" class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-help">

              class="arbeitszeitcheck-form-error"

               <span class="arbeitszeitcheck-icon-error" aria-hidden="true">⚠️</span>
   ```

- [ ] All form validation errors are clear and actionable

- [ ] Loading states show skeleton screens or spinners with text
- [ ] Error messages explain what happened and how to fix it
- [ ] Onboarding tour works correctly
- [ ] Contextual help tips visible throughout app

- [ ] **Zero CORS errors**

**Manual Testing:**

### Phase 7: Translations
**Status:** [ ] Not Started | [ ] In Progress | [ ] Complete
**Estimated Time:** 2-3 hours
**Prerequisites:** Phase 6 Complete

**Objective:** Ensure all text is properly translated in German and English, with proper pluralization and context.

**Tasks:**

1. [ ] **Audit all text in the application**
   
   **Search for untranslated strings:**
   ```bash
   # Search for hardcoded English text in templates
   grep -rn '"[A-Z][a-zA-Z ]*"' templates/ | grep -v '<?php'
   
   # Search for hardcoded text in JavaScript files
   grep -rn '"[A-Z][a-zA-Z ]*"' js/ | grep -v 't(' | grep -v '//' Copied from projectcheck - NEVER DO THIS */
.projectcheck-navigation {
  background: var(--color-main-background);
}
```

**Example of CORRECT:**
```css
/* Adapted pattern with proper naming */
.arbeitszeitcheck-navigation {
  background: var(--color-main-background);
}
```

#### 5. NO Style Leakage
- ❌ CSS must be scoped to arbeitszeitcheck only
- ❌ No global styles that affect other apps
- ❌ No generic class names without prefix
- ✅ Use app-specific prefixes for all classes
- ✅ Test with other apps active to verify no conflicts

**Example of WRONG:**
```css
/* Too generic - will affect all apps */
.navigation { }
.header { }
.button { }
```

**Example of CORRECT:**
```css
/* Properly scoped with prefix */
.arbeitszeitcheck-navigation { }
.arbeitszeitcheck-header { }
.arbeitszeitcheck-button { }
```

#### 6. NO CSP or CORS Errors
- ❌ Zero Content Security Policy (CSP) violations allowed
- ❌ Zero Cross-Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) errors allowed
- ✅ All inline scripts must use nonce: `nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>"`
- ✅ All inline styles must use nonce: `nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>"`
- ✅ All external resources must be from allowed origins
- ✅ All API calls must be same-origin or properly configured
- ✅ Check browser console for CSP/CORS violations after every change

**Example of WRONG:**
```php
<!-- No nonce - CSP violation -->
<script>
  document.getElementById('btn').addEventListener('click', doSomething);
</script>

<!-- Inline event handler - CSP violation -->
<button onclick="doSomething()">Click</button>
```

**Example of CORRECT:**
```php
<!-- Proper nonce for inline script -->
<script nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">
  document.getElementById('btn').addEventListener('click', doSomething);
</script>

<!-- Better: External script file -->
<button id="btn">Click</button>
```

#### 7. NO Untranslated Text
- ❌ No hard-coded English text in templates or components
- ❌ No "will translate later"
- ✅ All visible text must use translation functions
- ✅ Server-side: `$l->t('key')`
- ✅ Client-side: `t('arbeitszeitcheck', 'key')`
- ✅ Add translation keys immediately when adding text

**Example of WRONG:**
```php
<h1>Time Tracking Dashboard</h1>
```

**Example of CORRECT:**
```php
<h1><?php p($l->t('Time Tracking Dashboard')); ?></h1>
```

**Rule:** All CSS classes MUST use `arbeitszeitcheck-*` prefix.

## 🎯 BULLETPROOF PHASE-BY-PHASE CHECKLISTS

**CRITICAL RULE:** A task can ONLY be checked off when ALL completion criteria are met. No exceptions. No workarounds. No placeholders. No mocks. Production-ready code only.

---

## 📋 STANDARD "DEFINITION OF DONE" TEMPLATE

**Every task in this document MUST meet this standard before being marked complete. This is non-negotiable.**

### Universal Definition of Done (Applies to ALL Tasks)

**A task is ONLY "Done" when ALL of the following are true:**

#### 1. Code Quality
- [ ] **No TODOs, FIXMEs, or placeholders** - Code is complete, not "will implement later"
- [ ] **No mock/fake data** - All features work with real database data
- [ ] **No commented-out code** - Either code is active or removed (unless necessary comments)
- [ ] **No console.log statements** - Removed or replaced with proper logging
- [ ] **No hardcoded values** - Uses configuration, translation functions, or CSS variables
- [ ] **Proper error handling** - All operations wrapped in try-catch, errors logged
- [ ] **Type safety** - PHP strict types enabled, type hints on all functions
- [ ] **Code follows standards** - PSR-12, Nextcloud conventions, projectcheck patterns

#### 2. Functionality
- [ ] **Feature works end-to-end** - Complete workflow from user action to database to display
- [ ] **Works with real data** - Tested with actual database records, not test data
- [ ] **All edge cases handled** - Boundary conditions, error cases, unusual scenarios
- [ ] **No regressions** - Existing features still work after changes
- [ ] **All user roles work** - Employee, Manager, Admin (if applicable)

#### 3. Security
- [ ] **Input validated server-side** - All user input validated in PHP, not just JavaScript
- [ ] **Output escaped** - All output uses `p()` or `print_unescaped()` appropriately
- [ ] **SQL injection prevented** - All queries use parameterized statements
- [ ] **XSS prevented** - All user input escaped before output
- [ ] **CSRF protected** - All state-changing operations have CSRF tokens
- [ ] **Permission checks** - Controller and service level permission verification
- [ ] **CSP compliant** - All inline scripts/styles use nonce
- [ ] **No CORS errors** - All API calls same-origin

#### 4. Testing
- [ ] **Manually tested** - Actually used the feature, clicked buttons, filled forms
- [ ] **Tested in browser** - Chrome, Firefox, Safari, Edge (at minimum Chrome)
- [ ] **Tested with real data** - Not just empty database, but with actual records
- [ ] **Tested all user roles** - Employee, Manager, Admin (if applicable)
- [ ] **Tested error cases** - What happens when things go wrong?
- [ ] **Tested edge cases** - Boundary conditions, unusual inputs
- [ ] **No console errors** - Browser console shows zero errors
- [ ] **No PHP errors** - PHP error log shows zero errors
- [ ] **Zero CSP violations** - Browser console shows zero CSP violations
- [ ] **Zero CORS errors** - Browser network tab shows zero CORS errors

#### 5. Translations
- [ ] **All text translated** - No hardcoded English strings
- [ ] **Translation keys added** - All new text has keys in `l10n/en.json` and `l10n/de.json`
- [ ] **Tested in German** - Switched Nextcloud to German, verified all text is German
- [ ] **Tested in English** - Switched Nextcloud to English, verified all text is English
- [ ] **Pluralization works** - Used `$l->n()` or `n()` for plural forms

#### 6. Theming
- [ ] **Works in light theme** - Tested with Nextcloud light theme
- [ ] **Works in dark theme** - Tested with Nextcloud dark theme
- [ ] **Uses CSS variables** - No hardcoded colors, uses `var(--color-...)`
- [ ] **No visual issues** - Colors readable, contrast sufficient, no layout breaks

#### 7. Responsive Design
- [ ] **Works on desktop** - Tested at 1920px, 1280px, 1024px widths
- [ ] **Works on tablet** - Tested at 768px width
- [ ] **Works on mobile** - Tested at 375px, 414px widths
- [ ] **Touch-friendly** - Buttons/links at least 44x44px on mobile
- [ ] **No horizontal scroll** - Content fits within viewport

#### 8. Accessibility
- [ ] **Keyboard navigation** - Can use feature with only keyboard (Tab, Enter, Space, Arrow keys)
- [ ] **Focus indicators** - Visible focus outline on all interactive elements
- [ ] **ARIA labels** - All interactive elements have proper ARIA attributes
- [ ] **Screen reader tested** - Tested with NVDA, JAWS, or VoiceOver (at minimum one)
- [ ] **Color contrast** - Text meets WCAG AAA (7:1 for normal text, 4.5:1 for large text)

#### 9. Performance
- [ ] **Page loads quickly** - Loads in < 3 seconds on average connection
- [ ] **No N+1 queries** - Database queries optimized, no unnecessary queries
- [ ] **No performance warnings** - Browser performance tab shows no issues

#### 10. Documentation
- [ ] **Code documented** - PHPDoc for PHP classes/methods, JSDoc for JavaScript functions
- [ ] **Complex logic explained** - Inline comments for non-obvious code
- [ ] **Business rules documented** - Why certain validations or calculations exist

#### 11. Integration
- [ ] **Works with other apps** - Tested with projectcheck installed (no conflicts)
- [ ] **No CSS conflicts** - Styles don't affect other Nextcloud apps
- [ ] **No JavaScript conflicts** - JavaScript doesn't interfere with other apps

#### 12. Nextcloud Best Practices
- [ ] **Uses Nextcloud APIs** - `IUserSession`, `IDBConnection`, `IConfig`, etc. (not direct access)
- [ ] **Proper dependency injection** - Services injected via constructor
- [ ] **CSPTrait used** - All controllers use CSPTrait and call `configureCSP()`
- [ ] **Routes registered** - All routes in `appinfo/routes.php`
- [ ] **Services registered** - All services in `Application::register()`
- [ ] **CSS/JS loaded correctly** - Using `Util::addStyle()` and `Util::addScript()` in `boot()`

---

### Task-Specific Definition of Done

**In addition to the Universal Definition of Done above, each task has specific completion criteria listed in its "Completion Criteria (ALL must be met)" section.**

**Example of a well-defined task:**

```
#### Task X.Y: Create Dashboard Template

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Template file exists: `templates/dashboard.php`
- [ ] Template extends common layout: `<?php include 'common/layout.php'; ?>`
- [ ] Template displays real data from controller (not hardcoded)
- [ ] All text uses translation functions: `<?php p($l->t('Dashboard')); ?>`
- [ ] All CSS uses variables: `var(--color-main-background)`
- [ ] Template tested - renders without errors
- [ ] Dashboard shows actual time entries from database
- [ ] Dashboard shows actual statistics (not "0" or "N/A")
- [ ] No PHP errors in error log
- [ ] No console errors in browser
- [ ] Works in light theme
- [ ] Works in dark theme
- [ ] Responsive on mobile
- [ ] Keyboard navigable
- [ ] Screen reader tested

**Verification Steps:**
1. Open `templates/dashboard.php` - file exists
2. Check template includes common layout
3. Load page in browser - verify renders
4. Check browser console - zero errors
5. Check PHP error log - zero errors
6. Test in light theme - works
7. Test in dark theme - works
8. Test on mobile - responsive
9. Test with keyboard - navigable
10. Test with screen reader - accessible

**Files to Create:**
- `templates/dashboard.php`

**Files to Modify:**
- `lib/Controller/PageController.php` (add dashboard method)

**Cannot check off until:** Template exists, displays real data, uses translations, works in both themes, responsive, accessible, and passes all verification steps.
```

**Key Elements of Good Completion Criteria:**
1. **Specific and measurable** - "Template file exists" not "Template created"
2. **Verifiable** - Can be checked with a command or inspection
3. **Testable** - Can be tested manually or automatically
4. **Complete** - Covers all aspects (functionality, security, testing, etc.)
5. **No ambiguity** - Clear what "done" means

---

### ✅ Completion Criteria Standard

**Before checking ANY task as complete, verify:**
- [ ] Code is production-ready (no TODOs, FIXMEs, placeholders)
- [ ] All functionality works with REAL data (no mocks, no fake data)
- [ ] Zero console errors (JavaScript, CSP, CORS)
- [ ] Zero PHP errors or warnings
- [ ] Manual testing completed and documented
- [ ] All translations implemented (no hardcoded English)
- [ ] Works in light AND dark themes
- [ ] Responsive design works on mobile AND desktop
- [ ] Accessibility requirements met (keyboard navigation, screen readers)
- [ ] Code follows projectcheck patterns and conventions
- [ ] All files use proper naming conventions (`arbeitszeitcheck-*` prefix)
- [ ] Git status is clean (no uncommitted work unless intentionally staged)

### Phase 0.5: CSP & CORS Compliance - Nextcloud Best Practices

**Status:** [ ] Not Started | [ ] In Progress | [ ] Complete  
**Prerequisites:** Phase 0 Complete  
**Estimated Time:** 3-4 hours  
**CRITICAL:** This phase is MANDATORY for Nextcloud Store approval. CSP/CORS violations will BLOCK store submission.

**Objective:** Implement comprehensive Content Security Policy (CSP) and Cross-Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) compliance following Nextcloud best practices. Zero violations allowed.

---

#### Task 0.5.1: Understand CSP & CORS Requirements

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Understand what CSP is and why it's required
- [ ] Understand what CORS is and why it's required
- [ ] Understand Nextcloud's CSP nonce system
- [ ] Understand Nextcloud's CORS requirements
- [ ] Know how to check for CSP violations in browser console
- [ ] Know how to check for CORS errors in browser network tab
- [ ] Understand that CSP/CORS violations BLOCK store approval

**What is CSP (Content Security Policy)?**
- CSP is a security feature that prevents XSS attacks by controlling which resources can be loaded and executed
- Nextcloud enforces strict CSP policies
- **ALL inline scripts MUST use a nonce** (a random token generated by Nextcloud)
- **ALL inline styles MUST use a nonce**
- **NO inline event handlers** (e.g., `onclick="..."`) allowed
- **NO `javascript:` URLs** allowed
- **NO `eval()` or similar dynamic code execution** allowed

**What is CORS (Cross-Origin Resource Sharing)?**
- CORS controls which origins can make requests to your API
- Nextcloud apps should use **same-origin API calls only**
- **NO cross-origin requests** unless absolutely necessary and properly configured
- All API calls should go to the same domain as the app

**Why This Matters:**
- **CSP/CORS violations will BLOCK Nextcloud Store approval**
- Violations indicate security vulnerabilities
- Violations can break functionality in production
- Nextcloud's security team will reject apps with violations

**Cannot check off until:** You fully understand CSP and CORS requirements and their importance.

---

#### Task 0.5.2: Implement CSP Service (Following projectcheck Pattern)

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Created `lib/Service/CSPService.php` following projectcheck pattern
- [ ] Service implements proper CSP policy configuration
- [ ] Service provides method to get CSP nonce
- [ ] Service provides method to apply CSP to TemplateResponse
- [ ] Service uses Nextcloud's ContentSecurityPolicy class
- [ ] Service uses Nextcloud's ContentSecurityPolicyNonceManager
- [ ] Service tested and working

**Step-by-Step Implementation:**

1. **Create CSP Service:**

```php
<?php

declare(strict_types=1);

namespace OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Service;

use OCP\AppFramework\Http\ContentSecurityPolicy;
use OCP\AppFramework\Http\TemplateResponse;

/**
 * Centralized CSP policy management for ArbeitszeitCheck
 * 
 * Following Nextcloud best practices:
 * - All resources from 'self' only (no external CDNs)
 * - Proper nonce management for inline scripts/styles
 * - Strict policy to prevent XSS attacks
 */
class CSPService
{
    /**
     * Base policy shared by all contexts (no external CDNs)
     * 
     * Nextcloud best practice: Only allow resources from 'self'
     * This prevents loading external resources that could be compromised
     */
    public function getDefaultPolicy(): ContentSecurityPolicy
    {
        $policy = new ContentSecurityPolicy();

        // Scripts, styles, images, fonts, media, and connections from self only
        $policy->addAllowedScriptDomain("'self'");
        $policy->addAllowedStyleDomain("'self'");
        $policy->addAllowedImageDomain("'self'");
        $policy->addAllowedFontDomain("'self'");
        $policy->addAllowedMediaDomain("'self'");
        $policy->addAllowedConnectDomain("'self'");

        // Allow data/blob where commonly needed (for images, fonts, media)
        $policy->addAllowedImageDomain('data:');
        $policy->addAllowedImageDomain('blob:');
        $policy->addAllowedFontDomain('data:');
        $policy->addAllowedMediaDomain('blob:');

        // Clickjacking protection (allow framing by self only)
        $policy->addAllowedFrameAncestorDomain("'self'");

        return $policy;
    }

    /**
     * Get CSP policy for main app pages
     */
    public function getMainAppPolicy(): ContentSecurityPolicy
    {
        return $this->getDefaultPolicy();
    }

    /**
     * Get CSP policy for modal dialogs
     */
    public function getModalPolicy(): ContentSecurityPolicy
    {
        return $this->getDefaultPolicy();
    }

    /**
     * Get CSP policy for guest/public pages (if applicable)
     */
    public function getGuestPolicy(): ContentSecurityPolicy
    {
        return $this->getDefaultPolicy();
    }

    /**
     * Apply CSP and inject a template nonce parameter.
     * 
     * This method:
     * 1. Gets the CSP nonce from Nextcloud's nonce manager
     * 2. Adds it to template parameters as 'cspNonce'
     * 3. Sets the CSP policy on the response
     * 
     * Templates can then use: nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>"
     * 
     * @param TemplateResponse $response The template response
     * @param string $context Context: 'main', 'modal', or 'guest'
     * @return TemplateResponse Response with CSP configured
     */
    public function applyPolicyWithNonce(TemplateResponse $response, string $context = 'main'): TemplateResponse
    {
        // Get appropriate policy for context
        switch ($context) {
            case 'modal':
                $policy = $this->getModalPolicy();
                break;
            case 'guest':
                $policy = $this->getGuestPolicy();
                break;
            case 'main':
            default:
                $policy = $this->getMainAppPolicy();
                break;
        }

        // Expose nonce to templates that use inline tags
        // This is the CRITICAL part - templates MUST use this nonce
        $params = $response->getParams();
        $params['cspNonce'] = \OC::$server->getContentSecurityPolicyNonceManager()->getNonce();
        $response->setParams($params);

        // Set the CSP policy on the response
        $response->setContentSecurityPolicy($policy);
        
        return $response;
    }
}
```

2. **Create CSP Trait for Controllers:**

```php
<?php

/**
 * CSP Trait for arbeitszeitcheck app
 *
 * @copyright Copyright (c) 2024, Nextcloud GmbH
 * @license AGPL-3.0-or-later
 */

namespace OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Controller;

use OCP\AppFramework\Http\TemplateResponse;
use OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Service\CSPService;

/**
 * Trait for configuring Content Security Policy
 * 
 * Usage in controllers:
 * 
 * class MyController extends Controller {
 *     use CSPTrait;
 *     
 *     public function __construct(...) {
 *         // Inject CSPService
 *         $this->setCspService($cspService);
 *     }
 *     
 *     public function index(): TemplateResponse {
 *         $response = new TemplateResponse(...);
 *         return $this->configureCSP($response, 'main');
 *     }
 * }
 */
trait CSPTrait
{
    /** @var CSPService */
    private ?CSPService $cspService = null;

    /**
     * Provide CSP service to classes using this trait
     */
    public function setCspService(CSPService $cspService): void
    {
        $this->cspService = $cspService;
    }

    /**
     * Configure CSP for template responses via centralized service.
     * Defaults to 'main' context when not specified by caller.
     * 
     * @param TemplateResponse $response The template response
     * @param string $context Context: 'main', 'modal', or 'guest'
     * @return TemplateResponse Response with CSP configured
     */
    protected function configureCSP(TemplateResponse $response, string $context = 'main'): TemplateResponse
    {
        if (!isset($this->cspService)) {
            // If service isn't injected, return response unchanged to avoid fatal errors
            // But log a warning - CSP should always be configured
            \OC::$server->getLogger()->warning(
                'CSP not configured for template response',
                ['app' => 'arbeitszeitcheck']
            );
            return $response;
        }
        return $this->cspService->applyPolicyWithNonce($response, $context);
    }
}
```

3. **Register CSP Service in Application.php:**

```php
// In lib/AppInfo/Application.php

use OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Service\CSPService;

public function register(IRegistrationContext $context): void {
    // ... existing registrations ...
    
    // Register CSP service
    $context->registerService(CSPService::class, function($c) {
        return new CSPService();
    });
}
```

**Verification Steps:**
1. Create `lib/Service/CSPService.php` with code above
2. Create `lib/Controller/CSPTrait.php` with code above
3. Register service in `Application.php`
4. Verify no syntax errors: `php -l lib/Service/CSPService.php`
5. Verify no syntax errors: `php -l lib/Controller/CSPTrait.php`

**Files to Create:**
- `lib/Service/CSPService.php`
- `lib/Controller/CSPTrait.php`

**Files to Modify:**
- `lib/AppInfo/Application.php` (register service)

**Cannot check off until:** CSP service created, trait created, service registered, and no syntax errors.

#### Task 0.5.3: Use CSP Nonce in All Templates

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] ALL controllers use CSPTrait
- [ ] ALL controllers call `configureCSP()` on TemplateResponse
- [ ] ALL inline `<script>` tags use nonce attribute
- [ ] ALL inline `<style>` tags use nonce attribute
- [ ] NO inline event handlers (onclick, onchange, etc.)
- [ ] NO `javascript:` URLs
- [ ] NO `eval()` or similar dynamic code execution
- [ ] All templates tested for CSP compliance

**Step-by-Step Implementation:**

1. **Update ALL Controllers to Use CSP:**

```php
// Example: lib/Controller/PageController.php

use OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Controller\CSPTrait;
use OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Service\CSPService;

class PageController extends Controller {
    use CSPTrait;
    
    public function __construct(
        $appName,
        IRequest $request,
        CSPService $cspService,
        // ... other dependencies
    ) {
        parent::__construct($appName, $request);
        $this->setCspService($cspService);
        // ... other initialization
    }
    
    public function index(): TemplateResponse {
        $response = new TemplateResponse(
            $this->appName,
            'index',
            [
                'pageTitle' => $l->t('Dashboard'),
                // ... other params
            ]
        );
        
        // CRITICAL: Configure CSP before returning
        return $this->configureCSP($response, 'main');
    }
}
```

2. **Use Nonce in ALL Inline Scripts:**

```php
<!-- WRONG - No nonce, will cause CSP violation -->
<script>
    document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
        console.log('This will be blocked by CSP!');
    });
</script>

<!-- CORRECT - With nonce -->
<script nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">
    document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
        console.log('This will work!');
    });
</script>

<!-- EVEN BETTER - External script file (no nonce needed) -->
<script src="<?php print_unescaped(link_to('arbeitszeitcheck', 'js/common/utils.js')); ?>"></script>
```

3. **Use Nonce in ALL Inline Styles:**

```php
<!-- WRONG - No nonce, will cause CSP violation -->
<style>
    .my-class { color: red; }
</style>

<!-- CORRECT - With nonce -->
<style nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">
    .my-class { color: red; }
</style>

<!-- EVEN BETTER - External CSS file (no nonce needed) -->
<link rel="stylesheet" href="<?php print_unescaped(link_to('arbeitszeitcheck', 'css/common/base.css')); ?>">
```

4. **NEVER Use Inline Event Handlers:**

```php
<!-- WRONG - Inline event handler, will cause CSP violation -->
<button onclick="doSomething()">Click</button>
<a href="javascript:void(0)" onclick="doSomething()">Link</a>

<!-- CORRECT - Use addEventListener in external script or nonce script -->
<button id="my-button">Click</button>
<script nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">
    document.getElementById('my-button').addEventListener('click', doSomething);
</script>

<!-- EVEN BETTER - External script file -->
<button id="my-button">Click</button>
<script src="<?php print_unescaped(link_to('arbeitszeitcheck', 'js/common/components.js')); ?>"></script>
```

5. **NEVER Use eval() or Similar:**

```javascript
// WRONG - eval() is blocked by CSP
eval('console.log("This will be blocked!");');

// WRONG - Function constructor is blocked by CSP
new Function('console.log("This will be blocked!");')();

// WRONG - setTimeout/setInterval with string is blocked
setTimeout('console.log("This will be blocked!");', 1000);

// CORRECT - Use functions directly
setTimeout(function() {
    console.log('This will work!');
}, 1000);
```

**Verification Steps:**
1. Update ALL controllers to use CSPTrait
2. Update ALL controllers to call configureCSP()
3. Search for all `<script>` tags: `grep -r "<script" templates/`
4. Verify ALL have nonce attribute
5. Search for all `<style>` tags: `grep -r "<style" templates/`
6. Verify ALL have nonce attribute
7. Search for inline event handlers: `grep -r "onclick\|onchange\|onsubmit\|onload" templates/`
8. Remove ALL inline event handlers
9. Search for eval: `grep -r "eval\|Function\|setTimeout.*['\"]" js/ templates/`
10. Remove ALL eval usage

**Files to Modify:**
- ALL controller files in `lib/Controller/`
- ALL template files in `templates/`
- ALL JavaScript files in `js/` (if they contain eval)

**Cannot check off until:** ALL controllers use CSP, ALL inline scripts/styles use nonce, NO inline event handlers, NO eval, and verified with grep.

#### Task 0.5.4: Ensure CORS Compliance (Same-Origin API Calls)

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] ALL API calls use same-origin URLs
- [ ] NO cross-origin requests (unless absolutely necessary and properly configured)
- [ ] ALL fetch/XMLHttpRequest calls use relative URLs or same-origin absolute URLs
- [ ] NO external API calls without proper CORS configuration
- [ ] All API calls tested for CORS compliance

**Step-by-Step Implementation:**

1. **Use Same-Origin API Calls:**

```javascript
// WRONG - Cross-origin request, will cause CORS error
fetch('https://api.example.com/data')
    .then(response => response.json())
    .then(data => console.log(data));

// WRONG - Hardcoded absolute URL (may cause CORS if different origin)
fetch('https://nextcloud.example.com/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api/time-entries')

// CORRECT - Relative URL (same-origin)
fetch('/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api/time-entries')
    .then(response => response.json())
    .then(data => console.log(data));

// CORRECT - Using Nextcloud's generateUrl (same-origin)
const url = OC.generateUrl('/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api/time-entries');
fetch(url)
    .then(response => response.json())
    .then(data => console.log(data));
```

2. **Use Nextcloud's API Helpers:**

```javascript
// CORRECT - Using Nextcloud's API (handles CORS automatically)
OC.API.request({
    url: '/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api/time-entries',
    method: 'GET',
    success: function(data) {
        console.log(data);
    },
    error: function(error) {
        console.error(error);
    }
});
```

3. **Verify All API Endpoints Are Same-Origin:**

```bash
# Search for all fetch/XMLHttpRequest calls
grep -r "fetch\|XMLHttpRequest\|\.ajax\|\.get\|\.post" js/ templates/

# Check each one:
# - Relative URLs (starting with /) are OK
# - Absolute URLs must be same-origin
# - External URLs (different domain) are NOT OK
```

**Verification Steps:**
1. Search for all API calls: `grep -r "fetch\|XMLHttpRequest\|\.ajax" js/ templates/`
2. Verify ALL use relative URLs or same-origin absolute URLs
3. Verify NO external API calls (different domain)
4. Test all API calls in browser network tab
5. Verify NO CORS errors in console

**Files to Review:**
- ALL JavaScript files in `js/`
- ALL template files in `templates/` (for inline scripts)

**Cannot check off until:** ALL API calls are same-origin, NO CORS errors, and verified with grep and browser testing.

#### Task 0.5.6: Common CSP/CORS Mistakes to Avoid

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Reviewed common mistakes list
- [ ] Verified none of these mistakes exist in codebase
- [ ] Fixed any mistakes found
- [ ] Documented any edge cases

**Common CSP Mistakes:**

1. **Inline Scripts Without Nonce:**
   ```php
   <!-- WRONG -->
   <script>console.log('test');</script>
   
   <!-- CORRECT -->
   <script nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">console.log('test');</script>
   ```

2. **Inline Styles Without Nonce:**
   ```php
   <!-- WRONG -->
   <style>.test { color: red; }</style>
   
   <!-- CORRECT -->
   <style nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">.test { color: red; }</style>
   ```

3. **Inline Event Handlers:**
   ```php
   <!-- WRONG -->
   <button onclick="doSomething()">Click</button>
   
   <!-- CORRECT -->
   <button id="my-button">Click</button>
   <script nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">
       document.getElementById('my-button').addEventListener('click', doSomething);
   </script>
   ```

4. **javascript: URLs:**
   ```php
   <!-- WRONG -->
   <a href="javascript:void(0)">Link</a>
   
   <!-- CORRECT -->
   <a href="#" id="my-link">Link</a>
   <script nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">
       document.getElementById('my-link').addEventListener('click', function(e) {
           e.preventDefault();
           doSomething();
       });
   </script>
   ```

5. **eval() or Similar:**
   ```javascript
   // WRONG
   eval('console.log("test");');
   new Function('console.log("test");')();
   setTimeout('console.log("test");', 1000);
   
   // CORRECT
   setTimeout(function() { console.log('test'); }, 1000);
   ```

6. **External Resources (CDNs):**
   ```php
   <!-- WRONG - External CDN -->
   <script src="https://cdn.example.com/library.js"></script>
   
   <!-- CORRECT - Local file -->
   <script src="<?php print_unescaped(link_to('arbeitszeitcheck', 'js/library.js')); ?>"></script>
   ```

**Common CORS Mistakes:**

1. **Cross-Origin API Calls:**
   ```javascript
   // WRONG - Different origin
   fetch('https://api.example.com/data')
   
   // CORRECT - Same origin
   fetch('/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api/data')
   ```

2. **Hardcoded Absolute URLs:**
   ```javascript
   // WRONG - May be different origin
   fetch('https://nextcloud.example.com/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api/data')
   
   // CORRECT - Relative URL
   fetch('/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/api/data')
   ```

3. **Missing CORS Headers (if cross-origin needed):**
   ```php
   // If you MUST make cross-origin requests (NOT RECOMMENDED):
   // You need to configure CORS headers on the server
   // But this should be AVOIDED - use same-origin instead
   ```

**Verification Steps:**
1. Review all code for common mistakes
2. Fix any mistakes found
3. Re-test CSP/CORS compliance
4. Document any edge cases

**Cannot check off until:** All common mistakes reviewed, none exist in codebase, and verified.

- [ ] NO eval() or similar
- [ ] NO javascript: URLs

- [ ] NO CORS errors

### Phase 4.5: Workflow Design & German Law Compliance

**Status:** [ ] Not Started | [ ] In Progress | [ ] Complete  
**Prerequisites:** Phase 4 Complete (can run parallel with Phase 5)  
**Estimated Time:** 8-10 hours

**CRITICAL OBJECTIVE:** Design all workflows to be logical, based on real-world usage, compliant with German labor law (Arbeitszeitgesetz - ArbZG), and follow common sense. Every workflow must be documented in detail before implementation.

---

## 📋 COMPREHENSIVE DEFINITION: WHAT "LEGALLY COMPLIANT" MEANS

**"Legally Compliant" means the system fully implements and enforces ALL requirements of German labor law (Arbeitszeitgesetz - ArbZG) and related EU directives, ensuring:**

### 1. Arbeitszeitgesetz (ArbZG) - German Working Time Act

**Core Requirements:**

**A. Maximum Working Hours:**
- **Daily maximum**: 8 hours per day (standard)
- **Daily extension**: Can be extended to 10 hours per day ONLY if:
  - The average over 6 months (or 24 weeks) does not exceed 8 hours per day
  - System MUST calculate rolling 6-month average
  - System MUST prevent exceeding 10 hours in any single day
  - System MUST warn when approaching 8-hour limit
  - System MUST warn when 6-month average approaches 8 hours
- **Weekly maximum**: 48 hours average over 6 months (or 24 weeks)
  - System MUST calculate rolling 6-month average
  - System MUST track weekly totals
  - System MUST prevent exceeding 48 hours average
- **Calculation method**: 
  - Rolling average: Last 6 months (or 24 weeks) of data
  - Must account for all working days (including part-time, flexible, etc.)
  - Must exclude absences (vacation, sick leave, etc.) from calculation

**B. Break Requirements (ArbZG §4):**
- **After 6 hours of work**: Minimum 30 minutes break required
  - Break can be split (e.g., 2x 15 minutes = 30 minutes total)
  - System MUST track cumulative break time per day
  - System MUST warn if break not taken after 6 hours
  - System MUST prevent clock-out if break requirement not met (or allow with clear warning)
- **After 9 hours of work**: Minimum 45 minutes break required
  - Break can be split (e.g., 2x 22.5 minutes or 3x 15 minutes = 45 minutes total)
  - System MUST track cumulative break time per day
  - System MUST warn if break not taken after 9 hours
  - System MUST prevent clock-out if break requirement not met (or allow with clear warning)
- **Break rules**:
  - Breaks must be at least 15 minutes to count
  - Breaks shorter than 15 minutes do NOT count toward requirement
  - System MUST validate break duration
  - System MUST allow multiple breaks (split breaks)

**C. Rest Period Requirements (ArbZG §5):**
- **Minimum rest period**: 11 consecutive hours between end of work and start of next work day
  - System MUST calculate time between end of last shift and start of next shift
  - System MUST prevent clock-in if rest period not met
  - System MUST show clear error: "You need at least 11 hours rest. Your last shift ended at [time]. You can clock in after [calculated time]."
  - System MUST handle cross-midnight shifts correctly
  - System MUST account for timezone changes (if applicable)

**D. Sunday and Holiday Work (ArbZG §9, §10):**
- **Sunday work**: Generally prohibited
  - System MUST detect Sunday work
  - System MUST require works council agreement flag (if configured)
  - System MUST warn when Sunday work detected
  - System MUST allow exceptions (with proper documentation)
  - System MUST track Sunday work hours separately
- **Holiday work**: Generally prohibited (public holidays)
  - System MUST integrate with holiday calendar (if available)
  - System MUST detect holiday work
  - System MUST require works council agreement flag (if configured)
  - System MUST warn when holiday work detected
  - System MUST allow exceptions (with proper documentation)
  - System MUST track holiday work hours separately

**E. Night Work (ArbZG §6):**
- **Night work definition**: Work between 11:00 PM and 6:00 AM
  - System MUST detect night work hours
  - System MUST track night work hours separately
  - System MUST apply special regulations (if configured):
    - Maximum 8 hours per night (can be extended to 10 with agreement)
    - Health check requirements (if applicable)
    - Additional break requirements (if applicable)
  - System MUST warn about night work requirements

**F. Record Keeping (EU Directive 2019/1152, ArbZG §16):**
- **Mandatory recording**: Employers MUST record working time
  - System MUST record all clock-in/clock-out times
  - System MUST record all break times
  - System MUST record all time entries (manual and automatic)
  - System MUST record all changes (audit trail)
- **Retention period**: Minimum 2 years (German law)
  - System MUST retain all records for at least 2 years
  - System MUST allow export of records
  - System MUST allow deletion only after retention period
- **Data integrity**: Records MUST be tamper-proof
  - System MUST log all changes (who, when, what, why)
  - System MUST prevent unauthorized modifications
  - System MUST maintain audit trail

### 2. GDPR Compliance (EU General Data Protection Regulation)

**Core Requirements:**
- **Right to access**: Employees can export all their data
- **Right to rectification**: Employees can request corrections
- **Right to erasure**: Employees can request deletion (after retention period)
- **Data minimization**: Only collect necessary data
- **Purpose limitation**: Use data only for stated purposes
- **Storage limitation**: Delete data after retention period
- **Security**: Protect data with appropriate measures
- **Transparency**: Clear privacy policy and data processing information

### 3. Works Council Agreement (Betriebsvereinbarung)

**If applicable (companies with works council):**
- System MUST support works council agreement flags
- System MUST document exceptions (Sunday work, extended hours, etc.)
- System MUST allow configuration of works council rules
- System MUST track works council approvals

### 4. Industry-Specific Regulations

**Some industries have additional requirements:**
- **Healthcare**: Additional break requirements, shift regulations
- **Transportation**: Driving time regulations, rest periods
- **Construction**: Safety regulations, weather-related restrictions
- **System MUST be extensible** to support industry-specific rules

---

## 📋 COMPREHENSIVE WORK TIME MODELS - ALL TYPES COVERED

**The system MUST support ALL types of work time models used in Germany. This includes:**

### Standard Work Time Models

**1. Full-Time (Vollzeit)**
- **Definition**: Standard full-time employment, typically 35-40 hours per week
- **Common variations**:
  - 35 hours/week (e.g., public sector)
  - 37.5 hours/week
  - 38.5 hours/week
  - 40 hours/week (most common)
- **Requirements**:
  - Fixed daily hours (e.g., 8 hours/day)
  - Fixed weekly hours (e.g., 40 hours/week)
  - Standard work days (typically Monday-Friday)
  - Standard work times (e.g., 9:00-17:00)
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Configurable weekly hours (35-40)
  - [ ] Configurable daily hours (7-8)
  - [ ] Standard work week (Mon-Fri)
  - [ ] Overtime calculation based on weekly hours
  - [ ] Vacation days calculation (typically 25-30 days/year)

**2. Part-Time (Teilzeit)**
- **Definition**: Reduced working hours compared to full-time
- **Common variations**:
  - 50% part-time (20 hours/week)
  - 75% part-time (30 hours/week)
  - 80% part-time (32 hours/week)
  - Custom hours (e.g., 15 hours/week, 25 hours/week)
- **Requirements**:
  - Reduced weekly hours
  - Reduced daily hours (proportional)
  - Vacation days proportional to full-time
  - Overtime calculation based on part-time hours
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Configurable weekly hours (any value < full-time)
  - [ ] Configurable daily hours (proportional)
  - [ ] Proportional vacation days calculation
  - [ ] Overtime calculation based on part-time hours
  - [ ] Support for irregular part-time (different hours per day)

**3. Flexible Working Hours (Gleitzeit)**
- **Definition**: Flexible start/end times within core hours
- **Common variations**:
  - Core hours: 10:00-15:00 (must be present)
  - Flexible hours: 6:00-10:00 and 15:00-20:00 (can choose)
  - Time account: Can accumulate hours (positive/negative balance)
- **Requirements**:
  - Core hours (must be present)
  - Flexible hours (can choose)
  - Time account tracking (overtime/undertime)
  - Time account limits (e.g., max +40 hours, min -20 hours)
  - Settlement period (e.g., monthly, quarterly)
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Configurable core hours
  - [ ] Configurable flexible hours
  - [ ] Time account tracking (positive/negative balance)
  - [ ] Time account limits
  - [ ] Settlement period configuration
  - [ ] Automatic settlement (if configured)

**4. Trust-Based Working Time (Vertrauensarbeitszeit)**
- **Definition**: Employee manages own time, no fixed hours
- **Common variations**:
  - Target hours per week (e.g., 40 hours)
  - Target hours per month (e.g., 160 hours)
  - No fixed hours (results-based)
- **Requirements**:
  - Target hours tracking
  - Self-reporting of hours
  - Manager approval of reported hours
  - Compliance with ArbZG still required (breaks, rest periods)
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Target hours configuration (weekly/monthly)
  - [ ] Self-reporting interface
  - [ ] Manager approval workflow
  - [ ] Compliance checks (breaks, rest periods)
  - [ ] Overtime/undertime calculation

**5. Shift Work (Schichtarbeit)**
- **Definition**: Work in shifts (morning, afternoon, night)
- **Common variations**:
  - 2-shift system (early/late)
  - 3-shift system (early/late/night)
  - 4-shift system (with rotating shifts)
  - Irregular shifts
- **Requirements**:
  - Shift schedule configuration
  - Shift rotation tracking
  - Night shift tracking (11 PM - 6 AM)
  - Shift-specific break rules
  - Rest period between shifts
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Shift schedule configuration
  - [ ] Shift assignment per user
  - [ ] Shift rotation tracking
  - [ ] Night shift detection and tracking
  - [ ] Shift-specific break rules
  - [ ] Rest period calculation between shifts

### Special Work Time Models

**6. Compressed Work Week (Verdichtete Arbeitswoche)**
- **Definition**: Full-time hours in fewer days (e.g., 40 hours in 4 days)
- **Common variations**:
  - 4-day week (10 hours/day)
  - 9-day fortnight (9 hours/day)
- **Requirements**:
  - Extended daily hours (up to 10 hours allowed if 6-month average is 8)
  - Fewer work days
  - Longer weekends
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Configurable work days per week (e.g., 4 days)
  - [ ] Extended daily hours (up to 10 hours)
  - [ ] 6-month average calculation
  - [ ] Compliance with ArbZG (breaks, rest periods)

**7. Annualized Hours (Jahresarbeitszeit)**
- **Definition**: Hours calculated over a year, not per week
- **Common variations**:
  - Fixed annual hours (e.g., 1,800 hours/year)
  - Variable annual hours (e.g., 1,600-2,000 hours/year)
- **Requirements**:
  - Annual hours target
  - Variable weekly hours (busy/quiet periods)
  - Time account tracking
  - Settlement at year-end
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Annual hours configuration
  - [ ] Variable weekly hours
  - [ ] Annual time account tracking
  - [ ] Year-end settlement
  - [ ] Progress tracking (hours worked vs. target)

**8. Job Sharing (Job-Sharing)**
- **Definition**: Two employees share one full-time position
- **Common variations**:
  - 50/50 split (each works 20 hours/week)
  - 60/40 split (one works 24, other 16 hours/week)
  - Alternating days/weeks
- **Requirements**:
  - Shared position tracking
  - Individual hours tracking
  - Combined hours = full-time equivalent
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Job sharing configuration
  - [ ] Shared position assignment
  - [ ] Individual hours tracking
  - [ ] Combined hours calculation

**9. Zero-Hours Contracts (Minijob, geringfügige Beschäftigung)**
- **Definition**: No fixed hours, work as needed
- **Common variations**:
  - Minijob (up to 520€/month, ~10-15 hours/week)
  - Midijob (520-1,600€/month, ~15-30 hours/week)
  - On-call work
- **Requirements**:
  - No fixed hours
  - Variable schedule
  - Hourly tracking
  - Monthly limits (if applicable)
- **System support**:
  - [ ] No fixed hours requirement
  - [ ] Variable schedule support
  - [ ] Hourly tracking
  - [ ] Monthly limits (if configured)
  - [ ] Compliance with ArbZG (breaks, rest periods still apply)

### Leave and Special Status Models

**10. Sabbatical (Sabbatjahr)**
- **Definition**: Extended unpaid leave (typically 3-12 months)
- **Common variations**:
  - Full sabbatical (no work during period)
  - Partial sabbatical (reduced hours)
  - Paid sabbatical (if employer offers)
- **Requirements**:
  - Extended absence period
  - No time tracking during sabbatical
  - Return date tracking
  - Possible return to previous work time model
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Sabbatical absence type
  - [ ] Extended absence period (3-12 months)
  - [ ] No time tracking during sabbatical
  - [ ] Return date tracking
  - [ ] Automatic reactivation after sabbatical
  - [ ] Return to previous work time model

**11. Parental Leave (Elternzeit)**
- **Definition**: Leave for parents (up to 3 years per child)
- **Common variations**:
  - Full parental leave (no work)
  - Part-time parental leave (reduced hours)
  - Flexible parental leave (variable schedule)
- **Requirements**:
  - Extended absence period (up to 3 years)
  - Possible part-time work during leave
  - Return to previous work time model
  - Protected status
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Parental leave absence type
  - [ ] Extended absence period (up to 3 years)
  - [ ] Part-time work during leave (if applicable)
  - [ ] Return date tracking
  - [ ] Automatic reactivation after leave
  - [ ] Return to previous work time model

**12. Sick Leave (Krankheit)**
- **Definition**: Absence due to illness
- **Common variations**:
  - Short-term sick leave (few days)
  - Long-term sick leave (weeks/months)
  - Partial sick leave (reduced hours)
- **Requirements**:
  - Sick leave tracking
  - Medical certificate requirement (after 3 days)
  - No time tracking during sick leave
  - Return to work tracking
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Sick leave absence type
  - [ ] Sick leave tracking
  - [ ] Medical certificate tracking (if applicable)
  - [ ] No time tracking during sick leave
  - [ ] Return to work date tracking

**13. Unpaid Leave (Unbezahlter Urlaub)**
- **Definition**: Extended unpaid absence
- **Common variations**:
  - Short unpaid leave (few days/weeks)
  - Long unpaid leave (months)
  - Educational leave
  - Personal leave
- **Requirements**:
  - Unpaid leave tracking
  - No time tracking during leave
  - Return to work tracking
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Unpaid leave absence type
  - [ ] Unpaid leave tracking
  - [ ] No time tracking during leave
  - [ ] Return to work date tracking

**14. Internship/Traineeship (Praktikum, Ausbildung)**
- **Definition**: Training period with reduced hours
- **Common variations**:
  - Full-time internship (40 hours/week)
  - Part-time internship (20-30 hours/week)
  - Apprenticeship (dual system, school + work)
- **Requirements**:
  - Reduced hours (if applicable)
  - Training period tracking
  - School days (if applicable)
  - Work days tracking
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Internship work time model
  - [ ] Configurable hours (full-time or part-time)
  - [ ] Training period tracking
  - [ ] School days exclusion (if applicable)
  - [ ] Work days tracking

**15. Student Worker (Werkstudent)**
- **Definition**: Student working part-time during studies
- **Common variations**:
  - 20 hours/week during semester
  - Full-time during semester break
  - Flexible schedule
- **Requirements**:
  - Variable hours (semester vs. break)
  - Student status tracking
  - Semester break full-time option
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Student worker work time model
  - [ ] Variable hours configuration
  - [ ] Semester/break period tracking
  - [ ] Automatic hour adjustment (if configured)

**16. Retiree/Part-Time Retirement (Altersteilzeit)**
- **Definition**: Reduced hours before retirement
- **Common variations**:
  - Block model (full-time, then no work)
  - Continuation model (reduced hours throughout)
  - 50% part-time
- **Requirements**:
  - Reduced hours
  - Retirement date tracking
  - Transition period
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Part-time retirement work time model
  - [ ] Reduced hours configuration
  - [ ] Retirement date tracking
  - [ ] Transition period support

### Edge Cases and Special Scenarios

**17. Multiple Work Time Models (Concurrent)**
- **Definition**: Employee has multiple positions/contracts
- **Requirements**:
  - Multiple work time models per user
  - Separate tracking per model
  - Combined compliance checking
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Multiple work time models per user
  - [ ] Separate time tracking per model
  - [ ] Combined hours calculation
  - [ ] Combined compliance checking

**18. Temporary Work Time Model Changes**
- **Definition**: Temporary change in work time (e.g., project-based)
- **Requirements**:
  - Temporary model assignment
  - Start/end dates
  - Return to previous model
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Temporary work time model assignment
  - [ ] Start/end date configuration
  - [ ] Automatic return to previous model
  - [ ] Historical model tracking

**19. International/Secondment (Auslandseinsatz)**
- **Definition**: Work in different country/timezone
- **Requirements**:
  - Timezone handling
  - Local compliance (if applicable)
  - Home country compliance
- **System support**:
  - [ ] Timezone configuration per user
  - [ ] Timezone conversion
  - [ ] Local compliance (if configured)
  - [ ] Home country compliance

**20. On-Call Work (Bereitschaftsdienst)**
- **Definition**: On-call duty (not active work, but available)
- **Requirements**:
  - On-call time tracking
  - Active work time tracking
  - Different rules for on-call vs. active work
- **System support**:
  - [ ] On-call time tracking
  - [ ] Active work time tracking
  - [ ] Separate compliance rules (if applicable)
  - [ ] On-call to active work conversion

#### Task 4.5.1: Document Employee Time Tracking Workflow

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Documented complete clock-in workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] Documented complete clock-out workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] Documented break tracking workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] Documented manual time entry workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] Documented time entry correction workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] All workflows comply with ArbZG requirements
- [ ] All workflows follow common sense
- [ ] All workflows tested with real-world scenarios
- [ ] Workflow documentation includes screens/mockups

**Detailed Clock-In Workflow (Real-World Example):**

**Scenario:** Employee arrives at work at 8:45 AM

1. **Employee opens app** → Dashboard shows "Not clocked in" status
2. **Employee clicks "Clock In" button** → System checks:
   - Has employee had 11 hours rest since last shift? (ArbZG requirement)
   - Is there an active time entry? (Prevent duplicates)
   - Is current time valid? (Not in future, not too far in past)
3. **If checks pass** → System records:
   - Start time: 08:45
   - Date: Today's date
   - Status: "Active"
   - User ID: Current user
4. **System displays confirmation** → "You clocked in at 08:45"
5. **Dashboard updates** → Shows "Clocked in since 08:45" with live timer
6. **System starts compliance monitoring** → Begins checking for break requirements

**Edge Cases Handled:**
- Employee tries to clock in less than 11 hours after last shift → Show error: "You need at least 11 hours rest. Your last shift ended at [time]. You can clock in after [calculated time]."
- Employee already has active entry → Show error: "You are already clocked in since [time]. Please clock out first."
- Clock-in time is in future → Show error: "Clock-in time cannot be in the future. Please check your device time."

**Detailed Break Workflow (Real-World Example):**

**Scenario:** Employee has worked 6.5 hours, needs to take lunch break

1. **System detects 6 hours worked** → Shows notification: "You've worked 6 hours. Please take a 30-minute break soon."
2. **Employee clicks "Start Break"** → System:
   - Records break start time
   - Pauses work timer
   - Starts break timer
3. **During break** → Dashboard shows:
   - "On break since [time]"
   - Break duration timer
   - Work timer paused
4. **Employee clicks "End Break"** → System:
   - Records break end time
   - Calculates break duration
   - Resumes work timer
   - Updates total break time
5. **System checks compliance** → If break < 30 minutes after 6 hours → Shows warning: "Your break was only [X] minutes. German law requires 30 minutes after 6 hours. Please take additional break time."

**ArbZG Compliance:**
- After 6 hours: Minimum 30 minutes break (can be split: 2x 15 min)
- After 9 hours: Minimum 45 minutes break (can be split: 2x 22.5 min or 3x 15 min)
- System tracks cumulative break time per day
- System warns if break requirements not met

**Verification Steps:**
1. Document complete clock-in workflow
2. Document complete clock-out workflow
3. Document break workflow
4. Document manual entry workflow
5. Document correction workflow
6. Verify ArbZG compliance for each workflow
7. Test with real-world scenarios
8. Create workflow diagrams/mockups

**Files to Create:**
- `docs/workflows/employee-time-tracking.md` (detailed workflow documentation)

**Cannot check off until:** All employee workflows documented in detail, ArbZG compliant, tested with real scenarios, and workflow documentation complete.

#### Task 4.5.2: Document Absence Request Workflow

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Documented vacation request workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] Documented sick leave reporting workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] Documented special leave request workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] Documented manager approval workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] Documented absence cancellation workflow (step-by-step)
- [ ] All workflows comply with German labor law
- [ ] All workflows follow common sense
- [ ] Workflow documentation includes real-world examples

**Detailed Vacation Request Workflow (Real-World Example):**

**Scenario:** Employee wants to request vacation from March 15-22, 2024

1. **Employee navigates to "Absences" → "Request Absence"**
2. **Employee selects "Vacation" as absence type**
3. **Employee enters dates:**
   - Start date: March 15, 2024
   - End date: March 22, 2024
4. **System calculates:**
   - Total calendar days: 8 days
   - Working days (excluding weekends): 6 days (if Mon-Fri work week)
   - Remaining vacation days: Shows current balance
   - Available vacation days: Shows if request exceeds available days
5. **System validates:**
   - No overlapping requests
   - Dates are in future (or today)
   - End date is after start date
   - Sufficient vacation days available
6. **If validation passes** → Employee can add optional reason/description
7. **Employee clicks "Submit Request"** → System:
   - Creates absence request with status "Pending"
   - Sends notification to manager
   - Shows confirmation: "Your vacation request has been submitted. Your manager will review it."
8. **Manager receives notification** → "New vacation request from [Employee Name]"
9. **Manager reviews request** → Manager dashboard shows:
   - Employee name
   - Requested dates
   - Vacation days used
   - Remaining vacation days
   - Team coverage (who else is off)
10. **Manager approves** → System:
    - Updates status to "Approved"
    - Deducts vacation days from employee's balance
    - Sends notification to employee: "Your vacation request for March 15-22 has been approved."
    - Updates employee's calendar
11. **Manager rejects** → System:
    - Updates status to "Rejected"
    - Manager can add rejection reason
    - Sends notification to employee: "Your vacation request for March 15-22 has been rejected. Reason: [reason]"
    - Vacation days NOT deducted

**Common Sense Rules:**
- Employees can cancel pending requests (before approval)
- Employees cannot cancel approved requests (must contact manager)
- System prevents overlapping requests automatically
- System shows calendar view of all team absences (for managers)
- System calculates working days correctly (excludes weekends, holidays)

**Verification Steps:**
1. Document vacation request workflow
2. Document sick leave workflow
3. Document special leave workflow
4. Document manager approval workflow
5. Verify workflows make sense
6. Test with real-world scenarios
7. Create workflow diagrams

**Files to Create:**
- `docs/workflows/absence-management.md` (detailed workflow documentation)

**Cannot check off until:** All absence workflows documented, workflows make sense, tested with real scenarios, and documentation complete.

#### Task 4.5.3: Document Manager Workflows

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Documented manager dashboard workflow
- [ ] Documented team overview workflow
- [ ] Documented approval workflow (absences, time corrections)
- [ ] Documented team compliance review workflow
- [ ] Documented team reports workflow
- [ ] All workflows are simple and intuitive
- [ ] All workflows follow common sense
- [ ] Workflow documentation includes real-world examples

**Detailed Manager Approval Workflow (Real-World Example):**

**Scenario:** Manager needs to approve 3 absence requests and 2 time corrections

1. **Manager opens manager dashboard** → Shows:
   - "3 pending absence requests"
   - "2 pending time corrections"
   - Team overview (who's working, who's off)
2. **Manager clicks "Pending Approvals"** → Shows list:
   - Absence requests with employee name, dates, type
   - Time corrections with employee name, date, change details
3. **Manager reviews first absence request:**
   - Employee: Maria Schmidt
   - Request: Vacation, March 15-22
   - Vacation days: 6 working days
   - Remaining balance: 18 days (after this request: 12 days)
   - Team coverage: 2 other team members also off (but different dates)
4. **Manager approves** → Clicks "Approve" → System:
   - Shows confirmation: "Vacation request approved for Maria Schmidt"
   - Updates status to "Approved"
   - Deducts vacation days
   - Sends notification to employee
   - Removes from pending list
5. **Manager reviews time correction:**
   - Employee: John Doe
   - Original entry: March 10, 09:00 - 17:00
   - Correction request: Change to 08:30 - 17:30
   - Reason: "Forgot to clock in on time, actually started at 8:30"
6. **Manager reviews reason** → Makes sense, approves → System:
   - Updates time entry
   - Records correction in audit log
   - Sends notification to employee
   - Removes from pending list

**Common Sense Rules:**
- Managers can see all pending items in one place
- Managers can approve/reject with one click
- Managers can add comments when rejecting
- System shows context (vacation balance, team coverage)
- System prevents conflicts (overlapping absences)

**Verification Steps:**
1. Document manager dashboard workflow
2. Document team overview workflow
3. Document approval workflows
4. Document compliance review workflow
5. Verify workflows are simple
6. Test with real-world scenarios

**Detailed User Management Workflow (Real-World Example):**

**Scenario:** HR needs to add new employee and configure their working time

1. **HR opens "Admin" → "Users"** → Shows list of all employees
2. **HR clicks "Add User"** → Form appears:
   - Select user from Nextcloud user list (dropdown)
   - Select working time model (e.g., "Full-time 40h")
   - Set vacation days per year (e.g., 30 days)
   - Assign manager (dropdown of managers)
   - Set start date (when configuration becomes active)
3. **HR fills form** → System validates:
   - User not already added
   - Working time model exists
   - Manager exists
   - Dates are valid
4. **HR clicks "Save"** → System:
   - Creates user configuration
   - Assigns working time model
   - Sets vacation entitlement
   - Assigns manager
   - Shows confirmation: "User [Name] added successfully"
   - Sends welcome email to user (optional)
5. **User can now use the system** → With their configured working hours and vacation days

**Common Sense Rules:**
- HR can edit user settings anytime
- Changes take effect immediately (or on specified date)
- HR can see user's current status (active entries, vacation balance)
- HR can deactivate users (without deleting data)
- System shows helpful information (e.g., "This user has 5 pending time entries")

#### Task 4.5.6: Verify German Law Compliance for All Workflows

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] All workflows comply with Arbeitszeitgesetz (ArbZG)
- [ ] Break requirements enforced correctly
- [ ] Maximum working hours enforced correctly
- [ ] Rest period requirements enforced correctly
- [ ] Sunday/holiday work restrictions enforced (if applicable)
- [ ] Night work regulations considered (if applicable)
- [ ] Record keeping requirements met
- [ ] Compliance violations detected and reported correctly
- [ ] All compliance checks documented

**ArbZG Compliance Checklist:**

**Daily Working Time:**
- [ ] Maximum 8 hours per day (can extend to 10 if 6-month average is 8)
- [ ] System calculates 6-month average correctly
- [ ] System warns when approaching/exceeding limits
- [ ] System prevents clock-in if would exceed daily limit

**Weekly Working Time:**
- [ ] Maximum 48 hours average over 6 months
- [ ] System calculates weekly average correctly
- [ ] System tracks rolling 6-month average
- [ ] System warns when approaching/exceeding limits

**Break Requirements:**
- [ ] 30 minutes break required after 6 hours
- [ ] 45 minutes break required after 9 hours
- [ ] System tracks cumulative break time
- [ ] System allows split breaks (e.g., 2x 15 min = 30 min)
- [ ] System warns if break requirements not met
- [ ] System prevents clock-out if break requirements not met (or allows with warning)

**Rest Period:**
- [ ] Minimum 11 hours between end of work and start of next work
- [ ] System calculates rest period correctly
- [ ] System prevents clock-in if rest period not met
- [ ] System shows clear error message with required clock-in time

**Sunday/Holiday Work:**
- [ ] System tracks Sunday/holiday work
- [ ] System requires works council agreement flag (if applicable)
- [ ] System warns when Sunday/holiday work detected
- [ ] System allows configuration of exceptions

**Night Work:**
- [ ] System detects work between 11 PM and 6 AM
- [ ] System tracks night work hours
- [ ] System applies special regulations (if configured)
- [ ] System warns about night work requirements

**Record Keeping:**
- [ ] All time entries are recorded
- [ ] All changes are logged (audit trail)
- [ ] Records are retained for required period (2 years minimum)
- [ ] Records can be exported for inspection

**Verification Steps:**
1. Review all workflows against ArbZG requirements
2. Verify break requirements are enforced
3. Verify maximum hours are enforced
4. Verify rest period is enforced
5. Verify compliance violations are detected
6. Test compliance checks with real scenarios
7. Document all compliance rules

**Files to Create:**
- `docs/compliance/arbzg-compliance.md` (detailed compliance documentation)
