## 📋 COMPREHENSIVE ROLES & PERMISSIONS DOCUMENTATION

### Role Definitions

#### Role 1: Employee

**Definition:** A standard user who tracks their own working time and requests absences. Every user in the system has the Employee role by default. Employees can have additional roles (Manager, Admin) but always retain Employee capabilities.

**Who Has This Role:**
- All Nextcloud users who are added to the arbeitszeitcheck app
- Default role for all users
- Cannot be removed (all users are employees)

**Key Characteristics:**
- Tracks their own time (clock in/out, breaks, manual entries)
- Views only their own data
- Requests absences (vacation, sick leave, etc.)
- Views their own compliance status
- Exports their own data (GDPR)
- Cannot see other employees' data
- Cannot approve/reject requests
- Cannot manage system settings

---

#### Role 2: Manager

**Definition:** A user who manages a team of employees. Managers can approve/reject absence requests and time corrections from their team members, view team data, and generate team reports. Managers are also employees (they track their own time).

**Who Has This Role:**
- Users assigned as managers in admin settings
- Can be assigned to specific employees (team members)
- Can have their own manager (manager hierarchy)
- Can also be an employee (tracks own time)

**Key Characteristics:**
- All Employee capabilities (tracks own time, requests absences, etc.)
- Views team members' data (only their assigned team)
- Approves/rejects absence requests from team members
- Approves/rejects time entry corrections from team members
- Views team compliance status
- Generates team reports
- Cannot see data from employees outside their team
- Cannot manage system settings
- Cannot manage users

**Manager Hierarchy:**
- Managers can have team members
- Managers can have their own manager (multi-level hierarchy)
- System supports: Employee → Manager → Senior Manager → Admin
- Data visibility follows hierarchy (managers see only their direct reports)

---

#### Role 3: Admin

**Definition:** A Nextcloud administrator with full access to all features. Admins can manage users, configure working time models, view all compliance data, generate system-wide reports, and configure system settings.

**Who Has This Role:**
- Nextcloud administrators (users with admin privileges in Nextcloud)
- Automatically has full access
- Cannot be assigned (based on Nextcloud admin status)

**Key Characteristics:**
- All Employee capabilities (tracks own time, requests absences, etc.)
- All Manager capabilities (can approve/reject, view team data - if assigned as manager)
- Manages all users (assign working time models, vacation days, managers)
- Creates/edits/deletes working time models
- Configures global system settings
- Views all compliance violations (all users)
- Views all time entries (all users)
- Generates system-wide reports
- Exports all data
- Accesses audit logs
- Full access to all features

**Permission Inheritance:**
- Admin automatically has Manager capabilities (can approve/reject if assigned as manager)
- Admin automatically has Employee capabilities (can track own time)
- Admin can access any page/feature
- Admin can view any user's data

---

- ❌ = Not Allowed
- 🔒 = Allowed only for own data

### Use Cases by Role

#### Employee Use Cases

**Use Case 1: Daily Time Tracking**
- **Actor:** Employee
- **Goal:** Track working hours for the day
- **Preconditions:** Employee is logged in, has working time model assigned
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Employee opens dashboard
  2. Employee clicks "Clock In" (or system auto-clocks in if configured)
  3. System records clock-in time
  4. Employee works
  5. Employee takes break (clicks "Start Break", then "End Break")
  6. Employee finishes work, clicks "Clock Out"
  7. System records clock-out time, calculates hours worked
  8. System checks ArbZG compliance (breaks, max hours, rest period)
  9. System shows summary (hours worked, break time, compliance status)
- **Postconditions:** Time entry created, compliance checked, statistics updated
- **Alternative Flows:**
  - Employee forgets to clock in → Can create manual entry
  - Employee forgets to clock out → System warns, can correct
  - Break requirement not met → System warns, shows required break time
  - Rest period not met → System prevents clock-in, shows when can clock in

**Use Case 2: Request Vacation**
- **Actor:** Employee
- **Goal:** Request vacation days off
- **Preconditions:** Employee is logged in, has vacation entitlement
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Employee navigates to "Absences" → "Request Absence"
  2. Employee selects "Vacation" as absence type
  3. Employee enters start date and end date
  4. System calculates working days (excludes weekends/holidays)
  5. System shows remaining vacation days
  6. System validates (no overlapping requests, sufficient days available)
  7. Employee submits request
  8. System creates absence request with status "Pending"
  9. System sends notification to manager
  10. Employee sees confirmation: "Your vacation request has been submitted"
- **Postconditions:** Absence request created, manager notified
- **Alternative Flows:**
  - Insufficient vacation days → System shows error, prevents submission
  - Overlapping request → System shows error, prevents submission
  - Manager rejects → Employee receives notification, can view reason

**Use Case 3: Correct Time Entry**
- **Actor:** Employee
- **Goal:** Correct a mistake in time entry
- **Preconditions:** Employee has existing time entry, entry is editable
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Employee views time entries list
  2. Employee finds incorrect entry
  3. Employee clicks "Request Correction"
  4. Employee enters corrected times (start, end, breaks)
  5. Employee enters reason for correction
  6. Employee submits correction request
  7. System creates correction request with status "Pending"
  8. System sends notification to manager
  9. Manager reviews and approves/rejects
- **Postconditions:** Correction request created, manager notified
- **Alternative Flows:**
  - Manager approves → Time entry updated, employee notified
  - Manager rejects → Employee notified with reason, can request again

**Use Case 4: View Compliance Status**
- **Actor:** Employee
- **Goal:** Check if working time is compliant with ArbZG
- **Preconditions:** Employee has time entries
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Employee navigates to "Compliance" → "Dashboard"
  2. System shows compliance status:
     - Current week: Compliant / Warning / Violation
     - Current month: Compliant / Warning / Violation
     - Break compliance: Met / Not met
     - Rest period compliance: Met / Not met
  3. If violations exist, employee can view details
  4. Employee can see recommendations (e.g., "Take 15-minute break")
- **Postconditions:** Employee understands compliance status

---

#### Manager Use Cases

**Use Case 5: Approve Absence Request**
- **Actor:** Manager
- **Goal:** Review and approve team member's absence request
- **Preconditions:** Manager is logged in, has team members, pending request exists
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Manager opens manager dashboard
  2. Manager sees notification: "3 pending absence requests"
  3. Manager clicks "Pending Approvals"
  4. Manager views list of pending requests (team members only)
  5. Manager clicks on a request to view details:
     - Employee name
     - Absence type (vacation, sick leave, etc.)
     - Dates (start, end, working days)
     - Vacation balance (before/after request)
     - Team coverage (who else is off)
  6. Manager reviews request
  7. Manager clicks "Approve"
  8. System updates absence status to "Approved"
  9. System deducts vacation days (if vacation)
  10. System sends notification to employee
  11. System removes from pending list
- **Postconditions:** Absence approved, employee notified, vacation days deducted
- **Alternative Flows:**
  - Manager rejects → Manager enters reason, employee notified
  - Insufficient vacation days → System warns, manager can still approve (override)

**Use Case 6: View Team Overview**
- **Actor:** Manager
- **Goal:** See who's working, who's off, team status
- **Preconditions:** Manager is logged in, has team members
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Manager opens manager dashboard
  2. Manager sees team overview:
     - Who's currently clocked in
     - Who's on break
     - Who's off (vacation, sick leave)
     - Today's team hours summary
     - Team compliance status
  3. Manager can filter by date range
  4. Manager can view individual team member details
- **Postconditions:** Manager understands team status

**Use Case 7: Generate Team Report**
- **Actor:** Manager
- **Goal:** Generate report of team's working hours
- **Preconditions:** Manager is logged in, has team members
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Manager navigates to "Reports" → "Team Report"
  2. Manager selects date range (e.g., last month)
  3. Manager selects team members (or all team)
  4. Manager clicks "Generate Report"
  5. System generates report:
     - Total hours per team member
     - Overtime per team member
     - Absences per team member
     - Compliance violations (if any)
  6. Manager can export report (PDF, CSV)
- **Postconditions:** Report generated, manager can download

---

#### Admin Use Cases

**Use Case 8: Add New Employee**
- **Actor:** Admin
- **Goal:** Add new employee to system and configure their working time
- **Preconditions:** Admin is logged in, user exists in Nextcloud
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Admin navigates to "Admin" → "Users"
  2. Admin clicks "Add User"
  3. Admin selects user from Nextcloud user list
  4. Admin selects working time model (e.g., "Full-time 40h")
  5. Admin sets vacation days per year (e.g., 30 days)
  6. Admin assigns manager (from dropdown)
  7. Admin sets start date (when configuration becomes active)
  8. Admin clicks "Save"
  9. System creates user configuration
  10. System assigns working time model
  11. System sets vacation entitlement
  12. System assigns manager
  13. System shows confirmation: "User [Name] added successfully"
- **Postconditions:** User added, configured, can use system
- **Alternative Flows:**
  - User already exists → System shows error, prevents duplicate
  - Invalid working time model → System shows error, prevents save

**Use Case 9: Create Working Time Model**
- **Actor:** Admin
- **Goal:** Create a new working time model (e.g., "Part-time 20h")
- **Preconditions:** Admin is logged in
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Admin navigates to "Admin" → "Working Time Models"
  2. Admin clicks "Create Model"
  3. Admin enters model name (e.g., "Part-time 20h")
  4. Admin sets weekly hours (e.g., 20 hours)
  5. Admin sets daily hours (e.g., 4 hours/day, 5 days/week)
  6. Admin sets work days (e.g., Monday-Friday)
  7. Admin sets overtime calculation rules
  8. Admin sets compliance rules (if different from default)
  9. Admin clicks "Save"
  10. System creates working time model
  11. System shows confirmation: "Working time model created"
- **Postconditions:** Model created, can be assigned to users

**Use Case 10: View System-Wide Compliance**
- **Actor:** Admin
- **Goal:** View all compliance violations across all users
- **Preconditions:** Admin is logged in
- **Main Flow:**
  1. Admin navigates to "Admin" → "Compliance" → "Violations"
  2. System shows all violations:
     - Violations by user
     - Violation type (max hours, break, rest period, etc.)
     - Date/time of violation
     - Severity (warning, violation)
     - Status (open, resolved)
  3. Admin can filter by user, date, violation type
  4. Admin can view violation details
  5. Admin can resolve violations (add notes, mark as resolved)
- **Postconditions:** Admin understands system-wide compliance status

---

### Real-World Scenarios: How Roles Work Together

#### Scenario 1: Employee Requests Vacation → Manager Approves

**Participants:** Employee (Maria), Manager (John), System

**Timeline:**
1. **Day 1, 9:00 AM:** Maria (Employee) requests vacation for March 15-22
   - Maria navigates to "Absences" → "Request Absence"
   - Maria selects "Vacation", enters dates
   - System validates: 6 working days, Maria has 18 days remaining
   - System creates request with status "Pending"
   - System sends notification to John (Manager)

2. **Day 1, 10:30 AM:** John (Manager) receives notification
   - John opens manager dashboard
   - John sees "1 pending absence request"
   - John clicks "Pending Approvals"

3. **Day 1, 10:35 AM:** John reviews request
   - John sees: Maria, Vacation, March 15-22, 6 working days
   - John sees: Maria has 18 days remaining (after request: 12 days)
   - John sees: No team coverage conflicts (other team members not off)
   - John clicks "Approve"

4. **Day 1, 10:36 AM:** System processes approval
   - System updates absence status to "Approved"
   - System deducts 6 vacation days from Maria's balance (18 → 12)
   - System sends notification to Maria: "Your vacation request for March 15-22 has been approved"
   - System removes request from pending list

5. **Day 1, 11:00 AM:** Maria receives notification
   - Maria sees notification: "Vacation approved"
   - Maria views absences list, sees status "Approved"
   - Maria sees updated vacation balance: 12 days remaining

**Permissions Verified:**
- ✅ Employee can request absence
- ✅ Manager can see team member's request
- ✅ Manager can approve request
- ✅ System updates vacation balance
- ✅ Notifications sent correctly

---

#### Scenario 2: Employee Corrects Time Entry → Manager Approves

**Participants:** Employee (Tom), Manager (Sarah), System

**Timeline:**
1. **Day 1, 5:00 PM:** Tom (Employee) realizes he forgot to clock in this morning
   - Tom views time entries, sees no entry for today
   - Tom clicks "Create Time Entry"
   - Tom enters: March 10, 08:30 - 17:00 (actual times)
   - System validates: Times are valid, no conflicts
   - System creates time entry

2. **Day 2, 9:00 AM:** Tom realizes he made a mistake (actually started at 8:00, not 8:30)
   - Tom views yesterday's time entry
   - Tom clicks "Request Correction"
   - Tom enters corrected times: 08:00 - 17:00
   - Tom enters reason: "Forgot to clock in on time, actually started at 8:00"
   - Tom submits correction request
   - System creates correction request with status "Pending"
   - System sends notification to Sarah (Manager)

3. **Day 2, 10:00 AM:** Sarah (Manager) receives notification
   - Sarah opens manager dashboard
   - Sarah sees "1 pending time correction"
   - Sarah clicks "Pending Corrections"

4. **Day 2, 10:05 AM:** Sarah reviews correction
   - Sarah sees: Tom, March 10, Original: 08:30-17:00, Correction: 08:00-17:00
   - Sarah sees: Reason: "Forgot to clock in on time, actually started at 8:00"
   - Sarah sees: Difference: +30 minutes (8.5h → 9h)
   - Sarah reviews: Makes sense, approves

5. **Day 2, 10:06 AM:** System processes approval
   - System updates time entry: 08:00 - 17:00
   - System records correction in audit log (who, when, what, why)
   - System sends notification to Tom: "Your time correction has been approved"
   - System removes from pending list

6. **Day 2, 10:30 AM:** Tom receives notification
   - Tom sees notification: "Time correction approved"
   - Tom views time entry, sees updated times: 08:00 - 17:00
   - Tom's statistics updated (9 hours instead of 8.5 hours)

**Permissions Verified:**
- ✅ Employee can create time entry
- ✅ Employee can request correction
- ✅ Manager can see team member's correction request
- ✅ Manager can approve correction
- ✅ System updates time entry
- ✅ Audit log records change

---

#### Scenario 3: Admin Adds New Employee → Employee Starts Using System

**Participants:** Admin (HR), Employee (New Employee), System

**Timeline:**
1. **Day 1, 9:00 AM:** HR (Admin) adds new employee
   - HR navigates to "Admin" → "Users"
   - HR clicks "Add User"
   - HR selects "New Employee" from Nextcloud user list
   - HR selects working time model: "Full-time 40h"
   - HR sets vacation days: 30 days/year
   - HR assigns manager: "John"
   - HR sets start date: Today
   - HR clicks "Save"
   - System creates user configuration
   - System shows confirmation: "User added successfully"

2. **Day 1, 10:00 AM:** New Employee logs in for first time
   - New Employee opens arbeitszeitcheck app
   - System shows onboarding tour (first-time user)
   - New Employee completes onboarding:
     - Understands how to clock in/out
     - Understands how to request absences
     - Reviews personal settings (working hours, vacation days)

3. **Day 1, 10:15 AM:** New Employee starts working
   - New Employee clicks "Clock In"
   - System records clock-in time
   - System shows: "Clocked in at 10:15 AM"
   - New Employee works

4. **Day 1, 12:00 PM:** New Employee takes lunch break
   - New Employee clicks "Start Break"
   - System records break start time
   - System shows: "On break since 12:00 PM"
   - New Employee takes 30-minute break

5. **Day 1, 12:30 PM:** New Employee ends break
   - New Employee clicks "End Break"
   - System records break end time
   - System shows: "Break: 30 minutes"
   - System shows: "Total break time today: 30 minutes"

6. **Day 1, 6:00 PM:** New Employee finishes work
   - New Employee clicks "Clock Out"
   - System records clock-out time
   - System calculates: 7.75 hours worked (10:15 - 18:00, minus 30 min break)
   - System checks compliance: ✅ Compliant (break taken, hours within limit)
   - System shows summary: "Today: 7.75 hours, Break: 30 minutes, Status: Compliant"

**Permissions Verified:**
- ✅ Admin can add users
- ✅ Admin can assign working time model
- ✅ Admin can assign manager
- ✅ Employee can use system after being added
- ✅ Employee can clock in/out
- ✅ System tracks time correctly
- ✅ System checks compliance

### How to Use the Definition of Done

**For EVERY task in this document:**

1. **Read the task's "Completion Criteria (ALL must be met)" section**
   - This lists specific requirements for this task
   - ALL items must be checked before marking complete

2. **Apply the Universal Definition of Done checklist**
   - Go through ALL 12 categories (Code Quality, Functionality, Security, Testing, Translations, Theming, Responsive Design, Accessibility, Performance, Documentation, Integration, Nextcloud Best Practices)
   - Check off each item that applies to this task
   - If an item doesn't apply, note why (e.g., "N/A - no database queries in this task")

3. **Complete the Verification Steps**
   - Follow each step in the "Verification Steps" section
   - Document results (screenshots, test results, etc.)

4. **Verify Files Created/Modified**
   - Check that all files listed in "Files to Create" actually exist
   - Check that all files listed in "Files to Modify" were actually modified
   - Verify file contents match requirements

5. **Run Verification Commands**
   - Use grep commands to verify no hardcoded text, no security issues, etc.
   - Check browser console for errors
   - Check PHP error log for errors

6. **Test Manually**
   - Actually use the feature
   - Test with real data
   - Test all user roles (if applicable)
   - Test error cases
   - Test edge cases

7. **Only then mark as complete**
   - When ALL completion criteria are met
   - When ALL Universal Definition of Done items are checked
   - When ALL verification steps are completed
   - When ALL tests pass

**If ANY item is not checked, the task is NOT done. No exceptions.**

## ⚠️ CRITICAL REMINDER: DEFINITION OF DONE APPLIES TO ALL TASKS

**IMPORTANT:** The Universal Definition of Done checklist (12 categories) applies to EVERY task in this document, even if it's not explicitly listed in each task's completion criteria.

**Why?** To avoid repetition, we don't list all 12 categories for every single task. However, they MUST still be verified.

**How to apply:**

1. **For each task, check the task-specific "Completion Criteria"** - These are the unique requirements for that task.

2. **Then, mentally go through the Universal Definition of Done checklist:**
   - Code Quality: Does this task produce production-ready code? (No TODOs, no mocks, etc.)
   - Functionality: Does this feature work end-to-end with real data?
   - Security: Is input validated, output escaped, permissions checked?
   - Testing: Has this been manually tested? Tested in browsers? Tested with real data?
   - Translations: Is all text translated? Tested in German and English?
   - Theming: Does it work in light and dark themes? Uses CSS variables?
   - Responsive Design: Does it work on mobile and desktop?
   - Accessibility: Is it keyboard navigable? Screen reader friendly?
   - Performance: Is it fast? No unnecessary queries?
   - Documentation: Is code documented? Complex logic explained?
   - Integration: Does it work with other apps? No conflicts?
   - Nextcloud Best Practices: Uses Nextcloud APIs? Proper DI? CSP compliant?

3. **If any category doesn't apply, note why** (e.g., "No database queries in this CSS task, so Performance/N+1 doesn't apply")

4. **If any category applies but isn't met, the task is NOT done** - Fix it before marking complete.

**Example:**

Task: "Create button component CSS"

- Task-specific criteria: Button styles exist, variants work, uses CSS variables ✅
- Universal DoD - Code Quality: No TODOs ✅
- Universal DoD - Functionality: Buttons work when used ✅
- Universal DoD - Security: N/A (CSS only) ✅
- Universal DoD - Testing: Tested in browser, works ✅
- Universal DoD - Translations: N/A (CSS only) ✅
- Universal DoD - Theming: Works in light/dark ✅
- Universal DoD - Responsive: Works on mobile ✅
- Universal DoD - Accessibility: Focus indicators visible ✅
- Universal DoD - Performance: CSS loads quickly ✅
- Universal DoD - Documentation: CSS is clear ✅
- Universal DoD - Integration: No conflicts with other apps ✅
- Universal DoD - Nextcloud: Uses CSS variables ✅

**Only when ALL applicable categories are met is the task done.**

## 📝 COMPLETION CRITERIA FORMAT STANDARD

**Every task MUST have:**

1. **"Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):"** section
   - Lists specific requirements for this task
   - Each item is verifiable and testable
   - Uses checkboxes `- [ ]` for tracking

2. **"Verification Steps:"** section
   - Step-by-step instructions to verify completion
   - Can be followed by anyone
   - Includes commands, manual tests, inspections

3. **"Files to Create:"** section (if applicable)
   - Lists all files that must be created
   - Can be verified with `ls` or file explorer

4. **"Files to Modify:"** section (if applicable)
   - Lists all files that must be modified
   - Can be verified with `git diff` or file inspection

5. **"Cannot check off until:"** statement
   - Clear, specific conditions that must be met
   - Not vague like "works correctly" but specific like "template exists, displays real data, uses translations"

**If a task is missing any of these sections, it needs to be added.**

## 🔍 HOW TO VERIFY A TASK IS ACTUALLY DONE

**Don't just check boxes - VERIFY:**

### Step 1: Read the Completion Criteria
- Understand what needs to be done
- Note any dependencies

### Step 2: Check the Code
- Open the files listed in "Files to Create/Modify"
- Verify code actually exists (not just a stub)
- Verify code matches requirements

### Step 3: Run Verification Commands
- Execute the commands in "Verification Steps"
- Verify results match expected outcomes
- Fix any issues found

### Step 4: Test Manually
- Actually use the feature
- Test with real data (not empty database)
- Test all user roles (if applicable)
- Test error cases
- Test edge cases

### Step 5: Check Browser Console
- Open browser DevTools
- Check Console tab - must be zero errors
- Check Network tab - must be zero CORS errors
- Check for CSP violations

### Step 6: Check PHP Error Log
- Check Nextcloud error log
- Must be zero errors related to this task

### Step 7: Test Translations
- Switch Nextcloud to German
- Verify all text is German
- Switch to English
- Verify all text is English

### Step 8: Test Theming
- Test in light theme
- Test in dark theme
- Verify colors readable, no visual issues

### Step 9: Test Responsive
- Resize browser
- Test on mobile device (or browser dev tools mobile mode)
- Verify layout works, no horizontal scroll

### Step 10: Test Accessibility
- Tab through with keyboard
- Test with screen reader (or verify ARIA is correct)
- Verify focus indicators visible

### Step 11: Verify Integration
- Test with projectcheck installed
- Verify no conflicts
- Verify both apps work

### Step 12: Only Then Check Off
- When ALL steps above pass
- When ALL completion criteria met
- When ALL Universal DoD items checked (if applicable)
- When verified, not just assumed

**If you can't verify it, it's not done.**

- Commands to verify requirements
- Manual testing procedures

- 22 comprehensive criteria
- Must ALL be met before project complete

### What This Ensures:

1. **No Ambiguity**: Every task has clear, specific completion criteria
2. **No Missing Features**: Feature coverage checklist ensures everything is covered
3. **No Shortcuts**: Universal DoD prevents "almost done" or "good enough"
4. **Verifiable**: Every requirement can be checked with commands or tests
5. **Comprehensive**: Covers code quality, functionality, security, testing, translations, theming, responsive, accessibility, performance, documentation, integration, and Nextcloud best practices

### How to Use:

   - Apply Universal DoD checklist
   - Complete verification steps
   - Test manually
   - Only then check off

2. **For Each Phase:**
   - Complete all tasks in phase
   - Pass phase quality gate
   - Verify feature coverage for that phase

3. **For Entire Project:**
   - Complete all phases
   - Complete feature coverage checklist
   - Pass final project Definition of Done (22 criteria)
   - Only then mark project complete

**This system ensures nothing is missed, nothing is "almost done", and everything is production-ready.**

### Phase 5.5: Roles & Permissions System Implementation

**Status:** [ ] Not Started | [ ] In Progress | [ ] Complete  
**Prerequisites:** Phase 5 Complete (or can run parallel with Phase 5)  
**Estimated Time:** 6-8 hours

**CRITICAL:** This phase ensures the roles and permissions system works correctly. The app has three roles: **Employee**, **Manager**, and **Admin**. Each role has different access levels and capabilities.

#### Task 5.5.1: Verify Employee Role Permissions

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Employee can access their own dashboard
- [ ] Employee can view their own time entries
- [ ] Employee can create their own time entries
- [ ] Employee can edit their own time entries (if allowed)
- [ ] Employee can delete their own time entries (if allowed)
- [ ] Employee can view their own calendar
- [ ] Employee can view their own absences
- [ ] Employee can request absences
- [ ] Employee CANNOT access admin pages (403 Forbidden)
- [ ] Employee CANNOT access manager pages (403 Forbidden)
- [ ] Employee CANNOT see other employees' data
- [ ] Employee CANNOT see manager-only features
- [ ] Employee CANNOT see admin-only features
- [ ] All employee permissions tested with real user account
- [ ] All restrictions tested and verified

**Verification Steps:**
1. Create or use test employee user account
2. Log in as employee
3. Test access to employee dashboard - should work
4. Test access to time entries - should show only own entries
5. Test creating time entry - should work
6. Test editing own time entry - should work (if allowed)
7. Test deleting own time entry - should work (if allowed)
8. Test access to calendar - should show only own data
9. Test access to absences - should show only own absences
10. Test requesting absence - should work
11. Try to access `/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/admin/*` - should get 403
12. Try to access `/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/manager/*` - should get 403

#### Task 5.5.4: Implement Permission Checks in Controllers

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] All admin controller methods check for admin permissions
- [ ] All manager controller methods check for manager permissions
- [ ] All employee controller methods check user ownership (for data access)
- [ ] Permission checks return proper HTTP status codes (403 Forbidden)
- [ ] Permission checks return proper error messages (translated)
- [ ] Permission checks are consistent across all controllers
- [ ] Permission checks tested - unauthorized access is denied
- [ ] No permission bypass vulnerabilities exist

**Verification Steps:**
1. Review all controller files
2. Identify all methods that need permission checks
3. Add permission checks to admin controller methods
4. Add permission checks to manager controller methods
5. Add user ownership checks to employee data access
6. Test unauthorized access attempts
7. Verify 403 responses
8. Verify error messages are translated
9. Test edge cases (user trying to access other user's data)
10. Document permission check implementation

**Example Permission Check (Admin):**
```php
public function adminDashboard(): TemplateResponse {
    // Check if user is admin
    if (!$this->userSession->getUser() || 
        !$this->groupManager->isAdmin($this->userSession->getUser()->getUID())) {
        throw new \OCP\AppFramework\Http\ForbiddenException('Admin access required');
    }
    // ... rest of method
}
```

**Example Permission Check (Manager):**
```php
public function managerDashboard(): TemplateResponse {
    $user = $this->userSession->getUser();
    if (!$user) {
        throw new \OCP\AppFramework\Http\ForbiddenException('Authentication required');
    }
    
    // Check if user is manager (has team members assigned)
    $teamMembers = $this->getTeamMembers($user->getUID());
    if (empty($teamMembers)) {
        throw new \OCP\AppFramework\Http\ForbiddenException('Manager access required');
    }
    // ... rest of method
}
```

**Example Permission Check (Employee - Own Data):**
```php
public function viewTimeEntry(int $id): TemplateResponse {
    $user = $this->userSession->getUser();
    if (!$user) {
        throw new \OCP\AppFramework\Http\ForbiddenException('Authentication required');
    }
    
    $timeEntry = $this->timeEntryMapper->find($id);
    if ($timeEntry->getUserId() !== $user->getUID()) {
        throw new \OCP\AppFramework\Http\ForbiddenException('Access denied');
    }
    // ... rest of method
}
```

**Files to Modify:**
- `lib/Controller/AdminController.php` (add admin checks)
- `lib/Controller/ManagerController.php` (add manager checks and team filtering)
- `lib/Controller/PageController.php` (add user ownership checks)
- Any other controllers handling role-based data

**Cannot check off until:** All controllers have proper permission checks, unauthorized access is denied, and all permission checks tested.

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] Admin-only UI elements hidden from non-admins
- [ ] Manager-only UI elements hidden from non-managers

- [ ] Action buttons shown only if user has permission
- [ ] Data tables show only data user has permission to see

- [ ] No client-side-only permission checks (security risk)

**Verification Steps:**

12. Document UI visibility implementation

**Example Template Permission Check:**
```php
<?php
$user = \OC::$server->getUserSession()->getUser();
$isAdmin = $user && \OC::$server->getGroupManager()->isAdmin($user->getUID());
$isManager = $user && $this->hasTeamMembers($user->getUID());
?>

<?php if ($isAdmin): ?>
    <a href="<?php p($urlGenerator->linkToRoute('arbeitszeitcheck.admin.dashboard')); ?>" 
       class="arbeitszeitcheck-nav-link">
        <?php p($l->t('Admin Dashboard')); ?>
    </a>
<?php endif; ?>

<?php if ($isManager): ?>
    <a href="<?php p($urlGenerator->linkToRoute('arbeitszeitcheck.manager.dashboard')); ?>" 
       class="arbeitszeitcheck-nav-link">
        <?php p($l->t('Manager Dashboard')); ?>
    </a>
<?php endif; ?>
```

- `templates/common/header.php` (filter header actions by role)

**Cannot check off until:** All UI elements properly hidden/shown based on permissions, navigation filtered by role, and all permission-based UI tested.

## 🔒 COMPREHENSIVE SECURITY ARCHITECTURE

### Security Principles (Following Nextcloud Best Practices)

**1. Defense in Depth**
- [ ] Multiple layers of security (authentication, authorization, input validation, output escaping)
- [ ] No single point of failure
- [ ] Fail-secure (deny by default)
- [ ] Principle of least privilege

**2. Input Validation (Server-Side Always)**
- [ ] ALL user input validated on server-side (never trust client)
- [ ] Whitelist validation (allow only known good values)
- [ ] Type checking (ensure correct data types)
- [ ] Range checking (ensure values within acceptable ranges)
- [ ] Format validation (dates, times, emails, etc.)
- [ ] Business rule validation (ArbZG compliance, etc.)

**3. Output Escaping**
- [ ] ALL output escaped (prevent XSS)
- [ ] Context-aware escaping (HTML, JavaScript, SQL, URL)
- [ ] Use Nextcloud's escaping functions (`p()`, `print_unescaped()`)
- [ ] Never output user input without escaping

**4. Authentication & Authorization**
- [ ] Use Nextcloud's authentication system (no custom auth)
- [ ] All controllers check user authentication
- [ ] All controllers check user authorization (roles, permissions)
- [ ] Session management handled by Nextcloud
- [ ] No authentication bypasses

**5. CSRF Protection**
- [ ] ALL state-changing operations protected (POST, PUT, DELETE)
- [ ] CSRF tokens on all forms
- [ ] CSRF tokens validated on server-side
- [ ] Use Nextcloud's CSRF protection

**6. SQL Injection Prevention**
- [ ] Use parameterized queries (prepared statements)
- [ ] NEVER concatenate user input into SQL
- [ ] Use Nextcloud's database abstraction layer
- [ ] Input validation before database operations

**7. XSS Prevention**
- [ ] All output escaped
- [ ] CSP headers configured (Phase 0.5)
- [ ] No inline event handlers
- [ ] No `eval()` or similar
- [ ] Content Security Policy enforced

**8. Access Control**
- [ ] Role-based access control (RBAC) implemented
- [ ] Permission checks at controller level
- [ ] Permission checks at service level
- [ ] Data filtering by user role
- [ ] UI elements hidden based on permissions

**9. Data Protection**
- [ ] Sensitive data encrypted at rest (if applicable)
- [ ] Sensitive data encrypted in transit (HTTPS)
- [ ] Passwords never stored (use Nextcloud auth)
- [ ] Audit logging for sensitive operations
- [ ] Data retention policies enforced

**10. Error Handling**
- [ ] Errors logged securely (no sensitive data in logs)
- [ ] Generic error messages to users (no stack traces)
- [ ] Detailed errors logged for debugging
- [ ] No information leakage in error messages

---

## 🛡️ ROLE & PERMISSION MODEL VERIFICATION

### Role Definitions

**Employee Role:**
- **Can do:**
  - View own dashboard
  - Create/edit/delete own time entries
  - View own time entries
  - View own calendar
  - View own absences
  - Request absences
  - View own compliance status
  - Export own data (GDPR)
- **Cannot do:**
  - Access admin pages
  - Access manager pages
  - View other employees' data
  - Approve/reject requests
  - Manage users
  - Configure system

**Manager Role:**
- **Can do:**
  - Everything Employee can do (for own data)
  - View manager dashboard
  - View team members' data (only their team)
  - Approve/reject absence requests (from team)
  - Approve/reject time corrections (from team)
  - View team compliance status
  - Generate team reports
- **Cannot do:**
  - Access admin pages
  - View data from employees outside their team
  - Manage system configuration
  - Manage users (except assign managers)

**Admin Role:**
- **Can do:**
  - Everything Manager can do
  - Access admin dashboard
  - Manage all users
  - Assign work time models
  - Configure system settings
  - View all compliance data
  - Generate all reports
  - Manage working time models
- **Cannot do:**
  - Nothing (full access)

### Permission Verification Checklist

**Controller-Level Checks:**
- [ ] ALL controllers check authentication: `$this->userId !== null`
- [ ] ALL controllers check authorization: Role checks before action
- [ ] Admin controllers: `$this->isAdmin()` check
- [ ] Manager controllers: `$this->isManager()` check
- [ ] Employee controllers: `$this->userId` check
- [ ] 403 Forbidden returned for unauthorized access
- [ ] No information leakage in error messages

**Service-Level Checks:**
- [ ] ALL services check permissions before operations
- [ ] Data filtering by user role
- [ ] Managers only see their team's data
- [ ] Employees only see their own data
- [ ] Admins see all data
- [ ] Permission checks cannot be bypassed

**Template-Level Checks:**
- [ ] UI elements hidden based on permissions: `<?php if ($isAdmin): ?>`
- [ ] No sensitive data in templates for unauthorized users
- [ ] Links to unauthorized pages hidden
- [ ] Forms for unauthorized actions hidden

**Database-Level Checks:**
- [ ] Queries filter by user ID (for employees)
- [ ] Queries filter by team (for managers)
- [ ] No direct database access from templates
- [ ] All queries use parameterized statements

### Security Testing for Permissions

**Test Matrix:**
```
Action                    | Employee | Manager | Admin
--------------------------|----------|---------|--------
View own dashboard        | ✅       | ✅      | ✅
View own time entries     | ✅       | ✅      | ✅
Create own time entry     | ✅       | ✅      | ✅
View team dashboard       | ❌       | ✅      | ✅
View team time entries    | ❌       | ✅      | ✅
Approve absence request   | ❌       | ✅      | ✅
View admin dashboard      | ❌       | ❌      | ✅
Manage users             | ❌       | ❌      | ✅
Configure system         | ❌       | ❌      | ✅
View other employee data | ❌       | ❌      | ✅
```

**Penetration Testing:**
- [ ] Employee tries to access admin pages → 403 Forbidden
- [ ] Employee tries to access manager pages → 403 Forbidden
- [ ] Employee tries to view other employee's data → 403 Forbidden
- [ ] Manager tries to access admin pages → 403 Forbidden
- [ ] Manager tries to view non-team member data → 403 Forbidden or empty result
- [ ] Direct API calls without authentication → 401 Unauthorized
- [ ] Direct API calls with wrong role → 403 Forbidden
- [ ] SQL injection attempts → Blocked, no data returned
- [ ] XSS attempts → Escaped, no script execution
- [ ] CSRF attempts → Blocked, token validation fails

---

## 🔍 EDGE CASE HANDLING IN SECURITY CONTEXT

### Security Edge Cases

**1. User Deletion During Active Session**
- [ ] User deleted while has active time entry → Handle gracefully
- [ ] User deleted while has pending approvals → Reassign or cancel
- [ ] User deleted while viewing data → Redirect to login
- [ ] Session invalidated on user deletion

**2. Role Change During Active Session**
- [ ] User role changed (employee → manager) → Session updated or re-login required
- [ ] User role changed (manager → employee) → Access revoked immediately
- [ ] User role changed (admin → employee) → All admin access revoked

**3. Permission Change During Operation**
- [ ] Manager removed from team → Cannot access team data
- [ ] User assigned new manager → Old manager loses access
- [ ] Working time model deleted → Users reassigned or error handled

**4. Concurrent Access**
- [ ] Multiple sessions for same user → Both sessions valid (Nextcloud handles)
- [ ] Same user from different devices → Both work correctly
- [ ] Race conditions in permission checks → Handled with transactions

**5. Data Access Edge Cases**
- [ ] Employee tries to access deleted user's data → 404 Not Found (not 403)
- [ ] Manager tries to access user with no manager → Handled gracefully
- [ ] Admin tries to access non-existent user → 404 Not Found
- [ ] Time entry belongs to deleted user → Handled in queries

**6. Input Validation Edge Cases**
- [ ] Extremely long input → Truncated or rejected
- [ ] Special characters in input → Escaped properly
- [ ] SQL injection attempts → Blocked
- [ ] XSS attempts → Escaped
- [ ] Null bytes in input → Stripped or rejected
- [ ] Unicode attacks → Handled correctly

**7. Session Edge Cases**
- [ ] Session expires during form submission → Error message, data preserved if possible
- [ ] Session hijacking attempt → Detected and blocked
- [ ] Concurrent requests with same session → Handled correctly
- [ ] Session fixation → Prevented

---

## 📚 GLOSSARY: KEY TERMS DEFINED

**Before proceeding, ensure you understand these terms:**

### Security Terms

**CSP (Content Security Policy)**: A security standard that prevents XSS attacks by controlling which resources can be loaded and executed. In Nextcloud, inline scripts MUST use a nonce (random token) provided by Nextcloud's CSP system.

**CORS (Cross-Origin Resource Sharing)**: A security mechanism that controls which origins can make requests to your API. Nextcloud apps should use same-origin requests only (no cross-origin requests).

**CSRF (Cross-Site Request Forgery)**: An attack where a malicious site makes requests on behalf of an authenticated user. Prevented by validating CSRF tokens on all state-changing operations (POST, PUT, DELETE).

**XSS (Cross-Site Scripting)**: An attack where malicious scripts are injected into web pages. Prevented by escaping all user input before outputting it.

**SQL Injection**: An attack where malicious SQL code is injected into database queries. Prevented by using parameterized queries (prepared statements) instead of string concatenation.

**Parameterized Query**: A database query where user input is passed as parameters, not concatenated into the SQL string. Example: `$query->execute([$userId])` instead of `"SELECT * FROM users WHERE id = '$userId'"`.

**Nonce**: A random token generated by Nextcloud for each page load. Used in CSP to allow inline scripts/styles. Format: `nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>"`.

**RBAC (Role-Based Access Control)**: A security model where access is controlled by user roles (Employee, Manager, Admin). Each role has specific permissions.

**Defense in Depth**: A security strategy using multiple layers of security (authentication, authorization, input validation, output escaping) so that if one layer fails, others still protect.

**Fail-Secure**: A security principle where if something goes wrong, the system defaults to denying access rather than allowing it.

**Least Privilege**: A security principle where users have only the minimum permissions needed to perform their tasks.

### Architecture Terms

**MVC (Model-View-Controller)**: An architectural pattern:
- **Model**: Data structures (database entities, e.g., `TimeEntry`, `Absence`)
- **View**: Presentation layer (PHP templates that render HTML)
- **Controller**: Request handlers (PHP classes that process HTTP requests)

**Dependency Injection (DI)**: A design pattern where dependencies are provided to a class (via constructor) rather than created inside the class. Makes code testable and maintainable.

**Service Layer**: Business logic organized into service classes (e.g., `TimeEntryService`, `AbsenceService`). Controllers are thin and delegate to services.

**Mapper**: A class that handles database operations for a specific entity. Extends Nextcloud's `Mapper` class. Example: `TimeEntryMapper` handles all database operations for `TimeEntry` entities.

**Repository Pattern**: A design pattern where database access is abstracted through mapper classes. Controllers and services don't write SQL directly.

**Template Inheritance**: A pattern where a base template (e.g., `layout.php`) defines the structure, and page templates extend it. Reduces code duplication.

### Nextcloud-Specific Terms

**OCP (Open Cloud Platform)**: Nextcloud's public API namespace. All Nextcloud interfaces are in the `OCP\` namespace. Example: `OCP\IUserSession`, `OCP\IDBConnection`.

**App Framework**: Nextcloud's framework for building apps. Provides controllers, services, dependency injection, routing, etc.

**TemplateResponse**: A Nextcloud response class for rendering PHP templates. Example: `new TemplateResponse('arbeitszeitcheck', 'dashboard', $params)`.

**JSONResponse**: A Nextcloud response class for returning JSON data. Example: `new JSONResponse(['success' => true])`.

**IRegistrationContext**: The context used in `Application::register()` to register services, controllers, and capabilities with Nextcloud's DI container.

**IBootContext**: The context used in `Application::boot()` to perform initialization tasks (e.g., loading CSS/JS files).

**Util::addStyle()**: A Nextcloud function to load a CSS file. Example: `Util::addStyle('arbeitszeitcheck', 'dashboard')`.

**Util::addScript()**: A Nextcloud function to load a JavaScript file. Example: `Util::addScript('arbeitszeitcheck', 'dashboard')`.

**link_to()**: A Nextcloud function to generate URLs to app files. Example: `link_to('arbeitszeitcheck', 'css/common/base.css')`.

**image_path()**: A Nextcloud function to generate URLs to app images. Example: `image_path('arbeitszeitcheck', 'icon.png')`.

**$l->t()**: Nextcloud's translation function in PHP templates. Example: `<?php p($l->t('Dashboard')); ?>`.

**t()**: Nextcloud's translation function in JavaScript. Example: `t('arbeitszeitcheck', 'Dashboard')`.

**CSPTrait**: A trait (reusable code) for configuring CSP in controllers. Used via `use CSPTrait;` and `$this->configureCSP($response)`.

### Legal Terms

**ArbZG (Arbeitszeitgesetz)**: German Working Time Act. Regulates maximum working hours, breaks, rest periods, Sunday/holiday work, night work, and record keeping.

**GDPR (General Data Protection Regulation)**: EU regulation on data protection. Requires right to access, rectification, erasure, data minimization, purpose limitation, etc.

**Works Council Agreement (Betriebsvereinbarung)**: An agreement between employer and works council (if company has one) that may allow exceptions to standard working time rules (e.g., Sunday work).

### Data Terms

**UTC (Coordinated Universal Time)**: The standard time used for storing dates/times in databases. All times should be stored in UTC and converted to user's timezone for display.

**Timezone**: A region's standard time offset from UTC. Users may work in different timezones, so the system must handle timezone conversion correctly.

**Audit Log**: A record of all actions performed in the system (who, what, when, why). Required for legal compliance and security.

**Data Retention**: The period for which data must be kept. German law requires 2 years minimum for working time records.

---

## 🏗️ ARCHITECTURAL CONCEPT & NEXTCLOUD BEST PRACTICES

### Architecture Principles

**1. MVC Pattern (Model-View-Controller)**
- [ ] **Models**: Database entities (TimeEntry, Absence, etc.)
- [ ] **Views**: PHP templates (templates/*.php)
- [ ] **Controllers**: Request handlers (lib/Controller/*.php)
- [ ] **Services**: Business logic (lib/Service/*.php)
- [ ] Clear separation of concerns
- [ ] Controllers are thin (delegate to services)
- [ ] Services contain business logic
- [ ] Models represent data

**2. Dependency Injection**
- [ ] Use Nextcloud's dependency injection container
- [ ] Services injected via constructor
- [ ] No global state
- [ ] Testable code (can mock dependencies)

**3. Service Layer Pattern**
- [ ] Business logic in services, not controllers
- [ ] Services are reusable
- [ ] Services handle transactions
- [ ] Services handle error cases

**4. Repository Pattern (via Mappers)**
- [ ] Database access through mappers
- [ ] Mappers extend Nextcloud's Mapper class
- [ ] No direct SQL in controllers/services
- [ ] Queries in mappers

**5. Template Inheritance**
- [ ] Base layout template (templates/common/layout.php)
- [ ] Common components (header, footer, navigation)
- [ ] Page templates extend base layout
- [ ] Reusable components

### Nextcloud Best Practices (ACTUAL, VERIFIABLE REQUIREMENTS)

**These are NOT generic best practices - these are SPECIFIC Nextcloud requirements that can be verified:**

**1. App Structure (VERIFIABLE: Check directory structure)**
- [ ] Directory structure matches Nextcloud standard:
  ```
  apps/arbeitszeitcheck/
  ├── appinfo/          # Routes, info.xml, Application.php
  ├── lib/              # PHP classes (Controller/, Service/, Db/)
  ├── templates/        # PHP templates
  ├── js/               # JavaScript files
  ├── css/              # CSS files
  ├── l10n/             # Translation files (en.json, de.json)
  └── tests/            # Test files
  ```
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `ls -la apps/arbeitszeitcheck/` and verify structure

**2. Namespace Usage (VERIFIABLE: Check namespace declarations)**
- [ ] All classes use namespace: `namespace OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\...;`
- [ ] Controllers: `namespace OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Controller;`
- [ ] Services: `namespace OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Service;`
- [ ] Entities: `namespace OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck\Db;`
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "namespace" lib/` and verify all use `OCA\ArbeitszeitCheck`

**3. Database Access (VERIFIABLE: Check code for OCP\IDBConnection usage)**
- [ ] Use `\OCP\IDBConnection` (not direct PDO or mysqli)
- [ ] Mappers extend `\OCP\AppFramework\Db\Mapper`
- [ ] All queries use `$this->db->prepare()` with parameters
- [ ] No string concatenation in SQL: `"SELECT * FROM table WHERE id = $id"` ❌
- [ ] Use parameterized queries: `$this->db->prepare("SELECT * FROM table WHERE id = ?")->execute([$id])` ✅
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "prepare\|execute" lib/Db/` and verify all use parameters

**4. Controllers (VERIFIABLE: Check controller code)**
- [ ] Controllers extend `\OCP\AppFramework\Controller`
- [ ] Constructor uses dependency injection (services passed as parameters)
- [ ] Use `TemplateResponse` for templates: `new TemplateResponse('arbeitszeitcheck', 'dashboard', $params)`
- [ ] Use `JSONResponse` for API: `new JSONResponse(['data' => $data])`
- [ ] Use `CSPTrait` and call `$this->configureCSP($response)`
- [ ] **Verification**: Check `lib/Controller/*.php` - all extend Controller, use DI, use CSPTrait

**5. Service Registration (VERIFIABLE: Check Application.php)**
- [ ] Services registered in `Application::register(IRegistrationContext $context)`
- [ ] Use `$context->registerService()` for custom services
- [ ] Use `$context->registerService(ClassName::class, function($c) { ... })` for auto-wiring
- [ ] Mappers registered: `$context->registerService(MapperClass::class, function($c) { return new MapperClass($c->query(\OCP\IDBConnection::class)); })`
- [ ] **Verification**: Check `lib/AppInfo/Application.php` - all services registered

**6. User Management (VERIFIABLE: Check for OCP\IUserSession usage)**
- [ ] Use `\OCP\IUserSession` (injected via constructor)
- [ ] Get current user: `$this->userSession->getUser()->getUID()`
- [ ] Check if user logged in: `$this->userSession->getUser() !== null`
- [ ] **DO NOT** use `\OC_User::getUser()` or `$_SESSION` directly ❌
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "IUserSession\|OC_User\|\$_SESSION" lib/` - should only find IUserSession

**7. Configuration (VERIFIABLE: Check for OCP\IConfig usage)**
- [ ] Use `\OCP\IConfig` (injected via constructor)
- [ ] App config: `$config->getAppValue('arbeitszeitcheck', 'key', 'default')`
- [ ] User config: `$config->getUserValue($userId, 'arbeitszeitcheck', 'key', 'default')`
- [ ] **DO NOT** use `\OC::$server->getConfig()` directly in controllers ❌
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "IConfig\|getConfig" lib/` - should use IConfig

**8. Logging (VERIFIABLE: Check for PSR-3 LoggerInterface usage)**
- [ ] Use `\Psr\Log\LoggerInterface` (injected via constructor)
- [ ] Log levels: `$logger->debug()`, `$logger->info()`, `$logger->warning()`, `$logger->error()`
- [ ] **DO NOT** use `error_log()` or `\OC::$server->getLogger()` directly ❌
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "LoggerInterface\|error_log" lib/` - should use LoggerInterface

**9. CSS/JS Loading (VERIFIABLE: Check Application::boot() method)**
- [ ] Load CSS/JS in `Application::boot(IBootContext $context)` method
- [ ] Use `\OCP\Util::addStyle('arbeitszeitcheck', 'filename')` for CSS
- [ ] Use `\OCP\Util::addScript('arbeitszeitcheck', 'filename')` for JS
- [ ] Only load on app routes: `if (strpos($path, '/apps/arbeitszeitcheck') === 0)`
- [ ] **Verification**: Check `lib/AppInfo/Application.php::boot()` - CSS/JS loaded conditionally

**10. Templates (VERIFIABLE: Check template files)**
- [ ] Use `$l->t()` for translations: `<?php p($l->t('Text')); ?>`
- [ ] Use `p()` for escaped output: `<?php p($variable); ?>`
- [ ] Use `print_unescaped()` only for trusted HTML: `<?php print_unescaped($html); ?>`
- [ ] Use `link_to()` for app file URLs: `<?php print_unescaped(link_to('arbeitszeitcheck', 'css/file.css')); ?>`
- [ ] Use `image_path()` for app image URLs: `<?php print_unescaped(image_path('arbeitszeitcheck', 'icon.png')); ?>`
- [ ] Use CSP nonce for inline scripts: `<script nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>">`
- [ ] **Verification**: Check templates - all use `$l->t()`, `p()`, nonces for scripts

**11. Routing (VERIFIABLE: Check appinfo/routes.php)**
- [ ] Routes defined in `appinfo/routes.php`
- [ ] Format: `['name' => 'ControllerName#method', 'url' => '/path', 'verb' => 'GET']`
- [ ] Controller name matches class name (case-sensitive)
- [ ] **Verification**: Check `appinfo/routes.php` - all routes valid, controllers exist

**12. Type Safety (VERIFIABLE: Check for declare(strict_types=1))**
- [ ] All PHP files start with `<?php declare(strict_types=1);`
- [ ] All function parameters have type hints: `public function method(string $param): void`
- [ ] All return types declared: `public function method(): array`
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "declare(strict_types)" lib/` - all files should have it

**13. Exception Handling (VERIFIABLE: Check exception usage)**
- [ ] Use Nextcloud exceptions: `\OCP\AppFramework\Http\NotFoundResponse`, `\OCP\AppFramework\Http\ForbiddenResponse`
- [ ] Or custom exceptions extending `\Exception`
- [ ] **DO NOT** use generic `Exception` without context ❌
- [ ] **Verification**: Check exception usage - should use specific exceptions

**14. Translation (VERIFIABLE: Check translation files and usage)**
- [ ] Translation keys in `l10n/en.json` and `l10n/de.json`
- [ ] PHP templates use `$l->t('key')` or `$l->n('singular', 'plural', $count)`
- [ ] JavaScript uses `t('arbeitszeitcheck', 'key')` or `n('arbeitszeitcheck', 'singular', 'plural', count)`
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "t(" templates/ js/` - all use translation functions

**15. Theming (VERIFIABLE: Check CSS for hardcoded colors)**
- [ ] CSS uses Nextcloud variables: `var(--color-main-background)`, `var(--color-main-text)`
- [ ] **NO** hardcoded colors: `color: #000000;` ❌
- [ ] **NO** hardcoded colors: `background: white;` ❌
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "#[0-9a-fA-F]\{3,6\}\|rgb\|rgba" css/` - should find only in comments or var() definitions

**16. CSP Compliance (VERIFIABLE: Check for nonce usage)**
- [ ] All inline `<script>` tags have `nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>"`
- [ ] All inline `<style>` tags have `nonce="<?php p($_['cspNonce'] ?? ''); ?>"`
- [ ] **NO** inline event handlers: `onclick="..."` ❌
- [ ] **NO** `javascript:` URLs: `href="javascript:void(0)"` ❌
- [ ] **NO** `eval()` or `Function()` constructor ❌
- [ ] **Verification**: Run `grep -r "<script\|<style\|onclick\|javascript:" templates/` - check nonce usage

**17. Database Migrations (VERIFIABLE: Check migration files)**
- [ ] Migrations in `lib/Migration/Version[number]Date[YYYYMMDDHHMMSS].php`
- [ ] Migrations extend `\OCP\Migration\IOutput` and implement `changeSchema()` and `changeData()`
- [ ] **Verification**: Check migration files - proper naming, extend correct classes

**18. Capabilities (VERIFIABLE: Check Capabilities class)**
- [ ] Capabilities class implements `\OCP\Capabilities\ICapability`
- [ ] Registered in `Application::register()`: `$context->registerCapability(Capabilities::class)`
- [ ] **Verification**: Check `lib/Capabilities.php` exists and is registered

**19. Error Responses (VERIFIABLE: Check controller error handling)**
- [ ] Use `new NotFoundResponse()` for 404 errors
- [ ] Use `new ForbiddenResponse()` for 403 errors
- [ ] Use `new JSONResponse(['error' => 'message'], 400)` for API errors
- [ ] **Verification**: Check controllers - proper error responses used

**20. Asset Loading (VERIFIABLE: Check no direct file paths)**
- [ ] **DO NOT** use direct paths: `<link href="/apps/arbeitszeitcheck/css/file.css">` ❌
- [ ] Use `link_to()`: `<?php print_unescaped(link_to('arbeitszeitcheck', 'css/file.css')); ?>` ✅
- [ ] **Verification**: Check templates - no direct `/apps/` paths, use `link_to()`

**CRITICAL: These are NOT suggestions - these are REQUIREMENTS that MUST be verified. Each item has a verification step that can be checked with grep, file inspection, or code review.**

## ✅ VERIFICATION CHECKLIST: NO BULLSHIT BINGO

**Before marking any phase complete, run these verification commands to ensure requirements are ACTUALLY met, not just claimed:**

### Security Verification

```bash
# 1. Check for SQL injection vulnerabilities (should find NO string concatenation in SQL)
grep -rn "WHERE.*\$" lib/ | grep -v "//\|/\*" | grep -v "prepare\|execute"
# Expected: No results (or only in comments)

# 2. Check for XSS vulnerabilities (should find NO unescaped output)
grep -rn "echo.*\$" templates/ | grep -v "p(\|print_unescaped"
# Expected: No results (or only in comments)

# 3. Check for CSP violations (should find NO inline scripts without nonce)
grep -rn "<script" templates/ | grep -v "nonce="
# Expected: No results (all scripts have nonce)

# 4. Check for inline event handlers (should find NONE)
grep -rn "onclick\|onchange\|onsubmit\|onload" templates/
# Expected: No results

# 5. Check for eval() usage (should find NONE)
grep -rn "eval\|Function(" js/ templates/
# Expected: No results
```

### Architecture Verification

```bash
# 1. Check all controllers extend Nextcloud Controller
grep -rn "class.*Controller" lib/Controller/ | grep -v "extends Controller"
# Expected: No results (all extend Controller)

# 2. Check all controllers use dependency injection (have constructor with parameters)
grep -rn "public function __construct" lib/Controller/ -A 5 | grep -v "IRequest\|IUserSession\|Service"
# Expected: Only finds expected dependencies

# 3. Check all services registered in Application.php
grep -rn "registerService" lib/AppInfo/Application.php
# Expected: All services registered

# 4. Check all mappers extend Nextcloud Mapper
grep -rn "class.*Mapper" lib/Db/ | grep -v "extends Mapper"
# Expected: No results (all extend Mapper)

# 5. Check strict types enabled
find lib/ -name "*.php" -exec head -1 {} \; | grep -v "declare(strict_types=1)"
# Expected: No results (all files have strict types)
```

### Nextcloud API Usage Verification

```bash
# 1. Check for direct database access (should use OCP\IDBConnection)
grep -rn "new PDO\|mysqli\|mysql_connect" lib/
# Expected: No results

# 2. Check for direct session access (should use OCP\IUserSession)
grep -rn "\$_SESSION\|session_start" lib/
# Expected: No results

# 3. Check for direct config access (should use OCP\IConfig)
grep -rn "OC::\$server->getConfig" lib/
# Expected: No results

# 4. Check for direct logger access (should use PSR-3 LoggerInterface)
grep -rn "OC::\$server->getLogger\|error_log" lib/ | grep -v "LoggerInterface"
# Expected: No results

# 5. Check CSS uses Nextcloud variables (no hardcoded colors)
grep -rn "#[0-9a-fA-F]\{3,6\}\|rgb(" css/ | grep -v "var(\|/\*"
# Expected: No results (or only in comments)
```

### Translation Verification

```bash
# 1. Check for hardcoded English text in templates
grep -rn '"[A-Z][a-zA-Z ]*"' templates/ | grep -v '<?php\|$l->t\|//'
# Expected: No results (or only in comments)

# 2. Check for hardcoded English text in JavaScript
grep -rn '"[A-Z][a-zA-Z ]*"' js/ | grep -v 't(\|n(\|//'
# Expected: No results (or only in comments)

# 3. Check all translation keys exist in en.json
# (Manual check: compare keys used in code vs keys in l10n/en.json)
```

### Permission Verification

```bash
# 1. Check all controllers check permissions (should have permission checks)
grep -rn "isAdmin\|isManager\|getUser" lib/Controller/ | wc -l
# Expected: At least one permission check per controller method that needs it

# 2. Check for direct user ID access (should use IUserSession)
grep -rn "\$_GET\['user'\]\|\$_POST\['user'\]" lib/
# Expected: No results (use IUserSession instead)
```

### Code Quality Verification

```bash
# 1. Check for TODOs, FIXMEs, placeholders
grep -rn "TODO\|FIXME\|PLACEHOLDER\|XXX\|HACK" lib/ templates/ js/
# Expected: No results (or only in comments explaining why)

# Expected: No results (or only in commented code)
```

## 🎯 CONCRETE REQUIREMENTS (NOT BUZZWORDS)

**Every requirement in this document must be:**

1. **VERIFIABLE**: Can be checked with a command, code inspection, or test
2. **SPECIFIC**: Not vague like "follow best practices" but specific like "use `\OCP\IDBConnection`"
3. **MEASURABLE**: Can be measured (e.g., "zero CSP violations" not "few violations")
4. **ACTIONABLE**: Clear what needs to be done (e.g., "add nonce to all inline scripts")
5. **TESTABLE**: Can be tested (e.g., "run grep command and verify no results")

**If a requirement doesn't meet these criteria, it's been removed or made more specific.**

---

**NO VAGUE STATEMENTS ALLOWED:**
- ❌ "Follow security best practices" → ✅ "Use parameterized queries, escape all output, validate all input"
- ❌ "Use proper architecture" → ✅ "Controllers extend `\OCP\AppFramework\Controller`, services use dependency injection"
- ❌ "Ensure good performance" → ✅ "Page load time < 2 seconds, API response < 200ms, zero N+1 queries"
- ❌ "Handle errors properly" → ✅ "All database operations in try-catch, errors logged with context, users see generic messages"

**Every requirement has a verification step that proves it's actually implemented.**

- [ ] Numeric inputs validated for ranges (e.g., hours 0-24, minutes 0-59)

- [ ] XSS prevention (all output escaped)
- [ ] CSRF protection on all state-changing operations
- [ ] File upload validation (if applicable)
- [ ] All validation errors return helpful messages
- [ ] No validation bypassed or skipped
- [ ] All validation tested with malicious input

**Verification Steps:**

3. Test with invalid input (SQL injection attempts, XSS attempts, etc.)
4. Verify all input is sanitized before database operations
5. Verify all output is escaped before display
6. Test CSRF protection on all forms
7. Document all validation rules

**Files to Modify:**
- All controllers (add validation)
- All form templates (add client-side validation hints)

**Cannot check off until:** All input validated, all output escaped, SQL injection prevented, XSS prevented, CSRF protected, and tested with malicious input.

#### Task 10.3: Verify Role & Permission Model Security

**Completion Criteria (ALL must be met):**
- [ ] **Controller-level permission checks**: ALL controllers verify user role before action
- [ ] **Service-level permission checks**: ALL services verify permissions before operations
- [ ] **Data filtering**: Queries filter by user ID (employees), team (managers), or all (admins)
- [ ] **UI-level permission checks**: Templates hide/show elements based on permissions
- [ ] **API-level permission checks**: All API endpoints check permissions
- [ ] **Penetration testing**: All permission bypass attempts fail
- [ ] **Test matrix complete**: All role/action combinations tested
- [ ] **Edge cases handled**: User deletion, role changes, concurrent access all handled securely
- [ ] **No information leakage**: Unauthorized users don't see error messages revealing data existence
- [ ] **Audit logging**: All permission checks logged for security audit

**Permission Verification Test Cases:**

**Employee Tests:**
- [ ] Employee accesses own dashboard → ✅ Allowed
- [ ] Employee accesses admin dashboard → ❌ 403 Forbidden
- [ ] Employee accesses manager dashboard → ❌ 403 Forbidden
- [ ] Employee views own time entries → ✅ Allowed, sees only own data
- [ ] Employee views other employee's time entries → ❌ 403 Forbidden or empty result
- [ ] Employee creates time entry → ✅ Allowed, creates for self
- [ ] Employee creates time entry for other user → ❌ Rejected, validation error
- [ ] Employee approves absence request → ❌ 403 Forbidden (not a manager)

**Manager Tests:**
- [ ] Manager accesses manager dashboard → ✅ Allowed
- [ ] Manager accesses admin dashboard → ❌ 403 Forbidden
- [ ] Manager views team member's data → ✅ Allowed, sees team data
- [ ] Manager views non-team member's data → ❌ 403 Forbidden or empty result
- [ ] Manager approves team member's request → ✅ Allowed
- [ ] Manager approves non-team member's request → ❌ Rejected, validation error
- [ ] Manager views all employees → ❌ Only sees team members

**Admin Tests:**
- [ ] Admin accesses admin dashboard → ✅ Allowed
- [ ] Admin accesses manager dashboard → ✅ Allowed
- [ ] Admin accesses employee dashboard → ✅ Allowed
- [ ] Admin views any user's data → ✅ Allowed, sees all data
- [ ] Admin manages users → ✅ Allowed
- [ ] Admin configures system → ✅ Allowed

**Penetration Tests:**
- [ ] Direct URL access to admin page as employee → ❌ 403 Forbidden
- [ ] Direct API call to admin endpoint as employee → ❌ 403 Forbidden
- [ ] SQL injection in user ID parameter → ❌ Blocked, no data returned
- [ ] Manipulating user ID in request → ❌ Validation error, no data returned
- [ ] Session hijacking attempt → ❌ Detected and blocked
- [ ] CSRF attack on permission-protected action → ❌ Token validation fails

**Verification Steps:**
1. Review all controllers for permission checks
2. Review all services for permission checks
3. Review all database queries for data filtering
4. Review all templates for UI permission checks
5. Execute all test cases above
6. Perform penetration testing
7. Verify audit logging
8. Document all permission checks

**Files to Review/Modify:**
- All controllers (add/verify permission checks)
- All services (add/verify permission checks)
- All mappers (verify data filtering)
- All templates (verify UI permission checks)

**Cannot check off until:** All permission checks implemented, all test cases pass, penetration testing successful, and audit logging works.

---

## 🚨 CRITICAL REMINDERS - UPDATED

**Before checking ANY task as complete, ask yourself:**

1. ✅ Is this production-ready code? (No TODOs, no placeholders, no mocks)
2. ✅ Does it work with REAL data? (Not fake data, not "will implement later")
3. ✅ Are there ZERO errors? (No console errors, no PHP errors, no CSP violations, no CORS errors)
4. ✅ Is it fully tested? (Manual testing done, works in browser, works in both themes, all edge cases tested)
5. ✅ Are translations complete? (No hardcoded English, all keys in en.json and de.json)
6. ✅ Does it follow projectcheck patterns? (Same structure, same class names, same approach)
7. ✅ Is it accessible? (Keyboard navigation works, screen reader tested, WCAG compliant)
8. ✅ Is it responsive? (Works on mobile, works on desktop, touch targets adequate)
9. ✅ Is it secure? (Input validated, output escaped, SQL injection prevented, XSS prevented, CSRF protected)
10. ✅ Is it performant? (Queries optimized, no N+1 problems, page load < 3 seconds)
11. ✅ Is it documented? (PHPDoc, JSDoc, business rules, architecture)
12. ✅ Are errors handled? (All operations have error handling, errors logged, users see helpful messages)
13. ✅ Are edge cases handled? (DST, timezones, concurrent operations, network failures)
14. ✅ Is it GDPR compliant? (Export, deletion, correction work correctly)
15. ✅ Does it comply with German law? (ArbZG requirements met, compliance violations detected)
16. ✅ Are workflows logical? (Make sense, follow common sense, based on real-world usage)

**If ANY answer is NO, the task is NOT complete. Fix it before checking off.**

## 💡 ADDITIONAL RECOMMENDATIONS FOR EXCELLENCE

### Features That Would Make the App Even Better:

1. **Smart Defaults**: System remembers user's common work times and suggests them
2. **Quick Actions**: One-click actions for common tasks (e.g., "Same as yesterday")
3. **Time Entry Templates**: Pre-defined time entry templates for common scenarios
4. **Calendar Integration**: Sync with Nextcloud Calendar for absences
5. **Mobile Optimization**: Progressive Web App (PWA) support for mobile use
6. **Dark Mode Toggle**: Easy theme switching (already covered but emphasize)
7. **Export Formats**: Multiple export formats (CSV, JSON, PDF, Excel)
8. **Data Visualization**: Charts and graphs for time tracking trends
9. **Goal Setting**: Set and track working time goals
10. **Team Visibility**: See team members' status (who's working, who's off)

### Edge Cases to Consider:

1. **User Deletion**: What happens to time entries when user is deleted?
2. **Manager Change**: What happens when user's manager changes mid-approval?
3. **Working Time Model Change**: What happens when model changes mid-period?
4. **System Clock Changes**: What happens if system clock is adjusted?
5. **Leap Seconds**: How are leap seconds handled?
6. **Multiple Time Zones**: User travels and works in different time zones
7. **Partial Days**: User works partial day (sick in morning, works afternoon)
8. **Split Shifts**: User works morning shift, long break, evening shift
9. **On-Call Time**: How is on-call time tracked (if applicable)?
10. **Travel Time**: How is business travel time tracked (if applicable)?

### Clarifications Needed:

1. **Time Rounding**: Should time be rounded (e.g., to nearest 15 minutes)?
2. **Break Splitting**: Can breaks be split (e.g., 2x 15 min = 30 min)?
3. **Overtime Compensation**: How is overtime compensated (time off, pay)?
4. **Multi-Level Approvals**: Do some requests need multiple approvals?
5. **Delegation**: Can managers delegate approval authority?
6. **Time Entry Locking**: When are time entries locked from editing?
7. **Retroactive Changes**: Can past time entries be changed? How far back?
8. **Data Retention**: Exact retention periods for different data types?
9. **Backup Frequency**: How often should backups be performed?
10. **Support Channels**: How do users get help (email, ticket system, etc.)?

## 📋 CRITICAL CLARIFICATIONS & DECISIONS NEEDED

**Before starting implementation, these decisions must be made and documented:**

### Time Tracking Clarifications

1. **Time Rounding Policy**
   - [ ] Decision: Should time be rounded? (e.g., to nearest 15 minutes, 5 minutes, or no rounding)
   - [ ] If rounding: What rounding method? (round up, round down, round nearest)
   - [ ] If rounding: Applied to start time, end time, or both?
   - [ ] Decision documented in code and user documentation

2. **Break Splitting**
   - [ ] Decision: Can breaks be split? (e.g., 2x 15 min = 30 min requirement)
   - [ ] If yes: How is split break tracked?
   - [ ] Decision documented

3. **Cross-Midnight Shifts**
   - [ ] Decision: How are shifts that cross midnight handled?
   - [ ] Example: Clock in 23:00, clock out 01:00 next day
   - [ ] Decision: Which day does this count toward?
   - [ ] Decision documented

4. **Split Shifts**
   - [ ] Decision: Are split shifts allowed? (morning shift, long break, evening shift)
   - [ ] If yes: How are split shifts tracked?
   - [ ] Decision documented

5. **Multiple Shifts Per Day**
   - [ ] Decision: Can user have multiple time entries in one day?
   - [ ] If yes: How are they combined for daily totals?
   - [ ] Decision documented

### Approval Workflow Clarifications

6. **Multi-Level Approvals**
   - [ ] Decision: Do some requests need multiple approvals?
   - [ ] If yes: What triggers multi-level approval?
   - [ ] Decision documented

7. **Approval Delegation**
   - [ ] Decision: Can managers delegate approval authority?
   - [ ] If yes: How is delegation configured?
   - [ ] Decision documented

8. **Self-Approval**
   - [ ] Decision: Can managers approve their own requests?
   - [ ] If no: Who approves manager requests?
   - [ ] Decision documented

### Data Management Clarifications

9. **Time Entry Locking**
   - [ ] Decision: When are time entries locked from editing?
   - [ ] Options: After approval, after payroll processing, after X days, never
   - [ ] Decision documented

10. **Retroactive Changes**
    - [ ] Decision: How far back can time entries be changed?
    - [ ] Options: Unlimited, current month, current year, never
    - [ ] Decision documented

11. **Data Retention Periods**
    - [ ] Decision: Exact retention period for time entries? (minimum 2 years for legal)
    - [ ] Decision: Retention period for audit logs?
    - [ ] Decision: Retention period for deleted user data?
    - [ ] Decision documented

12. **Overtime Compensation**
    - [ ] Decision: How is overtime compensated?
    - [ ] Options: Time off in lieu, paid overtime, both, configurable
    - [ ] Decision documented

### User Experience Clarifications

13. **Default Values**
    - [ ] Decision: Should system remember user's common work times?
    - [ ] Decision: Should system suggest "Same as yesterday"?
    - [ ] Decision documented

14. **Quick Actions**
    - [ ] Decision: What quick actions should be available?
    - [ ] Examples: "Copy yesterday's entry", "Standard 8-hour day"
    - [ ] Decision documented

15. **Mobile Experience**
    - [ ] Decision: PWA support needed?
    - [ ] Decision: Mobile app needed, or web-only?
    - [ ] Decision documented

### Integration Clarifications

16. **Calendar Integration**
    - [ ] Decision: Integrate with Nextcloud Calendar?
    - [ ] If yes: Sync absences to calendar?
    - [ ] Decision documented

17. **Project Integration**
    - [ ] Decision: Integrate with ProjectCheck?
    - [ ] If yes: How deep is integration?
    - [ ] Decision documented

18. **Payroll Integration**
    - [ ] Decision: Export format for payroll systems?
    - [ ] Decision: DATEV export needed?
    - [ ] Decision documented

    - [ ] Decision: How is agreement tracked in system?
    - [ ] Decision documented

## 🎨 UX ENHANCEMENT RECOMMENDATIONS

### Smart Features That Improve Usability:

1. **Intelligent Defaults**
   - System remembers user's most common start time
   - System suggests "Same as yesterday" button
   - System pre-fills common values based on history

2. **Contextual Actions**
   - "Quick add" button for common scenarios
   - "Copy entry" from previous day/week
   - "Template" time entries for recurring work

3. **Visual Feedback**
   - Progress indicators for long operations
   - Success animations (subtle, not annoying)
   - Clear visual states (saving, saved, error)

4. **Progressive Disclosure**
   - Simple view by default
   - Advanced options available but hidden
   - "Show more" for power users

5. **Error Prevention**
   - Validate as user types (not just on submit)
   - Warn before destructive actions
   - Confirm unusual actions (e.g., deleting approved entry)

6. **Helpful Automation**
   - Auto-detect if user forgot to clock out
   - Auto-suggest break times based on work duration
   - Auto-calculate overtime

## 🔍 ADDITIONAL EDGE CASES TO HANDLE

### Time Entry Edge Cases (Additional):

1. **User works exactly 6 hours** → Break requirement triggered?
2. **User works exactly 9 hours** → 45 min break requirement triggered?
3. **User takes break exactly at 6-hour mark** → Requirement met?
4. **User works 11 hours exactly** → Rest period exactly 11 hours, can clock in?
5. **User clocks in/out at exact same time** → Duration is 0, allowed?
6. **User has break longer than work time** → Validation error?
7. **User edits time entry while manager is reviewing** → Conflict handling?
8. **User deletes time entry that's in approval process** → What happens?
9. **System time changes during active time entry** → How handled?
10. **User has multiple active time entries** → Prevented or handled?

### Absence Edge Cases (Additional):

1. **User requests absence for today** → Allowed or must be future?
2. **User requests absence that's already past** → Allowed for retroactive?
3. **User requests absence during active time entry** → Conflict?
4. **Manager approves absence but user's vacation balance changed** → Re-check balance?
5. **User requests absence but working time model changes** → Recalculate days?
6. **Absence request spans working time model change** → Which model applies?
7. **User cancels absence but it's already in payroll** → What happens?

### System Edge Cases:

1. **Database connection lost during operation** → Transaction rollback?
2. **Session expires during form filling** → Save draft or lose data?
3. **User deleted while has pending approvals** → What happens to approvals?
4. **Manager deleted while has pending approvals** → Reassign or cancel?
5. **Working time model deleted while assigned to users** → Prevent or handle?
6. **System maintenance during active time entry** → How handled?
7. **Concurrent clock-in from multiple devices** → Prevent or handle?
8. **Clock-in from different timezone** → Timezone conversion?

### Data Integrity Edge Cases:

1. **Time entry start time after end time** → Validation error?
2. **Time entry overlaps with existing entry** → Prevent or allow?
3. **Break time equals total time** → No work time, allowed?
4. **Negative overtime** → Displayed correctly?
5. **Overtime exceeds reasonable limits** → Warning or error?

**All edge cases must be identified, handled, tested, and documented.**

  - [ ] Break requirements (30min after 6h, 45min after 9h, split breaks)
  - [ ] Rest period (11 hours minimum)
  - [ ] Sunday/holiday work restrictions
  - [ ] Night work regulations
  - [ ] Record keeping (2 years minimum)
- [ ] **GDPR fully implemented**:
  - [ ] Right to access (data export)
  - [ ] Right to rectification
  - [ ] Right to erasure (after retention period)
  - [ ] Data minimization
  - [ ] Purpose limitation
  - [ ] Storage limitation
  - [ ] Security measures
  - [ ] Transparency (privacy policy)
- [ ] Works council agreement support (if applicable)
- [ ] All compliance checks working correctly
- [ ] All compliance violations detected and reported
- [ ] Compliance verified with legal review (if possible)

### Work Time Models Requirements
- [ ] **All 20 work time models supported** (see comprehensive list in Phase 4.5):
  - [ ] Standard models (full-time, part-time, flexible, trust-based, shift work)
  - [ ] Special models (compressed, annualized, job sharing, zero-hours)
  - [ ] Leave models (sabbatical, parental leave, sick leave, unpaid leave)
  - [ ] Special status (internship, student worker, part-time retirement)
  - [ ] Edge cases (multiple models, temporary changes, international, on-call)
- [ ] Each model:
  - [ ] Configurable in admin interface
  - [ ] Proper validation
  - [ ] Overtime calculation works
  - [ ] ArbZG compliance enforced
  - [ ] Transitions between models work
  - [ ] Historical data tracked
- [ ] All models tested with real data

### Documentation Requirements
- [ ] User manual complete
- [ ] Administrator guide complete
- [ ] Developer documentation complete
- [ ] API documentation complete
- [ ] All documentation translated

### Store Submission Requirements
- [ ] App metadata complete
- [ ] Screenshots provided
- [ ] Changelog created
- [ ] License correct
- [ ] All store requirements met
